Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The Purity of Mud When Water and Soil Differ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the purity of mud when the water is impure or pure, and explain the principle that the result follows the worst of the two premises.

Core Idea
If either the water or the soil is pure, the mud is pure; but the stronger principle is that the impure component governs.

This passage discusses a methodological dispute within the Hanafi school: when mud is formed from water and soil, and one of them is impure, what is the ruling on the mud? Multiple opinions are given, and the text evaluates their reasoning, ultimately favoring the view that the result follows the worst component.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the opinions
The issue is the purity of mud when water and soil have different purity statuses. The text lists four opinions: consideration of water, consideration of soil, consideration of the dominant, and the view that if either is pure, the mud is pure.
2
Analyze the preferred view
Ibn al-Humam and the majority hold that if either is pure, the mud is pure. The text says this is the choice of Abu Nasr and Muhammad, and the fatwa is upon it. However, the author then criticizes the justification (that it becomes something else) as weak.
3
Understand the final principle
The author praises Abu al-Layth and Qadikhan for stating that the result follows from the worst of the two premises (أخس المقدمتين). This means that if one component is impure, the mixture is impure, regardless of the other.
This principle is a strong methodological rule in Hanafi fiqh for dealing with mixtures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا فسا في السراويل وصلى معه قال بعضهم : لا يجوز لأن في الريح أجزاء لطيفة فتدخل أجزاء الثوب . وقيل : إن الشيخ الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني كان يصلي من غير السراويل ولا تأويل لفعله إلا التحرز من الخلاف، والسراج الوهاج والبزازية وكلهم أطلقوه عن ذكر الخلاف قوله : (فهو مخالف لتصحيح قاضيخان) أقول : قد مشى في المنية على ما ذكره قاضيخان وقال شارحها وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث. وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف ذكره في الخلاصة . وقيل : العبرة للماء إن كان نجساً فالطين نجس وإلا فطاهر. وقيل: العبرة للتراب. وقيل للغالب قال ابن الهمام والأكثر على أنه أيهما كان طاهراً فالطين طاهر اهـ . وهو اختيار أبي نصر محمد بن سلام قال البزازي وهو قول محمد. وقد ذكر أن الفتوى عليه اهـ. ووجهه في الخلاصة بصيرورته شيئاً آخر وهو توجيه ضعيف إذ يقتضي أن جميع الأطعمة إذا كان ماؤها نجساً أو دهنها أو نحو ذلك أن يكون الطعام طاهراً لصيرورته شيئاً آخر، وعلى هذا سائر المركبات إذا كان بعض مفرداتها نجساً ولا يخفى فساده فلله در الفقيه أبي الليث ودر قاضيخان حيث جعل قوله وهو الصحيح مشيراً إلى أن سائر الأقوال لا صحة لها بل هي فاسدة لأن النتيجة تابعة لأخس المقدمتين .اهـ. قوله: (وفيما عدا الأخيرة) أي من المسائل الأربع التي في طير لا يؤكل ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس والفتوى أنه يجوز سواء كان السراويل رطباً وقت الفسوة أو يابساً. إذا رأى على ثوب غيره نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم يخبره ولا يسعه تركه جلد مرارة الغنم نجس ومرارته وبوله سواء عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس. ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم بوله حتى لا تجوز الصلاة معه. إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم قطرة خمر وقعت في دن خل لا يحل شربه إلا بعد ساعة، ولو صب كوز من خمر في دن من خل ولا يوجد له طعم ولا رائحة حل الشراب في الحال. السلق والسلجم المطبوع في رماد العذرة نجس عند أبي يوسف اهـ.
If one passes wind (fasa) in the trousers and prays with it, some said it is not permissible because the wind contains fine particles that enter the fabric of the garment. And it is said that the Shaykh al-Imam Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani would pray without trousers, and there is no explanation for his action except avoidance of disagreement. And Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Al-Bazzaziyyah, and all of them, stated it without mentioning disagreement: 'So it contradicts the verification of Qadikhan.' I say: In Al-Munya they followed what Qadikhan said, and its commentator said it is the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth. And likewise it is narrated from Abu Yusuf in Al-Khulasah. And it is said the consideration is for the water: if the water is impure, then the mud is impure; otherwise it is pure. And it is said the consideration is for the soil. And it is said for the dominant. Ibn al-Humam said the majority are that whichever of them is pure, the mud is pure. End quote. And it is the choice of Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Salam, and al-Bazzazi said it is the opinion of Muhammad. And it has been mentioned that the fatwa is upon it. End quote. And its justification in Al-Khulasah is that it becomes something else, but that is a weak reasoning because it would imply that all foods, if their water or oil etc. is impure, the food would be pure because it became something else, and likewise all compounds if some of their components are impure - and its corruption is not hidden. So excellent is Abu al-Layth and Qadikhan in making their saying 'and it is the correct' indicating that other statements have no validity, rather they are corrupt because the result follows from the worst of the two premises. End quote. His saying: (and other than the last) i.e., from the four issues: a bird not eaten, fish blood, saliva of mule and donkey, urine that splashed like needle tips, and impurity, and the fatwa is that it is permissible whether the trousers were wet at the time of the wind or dry. If he sees on another's garment impurity more than the size of a dirham, he informs him and it is not permissible for him to leave it. The skin of the sheep's gall bladder is impure, and its gall and urine are equal: according to Muhammad they are pure, according to the two companions they are impure. And the sheep's bladder: its ruling is the same as its urine, so that prayer is not allowed with it. If a drop of wine falls into a jar of vinegar, it is not permissible to drink it until after an hour. And if a jug of wine is poured into a jar of vinegar and no taste or smell is found, then drinking is permissible immediately. Chard (silq) and cabbage (saljam) cooked in ash of human waste (ramad al-adhrah) are impure according to Abu Yusuf. End quote.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This long passage from page 405 covers several important rulings and discussions. It begins with a discussion about passing wind while wearing trousers (sarawil) and then praying. Some scholars say it is invalid because wind has subtle particles that penetrate the fabric, but the relied-upon fatwa is that it is permissible, regardless of whether the trousers were wet or dry at the time. The text then digresses into a discussion about the ruling when both water and soil are pure or impure in determining the purity of mud; the preferred view is that if either is pure, the mud is pure, but there is debate. The author praises the view of Qadikhan and Abu al-Layth that the result follows from the worst premise (the more impure component determines the impurity). The text then returns to the main point: 'other than the last' refers to the four issues: bird not eaten, fish blood, saliva of donkey/mule, and urine splashes (like tip of needles); the fatwa is that praying with these impurities is permissible as long as the amount is less than a dirham. Then additional rulings: if one sees an impurity larger than a dirham on another's garment, one must inform them; the skin of a sheep's gall bladder (mirarah) is impure, and according to Muhammad the actual gall and urine of sheep are pure, but according to the two companions they are impure; the bladder of a sheep has the same ruling as its urine (thus impure). Then a rule about wine in vinegar: if a single drop of wine falls into a jar of vinegar, it becomes permissible only after an hour (presumably for the alcohol to transform), but if a whole jug of wine is poured and no taste/smell remains, it is immediately permissible. Finally, vegetables cooked in the ash of human waste are impure according to Abu Yusuf, implying impurity due to contact with najasah.

Key Terms
الطين (al-teen): Mud, a mixture of water and soil.
أخس المقدمتين (akhass al-muqaddimatayn): The worst of the two premises; a principle meaning that in a mixture, the impurity of the more defiling component determines the whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, which principle should be applied to determine the purity of mud when one component is impure?
A) Consider only the water
B) Consider only the soil
C) The result follows from the worst of the two premises
D) The mud is pure because it becomes something else

Key Takeaway
The purity of a mixture is determined by its most impure component, not by the creation of a new substance.

Informing Others About Impurity on Their Clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the duty to inform a person if you see impurity larger than a dirham on their garment, and explain why it becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
If you see impurity exceeding a dirham on another's garment, you must inform them; it is not permissible to remain silent.

This lesson covers a social responsibility in taharah: when you notice a significant impurity (larger than a dirham) on someone else's clothing, you are obliged to tell them. The text presents it as a clear ruling without elaboration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The ruling applies when the impurity seen is more than the size of a dirham. Smaller impurities are excused in prayer and need not be mentioned.
2
Understand the obligation
The text says 'يخبره ولا يسعه تركه' meaning he must inform him and it is not permissible to leave it. This implies it is obligatory (wajib) to inform.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا فسا في السراويل وصلى معه قال بعضهم : لا يجوز لأن في الريح أجزاء لطيفة فتدخل أجزاء الثوب . وقيل : إن الشيخ الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني كان يصلي من غير السراويل ولا تأويل لفعله إلا التحرز من الخلاف، والسراج الوهاج والبزازية وكلهم أطلقوه عن ذكر الخلاف قوله : (فهو مخالف لتصحيح قاضيخان) أقول : قد مشى في المنية على ما ذكره قاضيخان وقال شارحها وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث. وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف ذكره في الخلاصة . وقيل : العبرة للماء إن كان نجساً فالطين نجس وإلا فطاهر. وقيل: العبرة للتراب. وقيل للغالب قال ابن الهمام والأكثر على أنه أيهما كان طاهراً فالطين طاهر اهـ . وهو اختيار أبي نصر محمد بن سلام قال البزازي وهو قول محمد. وقد ذكر أن الفتوى عليه اهـ. ووجهه في الخلاصة بصيرورته شيئاً آخر وهو توجيه ضعيف إذ يقتضي أن جميع الأطعمة إذا كان ماؤها نجساً أو دهنها أو نحو ذلك أن يكون الطعام طاهراً لصيرورته شيئاً آخر، وعلى هذا سائر المركبات إذا كان بعض مفرداتها نجساً ولا يخفى فساده فلله در الفقيه أبي الليث ودر قاضيخان حيث جعل قوله وهو الصحيح مشيراً إلى أن سائر الأقوال لا صحة لها بل هي فاسدة لأن النتيجة تابعة لأخس المقدمتين .اهـ. قوله: (وفيما عدا الأخيرة) أي من المسائل الأربع التي في طير لا يؤكل ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس والفتوى أنه يجوز سواء كان السراويل رطباً وقت الفسوة أو يابساً. إذا رأى على ثوب غيره نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم يخبره ولا يسعه تركه جلد مرارة الغنم نجس ومرارته وبوله سواء عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس. ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم بوله حتى لا تجوز الصلاة معه. إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم قطرة خمر وقعت في دن خل لا يحل شربه إلا بعد ساعة، ولو صب كوز من خمر في دن من خل ولا يوجد له طعم ولا رائحة حل الشراب في الحال. السلق والسلجم المطبوع في رماد العذرة نجس عند أبي يوسف اهـ.

Commentary
This long passage from page 405 covers several important rulings and discussions. It begins with a discussion about passing wind while wearing trousers (sarawil) and then praying. Some scholars say it is invalid because wind has subtle particles that penetrate the fabric, but the relied-upon fatwa is that it is permissible, regardless of whether the trousers were wet or dry at the time. The text then digresses into a discussion about the ruling when both water and soil are pure or impure in determining the purity of mud; the preferred view is that if either is pure, the mud is pure, but there is debate. The author praises the view of Qadikhan and Abu al-Layth that the result follows from the worst premise (the more impure component determines the impurity). The text then returns to the main point: 'other than the last' refers to the four issues: bird not eaten, fish blood, saliva of donkey/mule, and urine splashes (like tip of needles); the fatwa is that praying with these impurities is permissible as long as the amount is less than a dirham. Key Terms
النجاسة (al-najasah): Impurity, both physical (najis) and legal (hadath). Here it refers to physical impurity.
قدر الدرهم (qadr al-dirham): The size of a dirham coin, approximately the area of a fingertip.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if you see impurity less than a dirham on another's garment?
A) You must inform them
B) It is recommended to inform
C) No obligation to inform
D) It is forbidden to inform

Key Takeaway
Informing others about significant impurity is a communal duty to preserve the validity of their prayers.

Ruling on the Gall Bladder and Urine of Sheep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the impurity ruling for the gall bladder and urine of sheep, and explain the difference between Imam Muhammad and the two companions.

Core Idea
The skin of the gall bladder is impure; the gall and urine are pure according to Imam Muhammad, but impure according to the two companions.

This lesson addresses a specific issue of taharah: the parts of a sheep that are permissible to eat. While the meat is halal, the gall bladder and urine are subject to dispute. The text gives the skin of the gall bladder as impure, and then presents the differing views on the internal contents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and its parts
The passage discusses the gall bladder (mirarah) of sheep, including its skin, gall (contents), and urine. Also mentions the bladder (mathanah).
2
State the agreed ruling
The skin of the gall bladder is agreed to be impure. Why? Because it is a container for a najis substance? The text does not give the reason, but it is known that the gall bladder's skin is considered impure due to contact with the bile.
3
Explain the dispute on gall and urine
Imam Muhammad holds that the gall and urine of sheep are pure (tahir). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani? Actually 'عندهما' refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? In Hanafi terminology, 'عندهما' usually means Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but here 'عند محمد' explicitly states Muhammad's view. So 'عندهما' likely means the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? That is confusing. Actually, in the text: 'عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس'. So Muhammad says pure, and the two (Sahibayn) say impure. However, Muhammad is one of the Sahibayn? No, The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. So here Muhammad is singled out, and 'عندهما' refers to Abu Yusuf and one other? Possibly 'عندهما' means the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad?) But typically, in Hanafi texts, 'عند محمد' is mentioned separately from 'عندهما' to refer to Imam Muhammad's view alone, and 'عندهما' refers to Abu Yusuf and Al-Hasan? Actually, in the manual, 'عندهما' often refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani together. But here it contradicts because Muhammad's view is given separately. So likely 'عندهما' here refers to Abu Yusuf and another? It is ambiguous, but the point is there is an intra-Hanafi difference.
4
Apply the ruling to prayer
The bladder of the sheep has the same ruling as its urine; thus, if the urine is considered impure, the bladder is impure, and prayer with it is not allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا فسا في السراويل وصلى معه قال بعضهم : لا يجوز لأن في الريح أجزاء لطيفة فتدخل أجزاء الثوب . وقيل : إن الشيخ الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني كان يصلي من غير السراويل ولا تأويل لفعله إلا التحرز من الخلاف، والسراج الوهاج والبزازية وكلهم أطلقوه عن ذكر الخلاف قوله : (فهو مخالف لتصحيح قاضيخان) أقول : قد مشى في المنية على ما ذكره قاضيخان وقال شارحها وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث. وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف ذكره في الخلاصة . وقيل : العبرة للماء إن كان نجساً فالطين نجس وإلا فطاهر. وقيل: العبرة للتراب. وقيل للغالب قال ابن الهمام والأكثر على أنه أيهما كان طاهراً فالطين طاهر اهـ . وهو اختيار أبي نصر محمد بن سلام قال البزازي وهو قول محمد. وقد ذكر أن الفتوى عليه اهـ. ووجهه في الخلاصة بصيرورته شيئاً آخر وهو توجيه ضعيف إذ يقتضي أن جميع الأطعمة إذا كان ماؤها نجساً أو دهنها أو نحو ذلك أن يكون الطعام طاهراً لصيرورته شيئاً آخر، وعلى هذا سائر المركبات إذا كان بعض مفرداتها نجساً ولا يخفى فساده فلله در الفقيه أبي الليث ودر قاضيخان حيث جعل قوله وهو الصحيح مشيراً إلى أن سائر الأقوال لا صحة لها بل هي فاسدة لأن النتيجة تابعة لأخس المقدمتين .اهـ. قوله: (وفيما عدا الأخيرة) أي من المسائل الأربع التي في طير لا يؤكل ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس والفتوى أنه يجوز سواء كان السراويل رطباً وقت الفسوة أو يابساً. إذا رأى على ثوب غيره نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم يخبره ولا يسعه تركه جلد مرارة الغنم نجس ومرارته وبوله سواء عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس. ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم بوله حتى لا تجوز الصلاة معه. إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم قطرة خمر وقعت في دن خل لا يحل شربه إلا بعد ساعة، ولو صب كوز من خمر في دن من خل ولا يوجد له طعم ولا رائحة حل الشراب في الحال. السلق والسلجم المطبوع في رماد العذرة نجس عند أبي يوسف اهـ.

And it is the choice of Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Salam, and al-Bazzazi said it is the opinion of Muhammad. And it has been mentioned that the fatwa is upon it. End quote. And its justification in Al-Khulasah is that it becomes something else, but that is a weak reasoning because it would imply that all foods, if their water or oil etc. is impure, the food would be pure because it became something else, and likewise all compounds if some of their components are impure - and its corruption is not hidden. So excellent is Abu al-Layth and Qadikhan in making their saying 'and it is the correct' indicating that other statements have no validity, rather they are corrupt because the result follows from the worst of the two premises. End quote. His saying: (and other than the last) i.e., from the four issues: a bird not eaten, fish blood, saliva of mule and donkey, urine that splashed like needle tips, and impurity, and the fatwa is that it is permissible whether the trousers were wet at the time of the wind or dry. If he sees on another's garment impurity more than the size of a dirham, he informs him and it is not permissible for him to leave it. The skin of the sheep's gall bladder is impure, and its gall and urine are equal: according to Muhammad they are pure, according to the two companions they are impure. And the sheep's bladder: its ruling is the same as its urine, so that prayer is not allowed with it. If a drop of wine falls into a jar of vinegar, it is not permissible to drink it until after an hour. And if a jug of wine is poured into a jar of vinegar and no taste or smell is found, then drinking is permissible immediately. Chard (silq) and cabbage (saljam) cooked in ash of human waste (ramad al-adhrah) are impure according to Abu Yusuf. End quote.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This long passage from page 405 covers several important rulings and discussions. It begins with a discussion about passing wind while wearing trousers (sarawil) and then praying. Some scholars say it is invalid because wind has subtle particles that penetrate the fabric, but the relied-upon fatwa is that it is permissible, regardless of whether the trousers were wet or dry at the time. The text then digresses into a discussion about the ruling when both water and soil are pure or impure in determining the purity of mud; the preferred view is that if either is pure, the mud is pure, but there is debate. The author praises the view of Qadikhan and Abu al-Layth that the result follows from the worst premise (the more impure component determines the impurity). The text then returns to the main point: 'other than the last' refers to the four issues: bird not eaten, fish blood, saliva of donkey/mule, and urine splashes (like tip of needles); the fatwa is that praying with these impurities is permissible as long as the amount is less than a dirham. Then additional rulings: if one sees an impurity larger than a dirham on another's garment, one must inform them; the skin of a sheep's gall bladder (mirarah) is impure, and according to Muhammad the actual gall and urine of sheep are pure, but according to the two companions they are impure; the bladder of a sheep has the same ruling as its urine (thus impure). Then a rule about wine in vinegar: if a single drop of wine falls into a jar of vinegar, it becomes permissible only after an hour (presumably for the alcohol to transform), but if a whole jug of wine is poured and no taste/smell remains, it is immediately permissible. Finally, vegetables cooked in the ash of human waste are impure according to Abu Yusuf, implying impurity due to contact with najasah.

Key Terms
مرارة (mirarah): Gall bladder, a small organ containing bile.
مثانة (mathanah): Bladder, the organ that stores urine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on the gall (contents) of a sheep's gall bladder according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Impure
B) Pure
C) Makruh
D) It is not mentioned

Key Takeaway
Sheep's gall bladder skin is impure; the gall and urine are subject to internal Hanafi disagreement.

Wine in Vinegar: Transformation and Permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wine that falls into vinegar and identify the conditions under which the mixture becomes permissible to drink.

Core Idea
A single drop of wine requires a waiting period; a large amount with no trace is immediately permissible.

This lesson addresses the transformation (takhallul) of wine into vinegar. The ruling distinguishes between a small drop and a large quantity: a drop needs an hour to transform, while a jug that leaves no taste or smell is immediately halal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Case 1: A single drop of wine falls into a jar of vinegar. Case 2: A whole jug of wine is poured into a jar of vinegar with no remaining taste or smell.
2
State the ruling for each
For the drop: it is not permissible to drink until after an hour. For the jug: it is permissible immediately.
The difference is based on the likelihood of transformation: a drop may not fully mix or transform instantly, while a large amount that leaves no trace shows complete transformation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا فسا في السراويل وصلى معه قال بعضهم : لا يجوز لأن في الريح أجزاء لطيفة فتدخل أجزاء الثوب . وقيل : إن الشيخ الإمام شمس الأئمة الحلواني كان يصلي من غير السراويل ولا تأويل لفعله إلا التحرز من الخلاف، والسراج الوهاج والبزازية وكلهم أطلقوه عن ذكر الخلاف قوله : (فهو مخالف لتصحيح قاضيخان) أقول : قد مشى في المنية على ما ذكره قاضيخان وقال شارحها وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث. وكذا روي عن أبي يوسف ذكره في الخلاصة . وقيل : العبرة للماء إن كان نجساً فالطين نجس وإلا فطاهر. وقيل: العبرة للتراب. وقيل للغالب قال ابن الهمام والأكثر على أنه أيهما كان طاهراً فالطين طاهر اهـ . وهو اختيار أبي نصر محمد بن سلام قال البزازي وهو قول محمد. وقد ذكر أن الفتوى عليه اهـ. ووجهه في الخلاصة بصيرورته شيئاً آخر وهو توجيه ضعيف إذ يقتضي أن جميع الأطعمة إذا كان ماؤها نجساً أو دهنها أو نحو ذلك أن يكون الطعام طاهراً لصيرورته شيئاً آخر، وعلى هذا سائر المركبات إذا كان بعض مفرداتها نجساً ولا يخفى فساده فلله در الفقيه أبي الليث ودر قاضيخان حيث جعل قوله وهو الصحيح مشيراً إلى أن سائر الأقوال لا صحة لها بل هي فاسدة لأن النتيجة تابعة لأخس المقدمتين .اهـ. قوله: (وفيما عدا الأخيرة) أي من المسائل الأربع التي في طير لا يؤكل ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس والفتوى أنه يجوز سواء كان السراويل رطباً وقت الفسوة أو يابساً. إذا رأى على ثوب غيره نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم يخبره ولا يسعه تركه جلد مرارة الغنم نجس ومرارته وبوله سواء عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس. ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم بوله حتى لا تجوز الصلاة معه. إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم قطرة خمر وقعت في دن خل لا يحل شربه إلا بعد ساعة، ولو صب كوز من خمر في دن من خل ولا يوجد له طعم ولا رائحة حل الشراب في الحال. السلق والسلجم المطبوع في رماد العذرة نجس عند أبي يوسف اهـ.
If one passes wind (fasa) in the trousers and prays with it, some said it is not permissible because the wind contains fine particles that enter the fabric of the garment. And it is said that the Shaykh al-Imam Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani would pray without trousers, and there is no explanation for his action except avoidance of disagreement. And Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and Al-Bazzaziyyah, and all of them, stated it without mentioning disagreement: 'So it contradicts the verification of Qadikhan.' I say: In Al-Munya they followed what Qadikhan said, and its commentator said it is the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth. And likewise it is narrated from Abu Yusuf in Al-Khulasah. And it is said the consideration is for the water: if the water is impure, then the mud is impure; otherwise it is pure. And it is said the consideration is for the soil. And it is said for the dominant. Ibn al-Humam said the majority are that whichever of them is pure, the mud is pure. End quote. And it is the choice of Abu Nasr Muhammad ibn Salam, and al-Bazzazi said it is the opinion of Muhammad. And it has been mentioned that the fatwa is upon it. End quote. Vegetables Cooked in Ash of Human Waste

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on vegetables cooked in ash of human waste according to Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Vegetables cooked in the ash of human waste are impure according to Abu Yusuf.

This lesson presents a specific impurity ruling from Abu Yusuf regarding ash from human waste used in cooking. The text simply states the ruling without elaboration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the food and the fuel
The foods are chard (silq) and cabbage (saljam). The fuel is ash of human waste (ramad al-adhrah).
2
State the ruling and the authority
Abu Yusuf rules that such vegetables are impure (najis). The text does not give the ruling of other imams.

Source Text

8 min
Exemption for Light Impurities: The Quarter Standard
Ruling on exemption for light impurities with three measurement opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on light impurities on clothing/body during prayer, identify the three opinions on measuring the quarter, and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Light impurity less than a quarter of the affected part is excused; the quarter is measured by the part affected, not the whole garment.

Purity is of utmost importance; the first question in the grave will be about it. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance on when impurity on one's clothing or body during prayer is excusable. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the exemption for light impurities (mukhaffaf) and the three opinions on how to measure the quarter threshold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the basic rule: light impurities less than a quarter of the garment or body are excused; more than that is prohibited.
The quarter is a practical proxy for the conceptually vague 'excessively large amount' (kathir fahish).
2
Understand the basis
Recognize that Abu Hanifa preferred a subjective standard (what people deem excessive) but accepted the quarter by analogy to other rulings (e.g., wiping the head).
The quarter is attached to the whole in other contexts, so it is used here as well.
3
Differentiate the three opinions
Know each opinion: (1) quarter of the affected part (e.g., sleeve, hem if garment; limb if body) – the mufta bphi; (2) quarter of the entire garment/body; (3) quarter of the minimal garment for prayer.
The third opinion is limited to garments and does not cover the body.
4
Apply the mufta bihi
For fatwa, use the first opinion: quarter of the affected part. This is supported by many later authorities (Tuhfah, Muhit, Bada'i', etc.).
This practical measure is easy to apply in daily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما أكثرنا هذه من الفروع للحاجة إليها ولكون الطهارة من المهمات، ولهذا ورد أن أول شيء يسئل عنه العبد في قبره الطهارة . مثله قوله : (وما دون ربع الثوب من مخفف كبول ما يؤكل والفرس وخرء طير لا يؤكل) أي عفي ما كان من النجاسات أقل من ربع الثوب المصاب إذا كانت النجاسة مخففة لأن التقدير فيها بالكثير الفاحش للمنع على ما روي عن أبي حنيفة على ما هو دأبه في من عدم التقدير، وهو ما يستكثره الناظر ويستفحشه حتى روي عنه أنه كره تقديره وقال : الفاحش يختلف باختلاف طباع الناس لكن لما كان الربع ملحقاً بالكل في بعض الأحكام كمسح الرأس وانكشاف العورة ألحق به هنا وبالكل يحصل الاستفحاش فكذا بما قام مقامه وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة أيضاً، وصححه الشارح وغيره. وفي الهداية وعليه الاعتماد واختاره في فتح القدير وقال : إنه أحسن لاعتبار الربع كثيراً كالكل . ثم اختلفوا في كيفية اعتبار الربع على ثلاثة أقوال : فقيل ربع طرف أصابته النجاسة كالذيل والكم والدخريص إن كان المصاب ثوباً، وربع العضو المصاب كاليد والرجل إن كان بدناً وصححه صاحب التحفة والمحيط والبدائع والمجتبى والسراج الوهاج وفي الحقائق وعليه الفتوى وقيل ربع جميع الثوب والبدن وصححه صاحب المبسوط . وقيل ربع أدنى ثوب تجوز فيه الصلاة كالمئزر وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة . قال شارح القدوري الإمام البغدادي : الأقطع وهذا أصح ما روي فيه من غيره ا هـ. لكنه قاصر على الثوب ولم يفد حكم البدن فقد اختلف التصحيح كما ترى لكن الأول بأن الفتوى عليه. وفي فتح القدير ما يقتضي التوفيق بين القولين الأخيرين بأن يكون المراد من اعتبار ربع جميع الثوب الساتر الجميع بدن الذي هو عليه، وإن كان الذي هو عليه أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة اعتبر ربعه لأنه الكثير بالنسبة إلى المصاب ا هـ. وهو حسن جداً ترجح ، المجتبى . قوله : (ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم (بوله) قال الخير الرملي هذا لا يناسب قوله بعد ذلك لا تجوز الصلاة معه إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم إذ يول الغنم نجاسته مخففة، والمثانة على قوله هذا مغلظة فلم يكن حكمه حكمها، ولو فعل كما فعل أخوه في نهره حيث قال : واعلم أن الظاهر من إطلاقهم نجاسة شيء التغليظ كالاسآر النجسة وثوب الحية الذي لم يدبغ والدودة | الساقطة من السبيلين على
And we have expanded these branches due to the need for them and because purity is of important matters. For this reason it is narrated that the first thing a servant is asked about in his grave is purity. Similarly his saying: (and what is less than a quarter of the garment of light impurities, like the dung of something edible, the horse, and the droppings of a bird not eaten) meaning: exempted are those impurities that are less than a quarter of the affected garment when the impurity is light (mukhaffaf). Because the standard for prohibition is the excessively large amount (al-kathir al-fahish) as narrated from Abu Hanifa, in accordance with his practice of not setting a fixed amount. And 'that which the observer deems much and excessive' - it is narrated that he disliked specifying a limit and said: the excessive differs according to people's temperaments. But since the quarter is attached to the whole in some rulings, like wiping the head and uncovering the private parts, it is attached here. And with the whole, excessiveness is achieved, so likewise with what stands in its place - this is also a narration from Abu Hanifa, and the commentator and others have declared it sound. And in Al-Hidayah it is relied upon, and it was chosen in Fath al-Qadir, and he said: it is better to consider the quarter as much like the whole. Then they differed on how to consider the quarter according to three sayings: Some said: a quarter of the part affected by the impurity, like the hem, sleeve, or the lower edge if it is a garment, and a quarter of the affected limb, like the hand or foot if it is the body - and this was declared sound by the author of Al-Tuhfah, Al-Muhit, Al-Bada'i', Al-Mujtaba, Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and in Al-Haqa'iq, and the fatwa is upon it. Some said: a quarter of the entire garment and body - declared sound by the author of Al-Mabsut. Some said: a quarter of the minimal garment in which prayer is permissible, such as the waist wrapper (mi'zar) - this is a narration from Abu Hanifa. The commentator of Al-Quduri, Imam al-Baghdadi said: 'al-Aqta'' (the one-armed? Actually unclear) and this is the soundest of what is narrated about it. But it is limited to garments and does not cover the ruling of the body. So the verification differs, as you see, but the first is the fatwa. And in Fath al-Qadir there is something indicating a reconciliation between the last two sayings: that what is meant by considering a quarter of the entire garment is the garment that covers the entire body on which it is worn, but if the garment is the minimum in which prayer is permissible, its quarter is considered because it is much relative to the affected part. End quote. And it is very good and preponderant, Al-Mujtaba. His saying: (And the bladder of sheep: its ruling is the ruling of its urine) Al-Khayr al-Ramli said: This is inconsistent with his subsequent statement 'prayer is not allowed with it if it exceeds a dirham' since sheep's urine is a light impurity, and the bladder according to this statement would be a serious impurity, so its ruling would not be the same. And if he did as his brother did in his Nahrah where he said: know that the apparent from their unconditional statements of impurity of something is severity (taghliz), like the residual waters (as'ar) that are impure, the skin of a snake that has not been tanned, and the worm falling from the two passages on...
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage explains the exemption for light impurities on clothing when the amount is less than a quarter of the garment. The author notes that he has included many subsidiary rulings because purification is important. The base ruling from the matn (كنز الدقائق) is that impurities of a light nature (mukhaffaf) such as the dung of animals whose meat is eaten (like horses) and the droppings of birds not eaten, are excused if they are less than a quarter of the garment. This is based on the Hanafi principle that prohibition applies only to an excessive amount (al-kathir al-fahish). Abu Hanifa generally disliked fixing a specific number because what is considered excessive varies. However, the quarter standard is adopted by analogy to other rulings where a quarter relates to the whole (like wiping head). There are three opinions on how to measure the quarter: 1) a quarter of the part of the garment that was affected (e.g., sleeve, hem) or a quarter of the limb if on the body; 2) a quarter of the total garment or body; 3) a quarter of the minimum garment permissible for prayer (e.g., a waist-wrapper). The first opinion is declared sound by most authorities (Tuhfah, Muhit, Bada'i', Mujtaba, Siraj, Haqa'iq) and the fatwa is upon it. The second is supported by Al-Mabsut, and the third is a narration from Abu Hanifa but limited to clothing. The text then attempts a reconciliation from Fath al-Qadir: the quarter of the entire garment refers to the garment that covers the entire body; if the garment is minimal, its quarter is considered because relative to the affected part it is much. Finally, the passage discusses a discrepancy regarding the bladder of sheep: if its urine is light impurity, the bladder should also be light, but the matn says prayer is not allowed with it if it exceeds a dirham, which is the rule for heavy impurities. This is an unresolved issue in the text.

Key Terms
المخفف (al-mukhaffaf): Light impurity, such as urine of animals whose meat is eaten, or droppings of birds that are not edible.
الربع (al-rub'): The quarter proportion used as a threshold for exemption of light impurity on clothing/body.
الكثير الفاحش (al-kathir al-fahish): The excessively large amount that is noticeably distasteful; the criterion for prohibition of impurity in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, how is the quarter measured for light impurity on a garment?
A) Quarter of the entire garment
B) Quarter of the minimal garment permissible in prayer
C) Quarter of the part that was affected (e.g., sleeve, hem)
D) Quarter of the section where the impurity is located only

Key Takeaway
Light impurity less than a quarter of the affected part (not the whole garment) is excused in prayer – a practical standard from the Hanafi school.

6 min
Rulings on Light Impurities (al-Najasah al-Mukhaffafah)
Listing light impurities and their concession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific types of light impurities and state the Hanafi concession threshold.

Core Idea
Certain impurities are excused if less than a quarter of the garment.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage which lists several impurities that are considered 'light' in the Hanafi school. These include urine of a bird not eaten, fish blood, saliva of mule and donkey, and urine that splatters like needle heads. The fatwa permits prayer even if the trousers were wet at the time, indicating that the impurity does not require removal if it is minimal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types
List the specific impurities mentioned: bird not eaten, fish blood, mule/donkey saliva, and splattered urine.
These are all from non-pure animals or substances.
2
Note the threshold
The passage states 'al-fatwa annahu ja'iz' - the fatwa is that it is permissible. The condition 'whether wet or dry' suggests that slight spreading does not affect the ruling.
The threshold is less than a quarter of the garment.
3
Distinguish from heavy impurities
Heavy impurities like dog saliva or pig have no concession even in small amounts.
This is a Hanafi distinction.
4
Apply the ruling
If the impurity is one of these types and covers less than a quarter, prayer is valid. If it exceeds, it must be washed.
The concession is only for these specific types.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طير لا يؤكل ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس والفتوى أنه يجوز سواء كان السراويل رطباً وقت الفسوة أو يابساً. إذا رأى على ثوب غيره نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم يخبره ولا يسعه تركه جلد مرارة الغنم نجس ومرارته وبوله سواء عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس. ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم بوله حتى لا تجوز الصلاة معه. إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم قطرة خمر وقعت في دن خل لا يحل شربه إلا بعد ساعة، ولو صب كوز من خمر في دن من خل ولا يوجد له طعم ولا رائحة حل الشراب في الحال. السلق والسلجم المطبوع في رماد العذرة نجس عند أبي يوسف اهـ. وإنما أكثرنا هذه من الفروع للحاجة إليها ولكون الطهارة من المهمات، ولهذا ورد أن أول شيء يسئل عنه العبد في قبره الطهارة .
A bird that is not eaten, fish blood, the saliva of mule and donkey, urine that splashes like the heads of needles, and the impure, and the fatwa is that it is permissible whether the trousers were wet at the time of the fart or dry. If he sees on another's garment an impurity more than the size of a dirham, he should inform him and it is not permissible for him to leave it. The skin of the gall bladder of a sheep is impure, and its gall bladder and its urine are the same: according to Muhammad they are pure, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa) they are impure. The bladder of a sheep has the same ruling as its urine, so prayer is not permissible with it if it exceeds the size of a dirham. A drop of wine that falls into a jar of vinegar, its drinking is not permissible until after an hour. And if a jug of wine is poured into a jar of vinegar and no taste or smell of it remains, drinking is permissible immediately. Chard and turnip cooked in the ashes of human feces are impure according to Abu Yusuf, end. And we have multiplied these furu' due to the need for them and because purification is among the important matters, and for this reason it is narrated that the first thing a servant is asked about in his grave is purification.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a collection of subsidiary rulings (furu') on various impurities. The author lists several cases: the urine of a bird that is not eaten (e.g., hawk), fish blood, saliva of mule and donkey, and urine that splatters in tiny amounts are excused according to the fatwa. He then addresses the obligation to inform a fellow Muslim if one sees an impurity larger than a dirham on his garment. Next, he discusses the gall bladder and bladder of sheep: according to Imam Muhammad, the bladder and its contents are pure (tahir), while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider them impure. The operative ruling follows the majority. Then he deals with wine falling into vinegar: if a drop falls, it becomes permissible only after an hour (to allow transformation), but if a large quantity is poured and no trace remains, it is immediately permissible. Lastly, he mentions that vegetables cooked in the ashes of human feces are impure according to Abu Yusuf. The author concludes by noting that he has included many such furu' because of their practical importance in purification, which is the first matter a person will be questioned about in the grave.

Key Terms
النَّجاسة المُخففة (al-najasah al-mukhaffafah): Light impurities that are excused if less than a quarter of the garment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is considered a light impurity according to the passage?
A) Dog saliva
B) Urine of a bird that is not eaten
C) Wine
D) Human feces

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts specific light impurities (like bird urine and fish blood) if they cover less than a quarter of the garment.

Obligation to Inform about Impurity on Another's Garment
Ruling on informing about impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on seeing an impurity on another person's garment and apply it to real situations.

Core Idea
If you see an impurity larger than a dirham on another's garment, you must inform them.

This lesson addresses the social responsibility of a Muslim towards his brother. The passage states that if one sees an impurity larger than a dirham on someone's garment, it is obligatory to inform him, and it is not permissible to remain silent. This is based on the principle of mutual advice and removing harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
You see an impurity on another's garment that is more than the size of a dirham.
Dirham is about 2.97 grams but here it refers to a coin-sized area.
2
Determine the obligation
You must inform the person. It is not permissible to leave it.
This is based on the hadith 'Religion is sincere advice'.
3
Consider the amount
Only if it exceeds the size of a dirham; smaller amounts are excused.
The threshold for informing is same as for the impurity being significant.
4
Understand the reason
The person may be unaware and may pray with impurity, invalidating his prayer.
Failing to inform is like letting him sin.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Sheep Gall Bladder and Bladder
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sheep organs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two companions (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the purity of sheep gall bladder and bladder.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad holds the gall bladder and bladder of a sheep are pure, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider them impure.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The skin of the gall bladder is impure by consensus, but the contents and the bladder itself are disputed. Imam Muhammad considers them pure (tahir), while the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider them impure (najis). The operative ruling follows the majority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The gall bladder (mararah) and bladder (mathanah) of a sheep.
Sheep is an edible animal, so its urine is normally pure, but the bladder contains urine.
2
State the consensus
The skin of the gall bladder is impure (najis) by agreement.
This is because it is a part of the animal that is normally discarded and may contain impure fluids.
3
State the disagreement
Imam Muhammad says the gall bladder and its contents (including bile) are pure. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say they are impure.
The difference arises from whether the bile and bladder are considered impure due to origin.
4
Determine the operative ruling
The passage does not give a fatwa, but by context, the majority view is mufta bihi.
Later Hanafi works follow the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Transformation of Wine into Vinegar (Takhallul)
Ruling on wine falling into vinegar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wine that falls into vinegar and the conditions for its permissibility.

Core Idea
A drop of wine in vinegar requires an hour before it becomes permissible; a full jug poured in is immediately permissible if no trace remains.

This lesson covers the process of transformation (takhallul) of wine into vinegar. The ruling distinguishes between a small amount (a drop) and a large amount (a jug). If a drop falls into a jar of vinegar, you must wait an hour for it to transform completely. If a whole jug of wine is poured into a jar of vinegar, and no taste or smell of wine remains, it is permissible immediately. The key factor is whether any trace of wine remains.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Case 1: A drop of wine falls into vinegar. Case 2: A jug of wine is poured into vinegar.
The difference is the ratio.
2
Apply the ruling to case 1
It is not permissible to drink until after an hour, presumably for the transformation to complete.
The hour is a precaution to ensure complete conversion.
3
Apply the ruling to case 2
If no taste or smell of wine remains, it is immediately permissible.
Large quantity accelerates transformation.
4
Understand the principle
The transformation from impure (wine) to pure (vinegar) occurs when the wine changes into vinegar. The ruling depends on whether the change is complete.
This is based on the hadith 'Vinegar is a good condiment' and the principle that impurities become pure through transformation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طير لا يؤكل ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس والفتوى أنه يجوز سواء كان السراويل رطباً وقت الفسوة أو يابساً. إذا رأى على ثوب غيره نجاسة أكثر من قدر الدرهم يخبره ولا يسعه تركه جلد مرارة الغنم نجس ومرارته وبوله سواء عند محمد طاهر، وعندهما نجس. ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم بوله حتى لا تجوز الصلاة معه. إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم قطرة خمر وقعت في دن خل لا يحل شربه إلا بعد ساعة، ولو صب كوز من خمر في دن من خل ولا يوجد له طعم ولا رائحة حل الشراب في الحال. السلق والسلجم المطبوع في رماد العذرة نجس عند أبي يوسف اهـ. وإنما أكثرنا هذه من الفروع للحاجة إليها ولكون الطهارة من المهمات، ولهذا ورد أن أول شيء يسئل عنه العبد في قبره الطهارة .
A bird that is not eaten, fish blood, the saliva of mule and donkey, urine that splashes like the heads of needles, and the impure, and the fatwa is that it is permissible whether the trousers were wet at the time of the fart or dry. If he sees on another's garment an impurity more than the size of a dirham, he should inform him and it is not permissible for him to leave it. The skin of the gall bladder of a sheep is impure, and its gall bladder and its urine are the same: according to Muhammad they are pure, and according to them (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa) they are impure. The bladder of a sheep has the same ruling as its urine, so prayer is not permissible with it if it exceeds the size of a dirham. A drop of wine that falls into a jar of vinegar, its drinking is not permissible until after an hour. And if a jug of wine is poured into a jar of vinegar and no taste or smell of it remains, drinking is permissible immediately. Chard and turnip cooked in the ashes of human feces are impure according to Abu Yusuf, end. And we have multiplied these furu' due to the need for them and because purification is among the important matters, and for this reason it is narrated that the first thing a servant is asked about in his grave is purification.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a collection of subsidiary rulings (furu') on various impurities. The author lists several cases: the urine of a bird that is not eaten (e.g., hawk), fish blood, saliva of mule and donkey, and urine that splatters in tiny amounts are excused according to the fatwa. He then addresses the obligation to inform a fellow Muslim if one sees an impurity larger than a dirham on his garment. Next, he discusses the gall bladder and bladder of sheep: according to Imam Muhammad, the bladder and its contents are pure (tahir), while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider them impure. The operative ruling follows the majority. Then he deals with wine falling into vinegar: if a drop falls, it becomes permissible only after an hour (to allow transformation), but if a large quantity is poured and no trace remains, it is immediately permissible. Lastly, he mentions that vegetables cooked in the ashes of human feces are impure according to Abu Yusuf. The author concludes by noting that he has included many such furu' because of their practical importance in purification, which is the first matter a person will be questioned about in the grave.

Key Terms
تخلل (takhallul): Transformation of wine into vinegar

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when can a mixture of wine and vinegar be drunk immediately?
A) If the wine is a drop
B) If a full jug of wine is poured in and no trace remains
C) After exactly one hour
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Wine that falls into vinegar becomes permissible after transformation: a drop requires an hour, a large pour is immediate if no trace remains.

Vegetables Cooked in Impure Ashes: Ruling According to Abu Yusuf
Ruling on vegetables cooked in impure ashes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on vegetables cooked in ashes of human feces and identify the narrator (Abu Yusuf).

Core Idea
Vegetables cooked in ashes of human feces are impure according to Abu Yusuf.

This final ruling in the passage deals with vegetables (chard and turnip) that are cooked in the ashes of human feces (al-udhrah). According to Abu Yusuf, they become impure. This illustrates that impurities can transfer through indirect means like ash that was contaminated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the substance
Human feces (al-udhrah) is used as fuel, producing ash. The ash is used in cooking vegetables.
Feces is najis, but ash is normally pure. However, here the ash still carries impurity.
2
Note the ruling
Abu Yusuf says the vegetables are impure (najis).
This is a specific ruling from Abu Yusuf; the passage does not give the majority view.
3
Understand the basis
The ash may still contain particles of impurity, making it najis. Contact with the vegetables transfers impurity.
This is a cautionary ruling.
4
Contrast with other views
The passage does not mention other views, but presumably Abu Hanifa or Muhammad may differ.
The passage ends with 'according to Abu Yusuf'.

Concession for Light Impurities and Measurement of the Quarter
Explaining the concession for light impurities and the dispute on how to measure the quarter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on light impurities below a quarter of the garment and explain the intra-madhhab differences on calculating the quarter and the status of urine of edible animals.

Core Idea
Light impurities are excused below a quarter of the garment/limb, but how to measure the quarter and whether certain urines are light is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the concession for light impurities. While the basic ruling is clear, the text reveals multiple opinions on the technical measurement of 'quarter' and a significant disagreement on the classification of edible animal urine. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and its basis
Locate the claim that light impurities are excused if less than a quarter of the garment. Note that this concession is based on a transmitted estimate from Abu Hanifa, who originally disliked a fixed measure but later approved the quarter analogy.
The quarter concept is borrowed from similar rulings (e.g., wiping the head, 'awrah).
2
Trace the dispute on measuring the quarter
Identify the three opinions: (1) quarter of the affected part (sleeve, hem, limb), (2) quarter of the entire garment or body, (3) quarter of the minimal garment for prayer. Note which opinion is relied upon for fatwa and the reconciliation in Fath al-Qadir.
The first opinion is the mufta bihi.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on urine of edible animals
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf classify it as light impurity (mukhaffaf), while Muhammad considers it pure. Understand the textual evidence: the 'Urayniyyun hadith and the hadith 'Guard against urine' are in apparent conflict, leading to the difference.
The conflict of texts is not definitively resolved, so the lighter ruling is adopted.
4
Understand the reconciliation of the last two opinions on the quarter
Examine how Fath al-Qadir reconciles opinions (2) and (3): if the garment covers the whole body, its quarter; if minimal, the quarter of that minimal garment. This is considered 'kathir' relative to the affected part.
This shows the Hanafi method of harmonizing divergent riwayat.

Source Text

الأخيرين بأن يكون المراد من اعتبار ربع جميع الثوب الساتر الجميع بدن الذي هو عليه، وإن كان الذي هو عليه أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة اعتبر ربعه لأنه الكثير بالنسبة إلى المصاب ا هـ. وهو حسن جداً. ولم ينقل النصين وهما حديث العرنيين وحديث «استنزهوا البول. وفي الكافي : فإن قيل تعارض النصين كيف يتحقق وحديث العرنيين منسوخ عنده . قلنا : إنه قال ذلك رأياً ولم يقطع به فتكون صورة التعارض قائمة ا هـ. وهو أحسن أبين من الجي ولو سنا ومثانة الغنم .ومرارته لكان أولى. قوله : (الدخريص) قال الشيخ إسمعيل النابلسي رحمه الله : هو بكسر الدال المهملة وسكون الخاء المعجمة بالصاد المهملة. قيل هو معرب، وقيل عربي وهو عند العرب البنيقة. والدخرص والدخروصة لغة والجمع دخارص في المصباح اهـ. قوله : (لكن) ترجح الأول (الخ ) قال في النهر : وكلام المصنف يعطي اعتبار ربع كما ربع جميع الثوب قال في المبسوط وهو الأصح . ثم قال وما في الكتاب أولى لما مر ، ولا شك أن . المصاب ليس كثيراً فضلاً عن أن يكون فاحشاً ولضعف وجه هذا القول لم يعرج عليه في فتح القدير . قوله : (وفي فتح القدير ما يقتضي التوفيق الخ) قال في النهر : أقول فيه نظر بل إنما فيه تقييد حسن لمحل الخلاف وذلك أن اعتبار ربع الجميع محله ما إذا كان لابساً له، أما إذا لم يكن عليه إلا ثوب تجوز به الصلاة اعتبر ربعه اتفاقاً. ومقتضى القول الثاني أنه لو كان عليه ثوب كامل فتنجس منه أقل من الربع إلا أنه لو اعتبر بأدنى ثوب تجوز فيه الصلاة بلغ سنة ربعاً منع اهـ. أقول: وهو المتبادر في بادىء النظر من عبارة الفتح حيث ذكر ذلك على صورة التقييد والاستدراك على الإطلاق وعبارته هكذا، ويظهر أن الأول يعني اعتبار الربع أحسن لاعتبار الربع كثيراً كالكل في مسألة الثوب تنجس الأربعة وانكشاف ربع العضو من العورة بخلاف ما دونه فيهما غير أن ذلك الثوب الذي هو عليه إن كان شاملاً اعتبر ،ربعه وإن كان أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة اعتبر ربعه لأنه الكثير بالنسبة إلى الثوب المصاب اهـ. وحاصل كلام النهر أن مراد المحقق التنبيه على أن محل الخلاف هو ما إذا كان لابساً للشامل لا للأدنى بل هو محل وفاق، يخفى بعده بعد التأمل في كلام المحقق. والظاهر ما قاله في البحر وقد سبقه إليه العلامة الحلبي فقال : ووفق الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام بين هذا وبين القول الأول بأن الثوب إن كان شاملاً للبدن اعتبر ربعه وإن كان أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة اعتبر ربعه لأنه الكثير بالنسبة إلى الثوب المصاب أي لأن ربع الثوب الشامل كثير بالنسبة إليه وربع أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة كثير بالنسبة إليه وإن كان قليلاً بالنسبة إلى الشامل وهذا هو المختار .اهـ. قوله : (وهو أحسن مما أجاب به في النهاية إلا أنه قال في النهر وفيه نظر لا يخفى .اهـ. وعبارة النهاية سؤالاً وجواباً هكذا فإن قيل التعارض إنما يتحقق إذا جهل التاريخ وقد قيل إن في حديث العرنيين دلالة التقدم لأن فيه المثلة وهي منسوخة فيدل على نسخ الباقي قلت : الدلالة دون العبارة وفي عبارته تعارض فرجح جانب العبارة فيتحقق التعارض أو نقول : انتساخ المثلة لا يدل على انتساخ طهارة بول ما
His statement: 'And what is less than a quarter of the garment from light impurity, like the urine of what is eaten (i.e., edible animals), the horse, and the droppings of a bird that is not eaten' means that what is less than a quarter of the affected garment from impurities is excused if the impurity is light, because the estimation for it is by the gross excess (al-kathir al-fahish) for prohibition, as narrated from Abu Hanifa, in line with his practice of not setting a fixed measure, and it is what the viewer considers much and excessive. It is even narrated that he disliked estimating it and said: 'The grossness varies with people's natures.' But since a quarter is attached to the whole in some rulings, like wiping the head and uncovering the 'awrah, it is attached here, and by the whole grossness is achieved, so also by what stands in its place. This is a narration from Abu Hanifa, and the commentator and others considered it sound. In al-Hidayah, it is relied upon, and it was chosen in Fath al-Qadir, who said it is better for considering a quarter as much like the whole. Then they differed on how to consider the quarter on three opinions: some said a quarter of the part affected by the impurity, like the hem, sleeve, and الدخريص if the garment is affected, and a quarter of the affected limb like the hand or foot if it is the body. This was considered sound by the author of al-Tuhfah, al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', al-Mujtaba, and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and in al-Haqa'iq it is the basis of fatwa. Some said a quarter of the entire garment and body, considered sound by the author of al-Mabsut. Some said a quarter of the minimal garment in which prayer is permissible, like the waist-wrapper, which is a narration from Abu Hanifa. Sharh al-Quduri, Imam al-Baghdadi, said: 'It is the most sound narration from him.' But it is limited to the garment and does not cover the body. The reconciliation in Fath al-Qadir is to consider that if the garment is covering the whole body, then a quarter of it is considered, but if it is the minimal garment for prayer, then a quarter of that is considered, because it is much relative to the affected garment. This is good. The first opinion was not transmitted at all. The author gave three examples of light impurities: first, urine of edible meat, which is light according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), pure according to Muhammad, based on the hadith of al-'Urayniyyun. Abu Yusuf said it is light due to the difference of scholars on its origin, and Abu Hanifa also said so due to the conflict of two texts: the hadith of al-'Urayniyyun and the hadith 'Guard against urine.' In al-Kafi: if it is asked how the conflict arises while the hadith of al-'Urayniyyun is abrogated according to him, we say: he said that as an opinion and did not affirm it, so the conflict remains. This is better than the answer in al-Nihayah. The second example is horse urine, which is included in the previous, but due to disagreement on eating its meat, it might be mistakenly thought to be included in urine of inedible animals. The third example... Then a discussion on the term الدخريص. Then a discussion on the three opinions and the reconciliation in Fath al-Qadir. Finally, a discussion on the 'Urayniyyun hadith and the resolution of the textual conflict.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn that states the concession for light impurities (mukhaffaf) when they cover less than a quarter of the affected garment. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa initially avoided a fixed measure, relying on what is considered excessive by the viewer. However, since a quarter is analogous to the whole in other rulings (e.g., wiping a quarter of the head, uncovering a quarter of the 'awrah), it is adopted as the threshold. The passage then delves into a three-opinion dispute on how to calculate the quarter: (1) a quarter of the part affected (e.g., sleeve or hem for clothes, or limb for body), which is the relied-upon position for fatwa; (2) a quarter of the entire garment or body, considered by al-Mabsut; (3) a quarter of the minimal garment for prayer, a narration from Abu Hanifa. The commentator reconciles the last two views in Fath al-Qadir: if the garment covers the whole body, its quarter is considered; if it is minimal, the quarter of that minimal garment is considered, as it is 'much' relative to the affected part. The text then discusses the examples of light impurities given by the author: the urine of edible animals, horse urine, and droppings of inedible birds. For urine of edible animals, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider it light (mukhaffaf), while Muhammad considers it pure (tahir) based on the hadith of the 'Urayniyyun. The commentator addresses the issue of apparent contradiction between the 'Urayniyyun hadith and the hadith 'Guard against urine,' explaining that even though the 'Urayniyyun hadith is considered abrogated by some, the conflict still exists because the abrogation is not certain. The passage ends with a detailed discussion of the reconciliation of the opinions on calculating the quarter, citing various authorities.

Key Terms
المخفف (al-mukhaffaf): Light impurity that is excused in prayer if it covers less than a quarter of the garment. Examples: urine of edible animals, horse urine, droppings of inedible birds.
الربع (al-rub‘): The threshold for excusing light impurities: less than a quarter of the affected garment or limb. Disputed how to calculate this quarter.
الدخريص (al-dakhris): A narrow strip or part of a garment, similar to a border or hem; used as an example of a part of the garment that may be affected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, how is the quarter for light impurities measured?
A) A quarter of the entire garment
B) A quarter of the part affected (e.g., sleeve or limb)
C) A quarter of the minimal garment for prayer
D) It is not measured by quarter but by what is considered gross

Key Takeaway
Light impurities below a quarter of the affected part are excused in prayer, but the exact measurement and the status of certain urines involve valid intra-madhhab disputes.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on the Bladder of Sheep: Intra-Hanafi Dispute over Light and Heavy Impurity
Critiquing the equation of the bladder with urine, noting a discrepancy in degrees of impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the ruling of the sheep's bladder and apply the distinction between light (mukhaffaf) and heavy (mughallazah) impurity in taharah.

Core Idea
The bladder of a sheep is not automatically light impurity like its urine; solids from impure sources are generally heavy.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques a ruling in the matn Kanz al-Daqa'iq that equates the bladder of a sheep with its urine. Al-Khayr al-Ramli points out an inconsistency: if the urine is light impurity, the bladder, being a solid organ, should be heavy impurity according to Hanafi principles. This intra-madhhab dispute highlights the need for consistency in classifying impurities and affects the validity of prayer when such impurities are present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from the matn
The matn states that the bladder of a sheep has the same ruling as its urine. This implies it is light impurity.
The matn's position is that the bladder is mukhaffaf (light).
2
Understand the legal implication of the matn's ruling
Since sheep urine is light impurity, prayer is invalid if it exceeds the size of a dirham. Therefore, the bladder would also be excused in small amounts.
Light impurities have a higher threshold (dirham) before invalidating prayer.
3
Recognize the critique by al-Khayr al-Ramli
He argues that the bladder should be heavy impurity because solids from impure sources are generally mughallazah. He cites examples like impure vessels, untanned snake skin, and worms from private parts.
The critique is based on the principle that physical objects (solids) that contact impurity become heavily impure.
4
Trace the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If the bladder is considered light, it is excused below a dirham; if heavy, it may invalidate prayer even in small amounts, or require stricter washing.
The dispute affects the validity of salah when a small residue of bladder is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومثانة الغنم حكمه حكم (بوله) قال الخير الرملي هذا لا يناسب قوله بعد ذلك لا تجوز الصلاة معه إذا زاد على قدر الدرهم إذ يول الغنم نجاسته مخففة، والمثانة على قوله هذا مغلظة فلم يكن حكمه حكمها، ولو فعل كما فعل أخوه في نهره حيث قال : واعلم أن الظاهر من إطلاقهم نجاسة شيء التغليظ كالاسآر النجسة وثوب الحية الذي لم يدبغ والدودة الساقطة من السبيلين على
His statement: 'And the bladder of a sheep has the same ruling as its urine.' Al-Khayr al-Ramli said: This does not suit his statement later: 'Prayer is not permitted with it if it exceeds the size of a dirham', because the urine of the sheep is light impurity, while the bladder according to this statement is heavy (mughallazah), so its ruling is not the same as its urine. If only he had done as his brother did in his book al-Nahr, where he said: 'Know that the apparent from their general statements regarding the impurity of something is that it is heavy (mughallazah), like impure vessels (al-asar al-najisah), the skin of a snake that has not been tanned, and the worm fallen from the two passages...'
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hāshiyah-style) of the matn's ruling that equates the bladder of a sheep with its urine. Al-Khayr al-Ramli points out a contradiction: if the urine of sheep is considered light impurity (mukhaffaf), then the bladder, which is a solid organ, should be classified as heavy impurity (mughallazah) according to the general principle that solid impurities are heavy. Therefore, equating the two rulings is inconsistent. He suggests that the author should have followed his brother's approach in al-Nahr, which treats such items as heavy impurities, listing examples like impure vessels (al-asar al-najisah), untanned snake skin, and a worm coming from the private parts. The commentary thus highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute over the correct classification of the bladder and calls for consistency in applying the light/heavy impurity distinction.

Key Terms
المثانة (al-mathānah): The bladder of an animal, specifically sheep, whose ruling is disputed: is it a container of impurity or itself impure?
التغليظ (al-taghlīẓ): Classification as heavy impurity (mughallazah), which has stricter rules and is not excused even in small amounts.
المخفف (al-mukhaffaf): Light impurity, typically of fluid origin, which is excused if less than a dirham (for urine) or quarter (for other light impurities).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khayr al-Ramli, why is the matn's equation of the bladder with urine problematic?
A) Because urine is heavy impurity
B) Because the bladder should be heavy impurity, not light
C) Because the bladder is pure
D) Because the bladder and urine are both light

Key Takeaway
The bladder of a sheep is impure according to the majority of Hanafi scholars, but its classification as light or heavy impurity is disputed; al-Khayr al-Ramli argues for heavy impurity based on the principle that solids from impure sources are generally mughallazah.

Taharah — Purification

Three Light Impurities and Their Hanafi Rulings
Explaining three light impurities and Hanafi internal disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of light impurities in Hanafi fiqh and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the dung of non-edible birds.

Core Idea
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes three impurity levels: light (mukhaffaf), heavy (mghallaz), and pure (tahir), with the third type contested.

Impurities in Hanafi law are not all equal. Some are considered light, requiring less washing, while others are heavy. This lesson examines the three categories of light impurities as outlined in Kanz al-Daqa'iq, focusing on the intra-Hanafi disagreements, especially regarding bird droppings. Understanding these nuances is essential for correct purification practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
List the three types of light impurities mentioned: urine of edible animals, horse urine, and dung of non-edible birds.
The author classifies these as mukhaffaf (light) in the matn.
2
Examine the positions of the three imams
For each type, note the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The first two are mukhaffaf according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and tahir according to Muhammad.
Horse urine follows the same pattern due to the dispute over eating horse meat.
3
Understand the evidence conflict
The ruling for urine of edible animals is based on two conflicting hadith: one implies purity (al-Uraniyyin), the other impurity (istanzihu min al-bawl). Abu Hanifa derives takhfif due to ta'arud.
Some claim the hadith is abrogated; Ibn al-Humam rejects this.
4
Analyze the dispute on the third type
For dung of non-edible birds, two narrations from Hinduwani and Karkhi exist. Hinduwani reports it as mukhaffaf according to Abu Hanifa, mghallaz according to the Sahibayn. Karkhi reports it as tahir according to both and mghallaz according to Muhammad.
Abu Yusuf has three riwayat: tahara, taghleez, takhfif.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is that the third type is mukhaffaf (light impurity) following Hinduwani's narration, as it aligns with the matn and general necessity.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq favors this correction.

Source Text

النجاسة يقيناً بل يثبت الشك بالتعارض قوله : (والأولى اعتماد التصحيح الأول) قال النهر : ولا يخفى أنها بقولهما أنسب إذ لا وجه للتغليظ مع ثبوت الاختلاف وما في البحر من إن رواية الكرخي ضعيفة وإن رجحت And the first opinion was not transmitted at all. The author exemplified the light impurities with three: first, the urine of what is eaten; it is light according to both (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), pure according to Muhammad, the hadith of al-Uraniyyin. Abu Yusuf said it is light due to the disagreement of scholars on his principle, and Abu Hanifa also said so due to the conflict of the two texts, which are the hadith of al-Uraniyyin and the hadith 'Be careful to avoid urine'. In al-Kafi: if it is said how can the conflict be realized while the hadith of al-Uraniyyin is abrogated according to him? We say: he said that as an opinion and did not assert it, so the possibility of conflict remains. It is better than the answer in al-Nihaya, for the author of al-Inaya rejected it, so refer. Second, the urine of the horse; it is included in the previous, but because there is dispute about eating its meat, it might be thought that it is included in the urine of what is not eaten. The statement that it is nullifying... what is clearer from the water? and even if it is a tooth and the bladder of a sheep and its gall bladder would be better. His statement (al-Dhakhris): Sheikh Isma'il al-Nabulsi said: it is with a kasra on the dal and sukun on the kha and with a sad; it is said to be Persianized, and it is Arabic meaning the front of the gown. Al-Dhakhras and al-Dhakhrusa are linguistic, plural dakharis in al-Misbah. According to the Imam it would be heavy, but it is not so; it is light according to both, pure according to Muhammad, like the urine of what is eaten. The Imam disliked its meat either as tanzih or tahrim with difference in verification because it is the mount of jihad, not because its meat is impure, evidenced by the fact that its leftover water is pure by consensus. The third: the dung of a bird not eaten; the two imams al-Hinduwani and al-Karkhi differed in what they transmitted from our imams concerning it. Al-Hinduwani narrated that it is light according to the Imam, heavy according to both. Al-Karkhi narrated that it is pure according to both, heavy according to Muhammad. It is said that Abu Yusuf agreed with Abu Hanifa on lightness, so they agreed it is heavy according to Muhammad. As for Abu Yusuf, he has three narrations: purity, heaviness, and lightness. As for Abu Hanifa, two narrations: lightness and purity. As for heaviness, it is not transmitted from him. Qadikhan in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir corrected that it is impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf such that if it falls into a small amount of water it spoils it; it is said it does not spoil due to difficulty of preserving vessels from it. The commentator and a group adopted the narration of al-Hinduwani, so it is light according to him due to general necessity which necessitates lightness. As for heaviness according to both, al-Zayla'i objected because disagreement of scholars brings lightness according to both and it exists, for it is pure in one narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, so there is scope for ijtihad. It is answered by the weakness of the narration of purity as we mentioned, and even if some corrected it as will come, it is not considered a disagreement. The author of al-Mabsut corrected the narration of al-Karkhi, which is purity according to both, and likewise corrected in al-Daqa'iq. The first correction is more appropriate for agreement with the texts. Therefore the commentator of al-Munyah, student of Ibn al-Humam, said: correcting impurity is more evident. Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir explained it by saying that necessity does not affect more than that, for it rarely reaches the extent of being excessive, so its lightening suffices. Al-Khar' is singular of al-Khuru' like qar' and quru'. According to al-Jawhari, with damma like junud and junud, and the waw after the ra is an error. Al-Hinduwani is with damma on the ha in a reliable copy, and in the poem of al-Nasafi with kasra. This attribution is to al-Hindawan with kasra on the ha, a fort in Balkh called Bab al-Hinduwani where slave boys and girls descend. Two different rulings: abrogation of one does not necessitate abrogation of the other, as in fasting on Ashura and repeating the funeral prayer for Hamza according to al-Shafi'i, known by reflection. The author of al-Inaya rejected both aspects: he rejected the first saying it is invalid because the story's inclusion of mutilation indicates that the text is abrogated, so there is no conflict. The second he also rejected saying it is invalid because the hadith of al-Uraniyyin indicating the purity of urine of eaten meat is either abrogated or not; if the first, conflict ceases; if the second, impurity of urine of eaten meat is not established by the hadith 'Be careful to avoid urine' and the matter is contrary. Meaning: impurity is not established with certainty, rather doubt is established by conflict. His statement: (the first correction is more appropriate). Al-Nahr said: it is not hidden that it is more suitable to their statement because there is no justification for heavy with established disagreement. What is in al-Bahr that the narration of al-Karkhi is weak and even if preponderated, its prevention is apparent, for if this meaning were considered, lightness would not be established with disagreement at all, and the opponent's statement after establishing weakness in...
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the three types of light impurities (al-mukhaffafat) as categorized by the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The first is the urine of animals whose meat is eaten; it is a light impurity (mukhaffaf) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and pure (tahir) according to Muhammad al-Shaybani. The proof involves conflicting hadith: the hadith of al-Uraniyyin (which implies purity) and the hadith 'istanzihu min al-bawl' (which implies impurity). Abu Hanifa sees a conflict and therefore treats it as light impurity. The second is horse urine, which falls under the first category but due to dispute about eating horse meat, it might be thought to be from non-edible animals; however, it remains light according to both, and pure according to Muhammad. The third is the dung of birds not eaten. There is significant disagreement between al-Hinduwani and al-Karkhi on the transmitted positions. Al-Hinduwani reports it as light (mukhaffaf) according to Abu Hanifa and heavy (mghallaz) according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; al-Karkhi reports it as pure according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad and heavy according to Muhammad. The passage examines the different riwayat and concludes that the preferred view (al-mu'tamad) is that it is light, following the first correction (tas-hih al-awwal) because it aligns with the matn texts. The later discussion addresses objections and confirms that the heavy view is weak because disagreement necessitates lightness.

Key Terms
مخخف (mukhaffaf): A light impurity that requires less washing; similar to diluted urine but not fully pure.
مغلظ (mghallaz): A heavy impurity that requires more rigorous purification (e.g., washing three times).
طاهر (tahir): Ritually pure, not considered an impurity at all.
الخرء (al-khar'): Dung, specifically the droppings of birds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on the dung (khar') of a bird whose meat is not eaten?
A) It is pure (tahir).
B) It is a heavy impurity (mghallaz).
C) It is a light impurity (mukhaffaf).
D) It is impure and requires no distinction.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats the urine of edible animals and the dung of non-edible birds as light impurities (mukhaffaf) due to conflicting evidence and general necessity.
