Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Standard for Measuring Impurity: Rub' al-Thawb
Resolving the dispute over whether impurity is measured by quarter of the whole garment or the minimum for prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on measuring impurity on a garment and distinguish between the two views regarding the quarter measure.

Core Idea
The quarter of the garment worn determines if impurity is 'much'—and what is worn defines the measure.

In the Hanafi school, a garment with impurity less than a quarter of its area is excused for prayer. But what counts as 'the garment' when someone is wearing only a minimal covering? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an internal dispute: some measure the quarter from the entire garment, while others from the minimum prayer garment. Ibn al-Humam (in Fath al-Qadir) offers a reconciliation that became the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, note that the 'quarter rule' applies to impurity on a garment. The dispute: some say quarter of the whole garment, others say quarter of the minimum garment for prayer (adna ma tajuzu bihi al-salah).
The whole garment is called 'shamil' (covering the body).
2
Understand the basis of each position
The first position (quarter of the whole) sees the absolute text of the rule. The second view argues that the quarter must be relative to what is actually worn.
3
Follow Ibn al-Humam's reconciliation
He says: it depends on what the person is wearing. If wearing a full garment, its quarter applies. If wearing only the minimum, its quarter applies—because in each case that quarter is considered 'much' relative to that garment.
This reconciliation is recorded in Fath al-Qadir.
4
Apply the reconciled rule to scenarios
Practice: If a man wears a long robe, quarter of that robe is the threshold. If he wears only a waist-wrapper, quarter of that wrapper is the threshold.
The quarter is relative, not absolute.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical effect: if someone wears a small cloth, a tiny bit of impurity could exceed its quarter, invalidating prayer. Under the absolute whole-garment view, that small impurity might be excused.
The reconciled view is mufta bihi.

قوله : (لكن) ترجح الأول (الخ ) قال في النهر : وكلام المصنف يعطي اعتبار ربع كما ربع جميع الثوب قال في المبسوط وهو الأصح . ثم قال وما في الكتاب أولى لما مر ، ولا شك أن . المصاب ليس كثيراً فضلاً عن أن يكون فاحشاً ولضعف وجه هذا القول لم يعرج عليه في فتح القدير . قوله : (وفي فتح القدير ما يقتضي التوفيق الخ) قال في النهر : أقول فيه نظر بل إنما فيه تقييد حسن لمحل الخلاف وذلك أن اعتبار ربع الجميع محله ما إذا كان لابساً له، أما إذا لم يكن عليه إلا ثوب تجوز به الصلاة اعتبر ربعه اتفاقاً. ومقتضى القول الثاني أنه لو كان عليه ثوب كامل فتنجس منه أقل من الربع إلا أنه لو اعتبر بأدنى ثوب تجوز فيه الصلاة بلغ سنة ربعاً منع اهـ. أقول: وهو المتبادر في بادىء النظر من عبارة الفتح حيث ذكر ذلك على صورة التقييد والاستدراك على الإطلاق وعبارته هكذا، ويظهر أن الأول يعني اعتبار الربع أحسن لاعتبار الربع كثيراً كالكل في مسألة الثوب تنجس الأربعة وانكشاف ربع العضو من العورة بخلاف ما دونه فيهما غير أن ذلك الثوب الذي هو عليه إن كان شاملاً اعتبر ،ربعه وإن كان أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة اعتبر ربعه لأنه الكثير بالنسبة إلى الثوب المصاب اهـ. وحاصل كلام النهر أن مراد المحقق التنبيه على أن محل الخلاف هو ما إذا كان لابساً للشامل لا للأدنى بل هو محل وفاق، يخفى بعده بعد التأمل في كلام المحقق. والظاهر ما قاله في البحر وقد سبقه إليه العلامة الحلبي فقال : ووفق الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام بين هذا وبين القول الأول بأن الثوب إن كان شاملاً للبدن اعتبر ربعه وإن كان أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة اعتبر ربعه لأنه الكثير بالنسبة إلى الثوب المصاب أي لأن ربع الثوب الشامل كثير بالنسبة إليه وربع أدنى ما تجوز فيه الصلاة كثير بالنسبة إليه وإن كان قليلاً بالنسبة إلى الشامل وهذا هو المختار .اهـ.
His statement: (but) the first is preponderant... He said in al-Nahr: The author's statement gives consideration of the quarter as the quarter of the entire garment; it is said in al-Mabsut that it is the most correct. Then he said: what is in the book is more appropriate for what has passed, and there is no doubt that the affected part is not much, let alone excessive, and due to the weakness of this view, it was not relied upon in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (and in Fath al-Qadir there is what necessitates reconciliation...). He said in al-Nahr: I say there is consideration; rather, it is a good restriction for the place of dispute, namely that consideration of the quarter of the whole is when he is wearing it. But if he is only wearing a garment in which prayer is valid, its quarter is considered by agreement. The consequence of the second view is that if he had a complete garment and less than a quarter became impure, but if it were considered with the minimum garment valid for prayer, it would reach a quarter and prevent. I say: it is the immediately apparent from the wording of al-Fath where he mentioned that as a restriction and exception to the absolute. His wording is as follows: it appears that the first meaning, consideration of the quarter, is better because the quarter is considered much like the whole in the issue of the garment, the four impure areas, and exposure of a quarter of the private part, unlike less than that in both. However, that garment which he is wearing: if it is covering, its quarter is considered; if it is the minimum valid for prayer, its quarter is considered because it is much relative to the affected garment. The summary of al-Nahr's statement is that the intent of the investigator is to point out that the place of dispute is when he is wearing the covering garment, not the minimum; it is a matter of agreement. Its difficulty is hidden after reflection on the investigator's words. The apparent is what was said in al-Bahr, preceded by al-Halabi: Shaykh Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam reconciled between this and the first view by saying: if the garment covers the body, its quarter is considered; if it is the minimum valid for prayer, its quarter is considered because it is much relative to the affected garment, i.e., because the quarter of the covering garment is much relative to it, and the quarter of the minimum valid for prayer is much relative to it, even if it is little relative to the covering. This is the chosen view.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the standard for determining when impurity on a garment is considered 'much' (kathir) and thus prevents the validity of prayer. The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicated that the quarter (rub') of the garment is the measure. The dispute is whether this quarter is measured from the entire garment the person is wearing (shamil) or from the minimum garment that would suffice for prayer (adna ma tajuzu bihi al-salah). Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir reconciles the two views: if the garment covers the whole body, its quarter is the criterion; if it is the minimum prayer garment, its quarter is the criterion because in each case, that quarter is considered 'much' relative to the portion affected. This reconciliation is adopted as the relied-upon view (mukhtar). The passage clarifies that the disagreement only exists when the person is wearing a full garment; when wearing the minimum, there is consensus that the quarter is measured from that minimum.

Key Terms
ربع الثوب (rub' al-thawb): One quarter of the garment; used as the threshold for impurity that is considered 'much'.
شامل (shamil): A garment that covers the entire body (e.g., a full robe).
أدنى ما تجوز به الصلاة (adna ma tajuzu bihi al-salah): The minimum garment that makes prayer valid, covering the 'awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the reconciled view of Ibn al-Humam, what is the standard for measuring the quarter of the garment when determining if impurity is excessive?
A) Always one quarter of the entire full-sized garment.
B) One quarter of whatever garment the person is wearing, whether full or minimal.
C) The absolute size of the impurity must be larger than a dirham.
D) The quarter is measured from the minimum garment valid for prayer only.

Key Takeaway
The quarter measure for impurity is relative to the garment actually worn, not an absolute standard.

The Hanafi Dispute on Bird Dung: Narrations and Tarjih
Analysis of differing narrations regarding the impurity status of dung of non-edible birds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the different narrations regarding the impurity of dung of a non-edible bird from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and state the preferred (mufta bihi) position according to later Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
The dung of a non-edible bird is considered a heavy impurity according to the preferred Hanafi view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the impurity status of the dung of a bird whose flesh is not eaten (e.g., birds of prey). The text narrates conflicting transmissions from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and then discusses the preferred ruling (tarjih) based on agreement with established texts and principles. Understanding this dispute trains you to navigate the Hanafi school's internal ikhtilaf and identify the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of dispute
The dispute concerns the dung (خرء) of a bird whose flesh is not eaten. This is important because its impurity status affects the validity of prayer if it contaminates the body or clothing.
The rule for edible birds is different; they are considered pure or light impurity.
2
Catalog the narrations from the early imams
List what each imam (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) said according to the transmissions of al-Hinduwani and al-Karkhi. Note the three possible rulings: pure, light impurity, and heavy impurity.
Al-Hinduwani: Abu Hanifa says light, Sahibayn say heavy. Al-Karkhi: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say pure, Muhammad says heavy. Abu Yusuf has three narrations.
3
Analyze the tarjih arguments
The commentator prefers the first correction (impurity) because it aligns with the established texts (متون) and the narration of purity is weak. Fath al-Qadir argues that necessity (الضرورة) does not require more than a light impurity, but since it rarely reaches excess, lightness suffices.
General affliction (عموم البلوى) would normally cause lightness, but the preferred view is that it is heavy.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the dung is impure; if it falls into a small amount of water, it spoils it. The excusable amount depends on whether it is light or heavy. Since the preferred view is heavy, the excusable amount is less than a dirham's weight.
The practical consequence: one must avoid the dung and purify if it exceeds the threshold.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثالث خرء طير لا يؤكل وقد اختلف الإمامان الهندواني والكرخي فيما نقلاه أئمتنا فيه؛ فروى الهندواني أنه مخفف عند الإمام مغلظ عندهما، وروى الكرخي أنه طاهر عندهما مغلظ عند محمد. وقيل إن أبا يوسف مع أبي حنيفة في التخفيف أيضاً فاتفقوا على أنه مغلظ عند محمد، وأما أبو يوسف فله ثلاث روايات: الطهارة والتغليظ والتخفيف، وأما أبو حنيفة فروايتان: التخفيف والطهارة. وأما التغليظ فلم ينقل عنه وصحح قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير أنه نجس عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف حتى لو وقع في الماء القليل أفسده، وقيل لا يفسد التعذر صون الأواني عنه. الشارح وجماعة رواية الهندواني فالتخفيف عنده لعموم البلوى وهي موجبة للتخفيف، وأما التغليظ عندهما فاستشكله الشارح الزيعلي بأن اختلاف العلماء يورث التخفيف عندهما وقد وجد فإنه طاهر في رواية عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف فكان للاجتهاد فيه مساغ ا يجاب عنه بضعف رواية الطهارة كما قدمناه وإن صححها بعضهم كما سيأتي فلم يعد اختلافاً. وصحح صاحب المبسوط رواية الكرخي وهي الطهارة عندهما، وكذا صححه في الدقائق والأولى اعتماد التصحيح الأول لموافقته لما في المتون، ولهذا قال شارح المنية تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام: تصحيح النجاسة أوجه. ووجهه المحقق في فتح القدير بأن الضرورة فيه لا تؤثر أكثر من ذلك فإنه قل أن يصل إلى أن يفحش فيكفي تخفيفه ا هـ. والخرء واحد الخروء مثل قرء وقروء. وعن الجوهري بالضم كجند وجنود والواو بـعـد الـراء غلط. والهندواني بضم الهاء في نسخة معتبرة. وفي المنظومة للنسفي بكسرها. وهذه النسبة إلى الهندوان بكسر الهاء حصار ببلخ يقال له باب الهندواني ينزل فيه الغلمان والجواري التي تجلب من الهندوان فلعله ولد هناك. كذا في الحقائق. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية؛ وإن أصابه بول الشاة وبول الآدمي تجعل الخفيفة تبعاً للغليظة ا هـ .
And the third is the dung of a bird whose flesh is not eaten. The two imams al-Hinduwani and al-Karkhi differed in what they narrated from our imams regarding it: al-Hinduwani narrated that it is light (mukhaffaf) according to the Imam [Abu Hanifa] and heavy (mughallaz) according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]; al-Karkhi narrated that it is pure according to the two and heavy according to Muhammad. It is said that Abu Yusuf is with Abu Hanifa on lightness, so they agreed it is heavy according to Muhammad. As for Abu Yusuf, he has three narrations: purity, heaviness, and lightness. As for Abu Hanifa, two narrations: lightness and purity. Heaviness was not transmitted from him. Qadikhan in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghircorrected that it is impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, to the extent that if it fell into a small amount of water it would spoil it; it is said it does not spoil due to difficulty in protecting vessels from it. The commentator and a group [follow] the narration of al-Hinduwani, so it is light according to him due to general affliction which necessitates lightness. As for it being heavy according to the two, al-Zayla'i considered it problematic because disagreement of scholars causes lightness according to the two, and indeed there is purity in a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, so ijtihad has scope in it. It is answered by the weakness of the narration of purity as we mentioned, even if some corrected it as will come, so it was not considered a disagreement. The author of al-Mabsut corrected the narration of al-Karkhi, which is purity according to the two; likewise it was corrected in al-Daqa'iq. The first correction is preferred due to its agreement with the texts (mutun). For this reason, the commentator of al-Munyah, the student of Ibn al-Humam, said: correcting it as impurity is more appropriate. The researcher in Fath al-Qadir explained it: necessity does not affect more than that, for it rarely reaches excess; so its lightness suffices. 'Khur' is singular of 'khuru', like 'qur' and 'quru'. According to al-Jawhari, with dammah like 'jund' and 'junud', and the waw after the ra is a mistake. Al-Hinduwani with dammah on the ha in a reliable copy, and in al-Nasafi's versification with kasrah. This attribution is to al-Hindwan with kasrah on the ha, a fortress in Balkh called Bab al-Hinduwani, where slave boys and girls brought from al-Hindwan alight; perhaps he was born there. Thus in al-Haqa'iq. In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If a person is hit by the urine of a sheep and the urine of a human, the light impurity is made dependent on the heavy one.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal status of the dung (خرء) of a bird whose flesh is not eaten. The text begins by identifying the third type of impurity being discussed. Two early Hanafi scholars, al-Hinduwani and al-Karkhi, transmitted conflicting reports from the founding imams. According to al-Hinduwani's narration, Abu Hanifa considered it a light impurity, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) considered it heavy. According to al-Karkhi, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf considered it pure, while Muhammad considered it heavy. Further, Abu Yusuf has three different narrations: purity, heaviness, and lightness. Abu Hanifa has two: lightness and purity; heaviness is not transmitted from him. Qadikhan's correction in his Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir states it is impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, to the point that it would invalidate a small amount of water. The commentator of the text (Ibn al-Humam? actually al-Bahr al-Raiq) favors al-Hinduwani's narration, arguing that general affliction (عموم البلوى) necessitates a ruling of lightness. He counters the objection of al-Zayla'i that the existence of disagreement among jurists itself would necessitate lightness. The response is that the narration of purity is weak, so no real disagreement remains. The author of al-Mabsut (al-Sarakhsi) and the author of al-Daqa'iq corrected al-Karkhi's narration, i.e., purity. However, the preferred correction (الأولى) is the first one (impurity) because it agrees with the established texts (المتون). The commentator of al-Munyah (a student of Ibn al-Humam) explicitly says that correcting impurity is more appropriate. The researcher (Ibn al-Humam) in Fath al-Qadir explains that necessity (الضرورة) does not require more than this; the impurity rarely becomes excessive, so a light ruling suffices. The passage then provides lexicographical notes on the words 'khur' and 'al-Hinduwani'. Finally, it quotes al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah on how to combine light and heavy impurities, stating that if a person is hit by both sheep and human urine, the light is made dependent on the heavy.

Key Terms
خرء (khur'): Dung, excrement of birds
مخفف (mukhaffaf): A light impurity that requires less stringent washing and has a smaller quantity that is excused
مغلظ (mughallaz): A heavy impurity that requires more thorough purification and a smaller excusable amount
الهندواني (al-Hinduwani): A Hanafi scholar and transmitter of narrations from the early imams

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred correction (تصحيح الأول) in this passage, the dung of a non-edible bird is considered:
A) Pure
B) Light impurity
C) Heavy impurity
D) Excused in any amount

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is that the dung of a non-edible bird is a heavy impurity, based on the agreement of the established texts (mutun) and the weakness of alternative narrations.

Fish Blood: Pure and Excused
Explanation of the concession for fish blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fish blood and explain the proof based on its physical properties.

Core Idea
Fish blood is not true blood—it is pure and excused.

Among the concessions in purification is the ruling on fish blood. The commentator explains that fish blood differs fundamentally from the blood of land animals, both in appearance and nature, leading to its exceptional status in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: fish blood. The ruling is that it is pure (tahir) and excused (ma'fu 'anhu), meaning no washing is required if it gets on clothing.
This is a concession, not a general rule for all blood.
2
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The proof is based on observation: when fish blood dries, it turns white, whereas true blood turns black. Also, fish have cold blood, while warmth is a property of blood. Therefore, it is not blood in reality.
This is a rational proof ('aqli) and not a direct textual source.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Yusuf differs, holding fish blood impure. However, the commentator labels his view as weak (da'if) and the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwaya) is purity.
The strength of the proof for purity is considered overwhelming.
4
Apply the ruling
If a fish is cut and its blood splashes on clothes, no washing is necessary. The ruling applies to both small and large fish.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر) أي وعفي دم السمك وما عطف عليه. أما دم السمك فلأنه ليس بدم عن التحقيق وإنما هو دم صورة لأنه إذا يبس يبيض والدم يسود، وأيضاً الحرارة خاصية الدم والبرودة خاصيه الماء فلو كان للسمك دم لم يدم سكونه في الماء، أطلقه فشمل السمك الكبير إذا سال منه شيء فإن ظاهر الرواية طهارة دم السمك مطلقاً. أبي يوسف نجاسته مطلقاً وأنه مقدر بالكثير وعن الفاحش وعنه : نجاسة دم الكبير وما عن أبي يوسف ضعيف ذكره في المبسوط، وتقدم الكلام على أنواع الدماء وأحكامها، وأما لعاب البغل والحمار فقد قدمنا الكلام عليه في الأسار. وفي المجمع : ويلحق بالخفيفة لعاب البغل الخ) أقول في القنية: نصف النجاسة الخفيفة ونصف الغليظة يجمعان .اهـ. وفي القهستاني : تجمع النجاسة المتفرقة فتجعل الخفيفة غليظة إذا كانت نصفاً أو أقل من الغليظة كما في المنية .اهـ. أقول والظاهر أن ما في العلامة الحلبي بما لا يدركه الطرف ثم قال : والتقييد به ذكره المعلى في النوادر عن أبي يوسف قال : إذا انتضح من البول شيء يرى أثره لا بد من غسله وإن لم يغسل حتى صلى وهو بحال لو جمع كان أكثر من قدر الدرهم ظاهراً. ا هـ. وكذا نقله القهستاني عن الكرماني لكن قال بعده وفي التمرتاشي إن استبان أثره على الثوب بأن تدركه العين أو على الماء بأن ينفرج أو يتحرك فلا عبرة به وعن الشيخين أنه معتبر قوله : (لا يعتبر الجانبان) كذا
His statement: (and the blood of fish, the saliva of the mule and the donkey, and urine that splashes to the amount of needle tips) meaning that the blood of fish and what is conjoined with it are excused. As for the blood of fish, it is not actually blood but only blood in appearance, because when it dries it becomes white while blood becomes black; also heat is a property of blood and cold is a property of water, so if fish had blood it would not remain still in water. He [the author] gave it unrestrictedly, so it includes large fish if something flows from it. The apparent position of the school (zahir al-riwaya) is the purity of fish blood absolutely. Abu Yusuf [holds] its impurity absolutely, and that it is measured by muchness; and from the excessive, and from him: impurity of large fish. What is from Abu Yusuf is weak; it is mentioned in al-Mabsut. The discussion on types of blood and their rulings has preceded. As for the saliva of the mule and the donkey, we have already discussed it in the section on 'as'ar (urine?). In al-Majma': The saliva of the mule and donkey and their urine are included in the light [impurities]. It appears from Ghayat al-Bayan that it is a narration from Abu Yusuf, and that the apparent narration from him is like their statement (i.e., that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). As for urine that splashes to the amount of needle tips, it is excused due to necessity, even if it fills the garment. From Abu Yusuf, its washing is obligatory. He gave it unrestrictedly, so it includes if water touched it and increased, then it is not obligatory to wash it either; and it includes his urine and the urine of others. It is restricted to needle tips because if it were like the tips of sewing needles, it would prevent. In al-Kafi: It was said that the phrase 'needle tips' indicates that the other side of the needle is considered, but that is not the case; rather, both sides are not considered. By this, what is in al-Tabyin is refuted. He narrated his proof and refuted it, effective in lightening. It is not hidden that it is sound; how indeed, since disagreement in a non-school is considered, even if none of our imams held it at all. His statement: (In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, etc.) I say in al-Qunyah: Half of a light impurity and half of a heavy one are combined. In al-Qahastani: The scattered impurities are combined, and the light is made heavy if it is half or less of the heavy, as in al-Munyah. I say: The apparent meaning of what is in al-Zahiriyyah is when they mix and the heavy outweighs, even if it is less, as when mixed with water; while what is in al-Qunyah and al-Qahastani is when they are in two places and neither alone reaches the preventative amount; so if it reaches half the preventative amount from the heavy and half from the light, it prevents due to giving preference to the heavy; similarly if the heavy increases, contrary to when the light is more. This is what appeared to me. His statement: (In al-Majma' up to his saying: and their urine) i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. His statement: (the amount of tips of needles) restricted by al-Halabi to what the eye cannot perceive. Then he said: The restriction with this was mentioned by al-Mu'alla in al-Nawadir from Abu Yusuf: If something of urine splashes and its trace is seen, it must be washed; and if he does not wash it and prays in a state where, if collected, it would be more than a dirham in amount, he must repeat the prayer. He said: When some imam explicitly states a condition, and there is no explicit opposition from others, it must be considered, especially since the place is caution (ihtiyat). There is no hardship in avoiding such things, unlike what is not seen, like the traces of fly legs, because avoiding that entails manifest hardship. This is also transmitted by al-Qahastani from al-Kirmani, but he said after that: In al-Timurtashi, if its trace appears on the garment (the eye can see it) or on water (it divides or moves), it is not considered; and from the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?) that it is considered. His statement: (both sides are not considered), likewise.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses three items that are considered excused (معفو عنه) despite being impurities: the blood of fish, the saliva of mules and donkeys, and small splashes of urine (amounting to needle tips). The commentary begins with fish blood: it explains that fish blood is not true blood; when dried it turns white, and fish have cold blood, unlike warm-blooded animals. Therefore, the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya) is that fish blood is pure (طاهر). Abu Yusuf is reported to consider it impure, but that narration is weak. The text notes that large fish also fall under the same ruling. As for the saliva of mules and donkeys, it is considered a light impurity, following the earlier discussion in the section on 'as'ar. The commentary from al-Majma' includes their urine as well. Regarding urine splashes: if a person is splashed by urine in an amount equal to the tips of needles, it is excused even if the garment is covered with such spots. This is due to necessity (الضرورة), as it is difficult to avoid. Abu Yusuf is reported to require washing, but the relied-upon position is concession. The restriction to 'needle tips' (رؤوس الإبر) means the amount on the point of the needle, not the whole needle. The text then discusses the combination of light and heavy impurities when they are present in separate places: if the combined amount reaches the threshold of a heavy impurity, the ruling of heavy applies. This is based on al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, al-Qunyah, and al-Qahastani. The commentator (Ibn al-Humam) offers his own understanding: when light and heavy mix, the heavy is given precedence even if it is less. Finally, the text cites al-Halabi's caveat that the excused amount is only if the trace is imperceptible; if visible, washing is required. This aligns with Abu Yusuf's narration in al-Nawadir. The commentator concludes that if one imam explicitly states a condition and no other imam explicitly opposes it, it must be considered, especially out of caution.

Key Terms
دم السمك (dam al-samak): The liquid that comes out of fish when cut; considered not true blood in Hanafi fiqh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the blood of fish?
A) It is impure and must be washed
B) It is pure and excused
C) It is light impurity, excused up to a dirham
D) It is heavy impurity

Key Takeaway
Fish blood is pure in the Hanafi school because it is not true blood in reality, based on physical evidence.

Saliva of Mule and Donkey: Light Impurity
Explanation of the concession for saliva of mule/donkey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the saliva of mules and donkeys as a light impurity in the Hanafi school and apply the corresponding ruling.

Core Idea
Saliva of mules and donkeys is a light impurity, excused in small amounts.

The passage includes the saliva of mules and donkeys among the light impurities. This lesson unpacks the classification and the rationale behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item and its classification
The saliva of mules and donkeys is categorized as a light impurity (najasa khafifa). It is not heavy like the blood of land animals.
This is linked to the animals being non-eatable (ghayr ma'kul al-lahm).
2
Understand the evidence from the text
The commentator refers to previous sections (al-Asar) and cites al-Majma' which explicitly includes their saliva and urine in the light category.
The ruling is based on narration from Abu Yusuf, but it matches the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Apply the ruling
If a small amount of saliva from a mule or donkey gets on clothes, it is excused. The threshold is similar to other light impurities.
The text does not specify a precise amount; it is generally up to a quarter of the garment or similar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر) أي وعفي دم السمك وما عطف عليه. أما دم السمك فلأنه ليس بدم عن التحقيق وإنما هو دم صورة لأنه إذا يبس يبيض والدم يسود، وأيضاً الحرارة خاصية الدم والبرودة خاصيه الماء فلو كان للسمك دم لم يدم سكونه في الماء، أطلقه فشمل السمك الكبير إذا سال منه شيء فإن ظاهر الرواية طهارة دم السمك مطلقاً. أبي يوسف نجاسته مطلقاً وأنه مقدر بالكثير وعن الفاحش وعنه : نجاسة دم الكبير وما عن أبي يوسف ضعيف ذكره في المبسوط، وتقدم الكلام على أنواع الدماء وأحكامها، وأما لعاب البغل والحمار فقد قدمنا الكلام عليه في الأسار. وفي المجمع : ويلحق بالخفيفة لعاب البغل والحمار وطهراه، والظاهر من غاية البيان أنه رواية عن أبي يوسف وأن ظاهر الرواية عنه كقولهما. وأما البول المنتضح قدر رؤوس الإبر فمعفو عنه للضرورة وإن امتلأ الثوب، وعن أبي يوسف وجوب غسله. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا أصابه ماء فكثر فإنه لا يجب غلسه أيضاً، وشمل بوله وبول غيره. وقيد برؤوس الإبر لأنه لو كان مثل رؤوس المسلة منع. وفي الكافي : قيل قوله رؤوس الإبر يدل على أن الجانب الآخر من الإبر معتبر وليس كذلك بل لا يعتبر الجانبان وبه اندفع ما في التبيين. وحكى دليله ورده مؤثر في التخفيف .اهـ. ولا يخفى أنه وجيه كيف وقد اعتبر الاختلاف في مذهب الغير وإن لم يقل به أحد من أئمتنا أصلاً قوله : ( وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية الخ) أقول في القنية: نصف النجاسة الخفيفة ونصف الغليظة يجمعان .اهـ. وفي القهستاني : تجمع النجاسة المتفرقة فتجعل الخفيفة غليظة إذا كانت نصفاً أو أقل من الغليظة كما في المنية .اهـ. أقول والظاهر أن ما في الظهيرية فيما إذا اختلطا فترجح الغليظة ولو كانت أقل كما لو اختلطت بماء أو ما في القنية والقهستاني فيما إذا كان في موضعين ولم يبلغ كل منهما بانفراده القدر المانع، فإذا بلغ نصف القدر المانع من الغليظة ونصفه من الخفيفة منع ترجيحاً للغليظة، وكذا إذا زادت الغليظة بخلاف ما إذا كانت الخفيفة أكثر . هذا ما ظهر لي قوله : (وفي المجمع إلى قوله وطهراه أي أبو حنيفة ومحمد رحمهم الله قوله : (قدر رؤوس الأبر) قيده العلامة الحلبي بما لا يدركه الطرف ثم قال : والتقييد به ذكره المعلى في النوادر عن أبي يوسف قال : إذا انتضح من البول شيء يرى أثره لا بد من غسله وإن لم يغسل حتى صلى وهو بحال لو جمع كان أكثر من قدر الدرهم أعاد الصلاة . قال : وإذا صرح بعض الأئمة بقيد لم يرد عن غيره منهم تصريح بخلافه يجب أن يعتبر سيما والموضع احتياط، ولا حرج في التحرز عن مثله بخلاف ما لا يرى كما في أثر أرجل الذباب فإن في التحرز عنه حرجاً الجانبان) كذا

As for the blood of fish, it is not actually blood but only blood in appearance, because when it dries it becomes white while blood becomes black; also heat is a property of blood and cold is a property of water, so if fish had blood it would not remain still in water. Urine Splashes: Excused Up to Needle Tips
Explanation of the concession for urine splashes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi concession for urine splashes up to the size of needle tips and identify the conditions for this concession.

Core Idea
Small splashes of urine (like needle tips) are excused due to necessity.

The passage addresses a practical problem: urine splashes are difficult to avoid completely. The Hanafi school grants a concession for tiny amounts, defined as the size of needle tips. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity and the concession
The impurity is urine (bol) that splashes (muntadih) in very small amounts. The concession is that it is excused (ma'fu 'anhu) up to the amount of needle tips (ru'us al-ibar).
This applies even if the garment has many such spots, as long as each is tiny.
2
Understand the basis for the concession
The reason is necessity (darura): it is very difficult to avoid such splashes completely, especially in shared toilets or crowded places.
This is a manifestation of the principle 'al-mashaqqa tajlib al-taysir' (hardship brings ease).
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that such splashes must be washed, but the relied-upon position is the concession. The commentator cites Abu Yusuf's view as weak and mentions that the need for caution is overridden by necessity.
The text later mentions a condition from al-Halabi: the stain should be imperceptible; if visible, washing is required. This is a point of caution.
4
Apply the ruling with conditions
If the urine splash is so small that it is not easily seen (the amount on a needle tip), it is excused. If it is visible or larger, washing is necessary.
The text also discusses whether both sides of the needle are considered; the conclusion is that only the tip matters.

It appears from Ghayat al-Bayan that it is a narration from Abu Yusuf, and that the apparent narration from him is like their statement (i.e., that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). As for urine that splashes to the amount of needle tips, it is excused due to necessity, even if it fills the garment. From Abu Yusuf, its washing is obligatory. He gave it unrestrictedly, so it includes if water touched it and increased, then it is not obligatory to wash it either; and it includes his urine and the urine of others. It is restricted to needle tips because if it were like the tips of sewing needles, it would prevent. In al-Kafi: It was said that the phrase 'needle tips' indicates that the other side of the needle is considered, but that is not the case; rather, both sides are not considered. By this, what is in al-Tabyin is refuted. He narrated his proof and refuted it, effective in lightening. It is not hidden that it is sound; how indeed, since disagreement in a non-school is considered, even if none of our imams held it at all. His statement: (In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, etc.) I say in al-Qunyah: Half of a light impurity and half of a heavy one are combined. In al-Qahastani: The scattered impurities are combined, and the light is made heavy if it is half or less of the heavy, as in al-Munyah. I say: The apparent meaning of what is in al-Zahiriyyah is when they mix and the heavy outweighs, even if it is less, as when mixed with water; while what is in al-Qunyah and al-Qahastani is when they are in two places and neither alone reaches the preventative amount; so if it reaches half the preventative amount from the heavy and half from the light, it prevents due to giving preference to the heavy; similarly if the heavy increases, contrary to when the light is more. This is what appeared to me. His statement: (In al-Majma' up to his saying: and their urine) i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. His statement: (the amount of tips of needles) restricted by al-Halabi to what the eye cannot perceive. Then he said: The restriction with this was mentioned by al-Mu'alla in al-Nawadir from Abu Yusuf: If something of urine splashes and its trace is seen, it must be washed; and if he does not wash it and prays in a state where, if collected, it would be more than a dirham in amount, he must repeat the prayer. He said: When some imam explicitly states a condition, and there is no explicit opposition from others, it must be considered, especially since the place is caution (ihtiyat). There is no hardship in avoiding such things, unlike what is not seen, like the traces of fly legs, because avoiding that entails manifest hardship. This is also transmitted by al-Qahastani from al-Kirmani, but he said after that: In al-Timurtashi, if its trace appears on the garment (the eye can see it) or on water (it divides or moves), it is not considered; and from the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?) that it is considered. His statement: (both sides are not considered), likewise.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It discusses three items that are considered excused (معفو عنه) despite being impurities: the blood of fish, the saliva of mules and donkeys, and small splashes of urine (amounting to needle tips). The commentary begins with fish blood: it explains that fish blood is not true blood; when dried it turns white, and fish have cold blood, unlike warm-blooded animals. Therefore, the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya) is that fish blood is pure (طاهر). Abu Yusuf is reported to consider it impure, but that narration is weak. The text notes that large fish also fall under the same ruling. As for the saliva of mules and donkeys, it is considered a light impurity, following the earlier discussion in the section on 'as'ar. The commentary from al-Majma' includes their urine as well. Regarding urine splashes: if a person is splashed by urine in an amount equal to the tips of needles, it is excused even if the garment is covered with such spots. This is due to necessity (الضرورة), as it is difficult to avoid. Abu Yusuf is reported to require washing, but the relied-upon position is concession. The restriction to 'needle tips' (رؤوس الإبر) means the amount on the point of the needle, not the whole needle. The text then discusses the combination of light and heavy impurities when they are present in separate places: if the combined amount reaches the threshold of a heavy impurity, the ruling of heavy applies. This is based on al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah, al-Qunyah, and al-Qahastani. The commentator (Ibn al-Humam) offers his own understanding: when light and heavy mix, the heavy is given precedence even if it is less. Finally, the text cites al-Halabi's caveat that the excused amount is only if the trace is imperceptible; if visible, washing is required. This aligns with Abu Yusuf's narration in al-Nawadir. The commentator concludes that if one imam explicitly states a condition and no other imam explicitly opposes it, it must be considered, especially out of caution.

Key Terms
بول منتضح (baul muntadih): Urine that splashes in small amounts due to splattering, as opposed to pouring or flowing
رؤوس الإبر (ru'us al-ibar): The tips of needles; a measure for the maximum amount of urine splashes that is excused

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a urine splash on clothing is excused (ma'fu 'anhu) if it is:
A) Less than the size of a dirham
B) Equal to the tip of a needle
C) Visible to the naked eye
D) From a baby

Key Takeaway
Small urine splashes (needle tip size) are excused due to necessity, with the condition that they are not clearly visible.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Excused Impurities: Fish Blood and Scattered Urine
Commentary on three excused impurities with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on fish blood, mule/donkey saliva, and scattered urine, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on fish blood.

Core Idea
Fish blood is pure; scattered urine is pardoned in small amounts.

Not all impurities require washing. The Hanafi school identifies certain impurities as excused (ma'fu 'anha) due to necessity or their unique nature. In this passage, the commentator discusses three such cases: fish blood, the saliva of mules and donkeys, and urine that scatters in tiny amounts like the heads of needles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three excused impurities
List from the text: fish blood, mule/donkey saliva, scattered urine.
These are stated in the matn 'ودم السمك ولعاب البغل والحمار وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر'.
2
State the ruling for each
Fish blood: pure (tahir) according to Abu Hanifa and the apparent school. Mule/donkey saliva: considered a light impurity and ruled pure by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Scattered urine: pardoned (ma'fu) if in amount of needle heads due to necessity.
3
Analyze the dalil for fish blood
The commentator provides a qiyas argument: fish blood is not true blood because it whitens when dry and has cold property like water, unlike real blood which blackens and is hot.
This is a talil based on physical properties.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds fish blood is impure absolutely, but the text considers his opinion weak (da'if). The mufta bihi is purity.

والقهستاني فيما إذا كان في موضعين ولم يبلغ كل منهما بانفراده القدر المانع، فإذا بلغ نصف القدر المانع من الغليظة ونصفه من الخفيفة منع ترجيحاً للغليظة، وكذا إذا زادت الغليظة بخلاف ما إذا كانت الخفيفة وبتثليث مع أن القول الأول في فتح القدير الهندواني قال : وغيره من المشايخ لا يعتبر الجانبان دفعاً للحرج. وأشار إلى ما قالوا لو ألقى عذرة أو بولاً في ماء فانتضح عليه ماء من وقعها لا ينجس ما لم يظهر لون القدير : فالبول في المختصر قيد احترازي وقد قدمنا التصحيح في غسالة الميت قريباً. وقد أطلق المصنف رحمه الله العفو على الكل هذه الثلاثة طاهرة، فتعقبه الشارح الزيلعي لأن العفو يقتضي النجاسة، وقد يجاب بأن هذه ذكرت بطريق الاستطراد والتبعية ولا لبس لتصريحه في الكافي بالطهارة أو لأنه لم يقع الاتفاق على طهارتها كما قدمناه وانتضح بمعنى ترشش وفي القنية والبول الذي يصيب الثوب مثل رؤوس الإبر إذا اتصل وانبسط وزاد على قدر الدرهم ينبغي أن يكون كالدهن النجس إذا انبسط. أبوال البراغيث لا تمنع جواز الصلاة. يمشي في السوق فتبتل قدماه بماء رش به السوق فصلى لم يجزه لأن النجاسة غالبة في أسواقنا وقيل بجزئه. وعن أبي نصر الدبوسي : طين الشارع ومواطىء الكلاب فيه طاهر، وكذا الطين المسرقن وردغة طريق فيه نجاسة طاهرة إلا إذا رأى عين النجاسة . قال رحمه الله : وهو الصحيح من حيث الرواية وقريب من حيث المنصوص عن أصحابنا ا هـ . قوله : (والنجس المرئي يطهر بزوال عينه إلا ما يشق) أي يطهر محله بزوال عينه لأن تنجس المحل باعتبار العين فيزول بزوالها والمراد بالمرئي ما يكون مرئياً بعد الجفاف كالدم والعذرة، وما ليس بمرئي هو ما لا القدير قوله : ( ما لم يظهر لون النجاسة أو يعلم أنه البول) قال في مختارات النوازل: وإن كان الماء راكداً يفسده .اهـ. فما ذكره هنا مقيد بالجاري لكن ذكر في المنية اختلافاً في هذه المسألة ونقل التفصيل عن الخانية والتنجيس مطلقاً عن أبي بكر بن الفضل وعكسه عن أبي الليث واختاره شارحها. وعلله بأن الرشاش المتصاعد من صدم شيء إنما هو من أجزاء الماء لا من أجزاء الشيء الصادم فيحكم بالغالب ما لم يظهر خلافه وللقاعدة المطردة أن اليقين لا يزول بالشك. قوله : (وما ترشش إلى قوله (نجسة مبني على ما أطلقه محمد في أن غسالة الميت نجسة. قال في السراج والأصح أنه إذا لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة يصير الماء مستعملاً ولا يكون نجساً إلا أن محمداً إنما أطلق ذلك لأن بدن الميت لا يخلو عن نجاسة غالباً. الفتاوى اهـ. قوله: (وردغة) قال في القاموس : محركة وتسكن الماء والطين والوحل الشديد. قول المصنف : (يطهر بزوال عينه الخ ويطهر البدن بغسله والثوب بغسله ثلاثاً بمياه طاهرة وعصره
He said: '(And the blood of fish, and the saliva of the mule and donkey, and urine that scatters like the heads of needles)' meaning: and the blood of fish and what is coordinated with it are pardoned. As for the blood of fish, it is not really blood but only blood in appearance, because when it dries it becomes white while blood becomes black. Also, heat is a property of blood and cold is a property of water; if fish had blood it would not remain still in water. He made it general, so it includes large fish if something flows from it. The apparent of the school (zahir al-riwaya) is the absolute purity of fish blood. Abu Yusuf considers it absolutely impure and that it is measured by the large amount, and from him (another narration) of impurity of large fish blood. What is from Abu Yusuf is weak as mentioned in al-Mabsut. The discussion on types of blood and their rulings has preceded. As for the saliva of the mule and donkey, we have already discussed it in the [chapter of] asar. In al-Majma': the saliva of the mule and donkey is annexed to the light (impurity) and both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) declared it pure. The apparent from Ghayat al-Bayan is that it is a narration from Abu Yusuf and that the apparent narration from him is like their statement. As for the urine that scatters in the amount of needle heads, it is pardoned due to necessity even if the garment becomes full. From Abu Yusuf is the obligation of washing it. He made it general so it includes if water hits it and increases, then washing it is not obligatory, and it includes his urine and the urine of others. It is restricted to needle heads because if it were like the heads of awls it would prevent. In al-Kafi: it was said that his statement 'heads of needles' indicates that the other side of the needle is considered, but it is not so; rather both sides are not considered, and by this what is in al-Tabyin is refuted. He narrated his proof and refuted it, which has an effect in lightening. End. His statement: 'And in al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriya...' I say in al-Qunyah: half of the light impurity and half of the heavy impurity are combined. End. And in al-Qahistani: the scattered impurities are combined, so the light is made heavy if it is half or less of the heavy, as in al-Munya. End. I say: and apparent is that what is in al-Dhahiriya is when they mix, then the heavy prevails even if it is less, like when mixed with water. And what is in al-Qunyah and al-Qahistani is when they are in two places and neither alone reaches the preventing amount. So if the heavy reaches half the preventing amount and the light half, it prevents, giving weight to the heavy; similarly if the heavy increases, contrary to when the light is more. This is what appears to me. His statement: 'and in al-Majma' up to his statement 'and both declared it pure' means Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them. His statement: 'the amount of heads of needles' was restricted by al-Allama al-Halabi to what the eye cannot perceive. Then he said: the restriction was mentioned by al-Ma'alla in al-Nawadir from Abu Yusuf who said: if something of urine splashes that shows its trace, it must be washed, and if he did not wash and prayed while in such a state that if collected it would be more than the amount of a dirham, he must repeat the prayer. He said: when some imams explicitly mention a condition that is not contradicted by others, it must be considered, especially if the place is one of caution, and there is no hardship in avoiding it, unlike what is not seen like the traces of flies' feet, for there is obvious hardship in avoiding it. End. Al-Qahistani similarly transmitted from al-Kirmani, but he said later: in al-Timirtashi: if its trace appears on the garment so that the eye sees it, or on water so that it parts or moves, then it is not considered; and from the two shaykhs that it is considered. His statement: 'both sides are not considered' like that in al-Mari'i: it is purified by removal of its trace except what is difficult; and other than that by washing three times and wringing each time, and by threefold. While the first statement in Fath al-Qadir al-Hindwani said: others from the mashayikh do not consider both sides to remove hardship. He indicated what they said: if one throws dung or urine into water and some water splashes on him from its fall, it does not become impure unless the color of impurity appears or he knows it is urine. And what splashes on the washer from the washing water of the deceased, which he cannot avoid as long as he is treating it, does not make him impure due to general affliction, unlike the three washes if they collect in a place and then touch something, they make it impure. Like this in Fath al-Qadir: 'urine' in al-Mukhtasar is a restrictive condition, and we have presented the correction regarding the washing water of the deceased recently. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, made pardon general for all these three, which are pure. Al-Sharih al-Zayla'i objected because pardon implies impurity. It may be answered that these were mentioned by way of digression and following, and there is no confusion because of his explicit statement in al-Kafi of purity, or because there is no agreement on their impurity as we have presented. And 'intadaha' means splashed. In al-Qunyah: urine that hits the garment like heads of needles, if it connects and spreads and exceeds the amount of a dirham, it should be like impure oil when it spreads. Fleas' urine does not prevent the validity of prayer. A person walking in the market whose feet become wet with water sprayed on the market prays, it is not valid because impurity is prevalent in our markets, and it is said it is valid. From Abu Nasr al-Dabusi: the mud of the street and the stepping places of dogs are pure, likewise the mud of the gutter and the puddle of the road containing impurity are pure unless one sees the substance of impurity. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: this is correct according to transmission and close to the explicit statements of our companions. End. His statement: 'and the visible impurity is purified by the removal of its trace except what is difficult' means its place is purified by the removal of its trace because the impurity of the place is due to the substance, so it goes away by its removal. By 'visible' is meant what is visible after drying like blood and feces; by 'non-visible' is meant what is not visible after drying like urine. Like this in Ghayat al-Bayan. That which has no body. What was differentiated by in al-Dhakhira: visible is that which has a body, and non-visible is meaning... (the text is unclear). His statement: 'unless the color of impurity appears or he knows it is urine' – it was said in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: if the water is stagnant it spoils it. So what he mentioned here is restricted to running water, but in al-Munya there is a difference of opinion in this issue and detail was transmitted from al-Khaniya, and absolute impurity from Abu Bakr ibn al-Fadl, and its opposite from Abu al-Layth, and the commentator chose it. He reasoned that the spray rising from hitting something is only from parts of water, not from parts of the hitting object, so judgment is by the dominant unless the opposite appears, according to the established rule that certainty is not removed by doubt. His statement: 'and what splashes up to his statement impure' is based on what Muhammad stated that the washing water of the deceased is impure. It was said in al-Siraj: the correct is that if there is no impurity on his body, the water becomes used but is not impure, but Muhammad only stated that because the body of the deceased is not free from impurity usually. Al-Fatawa. End. His statement: 'and puddle' – in al-Qamus: it is a water and mud and severe mire. The statement of the author: 'it is purified by removal of its trace' – and the body is purified by washing it, and the garment by washing it three times with pure water and wringing.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering two main topics: (1) what impurities are excused (ma'fu 'anhu), and (2) the general principle of purification of visible and non-visible impurities. The author follows the order of the matn. On excused impurities: The blood of fish is ruled pure (tahir) by Abu Hanifa and the apparent school, because it is not real blood—it whitens when dry and has cold properties like water. Abu Yusuf considers it impure, but his opinion is weak. The saliva of mule and donkey is considered a light impurity, and there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that it is pure. Urine that splatters in amounts like the heads of needles (very small drops) is pardoned due to necessity, even if it fills the garment; if it is larger than needle heads, it is not pardoned. There is discussion about whether both sides of the needle are considered, and the preferred view is that only the drop itself is considered, not its two sides. The passage then addresses the rule of combining light and heavy impurities: if half a heavy impurity and half a light impurity are present together, they combine to prevent prayer, giving weight to the heavy. Finally, the principle of purification: a visible impurity (like blood or feces) is purified simply by removing its substance; a non-visible impurity (like dried urine) requires washing three times with wringing. Exceptions are made for unavoidable splashes like from washing the deceased or from market water due to general affliction. The commentary ends with the rule that mud from streets and stepping places of dogs is pure unless the impurity is actually seen.

Key Terms
دم السمك (dam al-samak): Blood of fish; the text rules it pure (tahir) because it is not real blood based on its physical properties.
بول منتضح (bawl muntadih): Urine that scatters or splashes; the text discusses when it is excused (ma'fu 'anhu) if it is in small amounts like heads of needles.
رؤوس الإبر (ru'us al-ibar): Heads of needles; a measure for the maximum amount of scattered urine that is pardoned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent of the school (zahir al-riwaya), what is the ruling on fish blood?
A) It is impure (najis) absolutely
B) It is pure (tahir) absolutely
C) It is impure only if from large fish
D) It is pardoned if less than a dirham

Key Takeaway
Fish blood is pure, mule/donkey saliva is a light impurity ruled pure, and scattered urine is pardoned if no larger than needle heads – necessity eases purification rules.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Purification of Visible and Non-Visible Impurities
Commentary on purification principles and combining impurities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between visible and non-visible impurities and apply the Hanafi rule for purifying each, including the combining rule for light and heavy impurities.

Core Idea
Visible impurity is purified by removal; non-visible requires washing three times with wringing.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between impurities that are visible after drying (like blood and feces) and those that are not (like dried urine). The method of purification differs accordingly. This lesson also covers the rule when light and heavy impurities are combined, and the general excuse for unavoidable contact with impurity in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Define visible impurity (najis mari'i) and non-visible impurity
Visible: has a body (jirm), seen after drying e.g., blood, feces. Non-visible: no body, e.g., dried urine.
From the text: 'ما يكون مرئياً بعد الجفاف كالدم والعذرة، وما ليس بمرئي هو ما لا يكون مرئياً بعد الجفاف كالبول'.
2
State the rule for purification
Visible impurity: purified by removal of the substance (zawal al-ayn). Non-visible: must be washed three times with wringing each time.
The text says: 'النجس المرئي يطهر بزوال عينه' and for non-visible: 'يطهر بالغسل ثلاثا والعصر'.
3
Apply the combining rule for light and heavy impurities
If half a heavy impurity and half a light impurity are present together, they combine to prevent prayer, giving weight to the heavy. If the light is more, it may not prevent.
From the fatwa: 'إذا كان نصف النجاسة الخفيفة ونصف الغليظة يجمعان'.
4
Identify exceptions due to hardship
Splashes from washing the deceased, market mud, and similar unavoidable impurities are pardoned due to general affliction.
Examples: 'ما ترشش على الغاسل من غسالة الميت... لا ينجسه لعموم البلوى'.

وللقاعدة المطردة أن اليقين لا يزول بالشك. قوله : (وما ترشش إلى قوله (نجسة مبني على ما أطلقه محمد في أن غسالة الميت نجسة. قال في السراج والأصح أنه إذا لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة يصير الماء مستعملاً ولا يكون نجساً إلا أن محمداً إنما أطلق ذلك لأن بدن الميت لا يخلو عن نجاسة غالباً. الفتاوى اهـ. قوله: (وردغة) قال في القاموس : محركة وتسكن الماء والطين والوحل الشديد. قول المصنف : (يطهر بزوال عينه الخ ويطهر البدن بغسله والثوب بغسله ثلاثاً بمياه طاهرة وعصره
He said: '(And the blood of fish, and the saliva of the mule and donkey, and urine that scatters like the heads of needles)' meaning: and the blood of fish and what is coordinated with it are pardoned. As for the blood of fish, it is not really blood but only blood in appearance, because when it dries it becomes white while blood becomes black. Also, heat is a property of blood and cold is a property of water; if fish had blood it would not remain still in water. He made it general, so it includes large fish if something flows from it. The apparent of the school (zahir al-riwaya) is the absolute purity of fish blood. Abu Yusuf considers it absolutely impure and that it is measured by the large amount, and from him (another narration) of impurity of large fish blood. What is from Abu Yusuf is weak as mentioned in al-Mabsut. The discussion on types of blood and their rulings has preceded. As for the saliva of the mule and donkey, we have already discussed it in the [chapter of] asar. In al-Majma': the saliva of the mule and donkey is annexed to the light (impurity) and both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) declared it pure. The apparent from Ghayat al-Bayan is that it is a narration from Abu Yusuf and that the apparent narration from him is like their statement. As for the urine that scatters in the amount of needle heads, it is pardoned due to necessity even if the garment becomes full. From Abu Yusuf is the obligation of washing it. He made it general so it includes if water hits it and increases, then washing it is not obligatory, and it includes his urine and the urine of others. It is restricted to needle heads because if it were like the heads of awls it would prevent. In al-Kafi: it was said that his statement 'heads of needles' indicates that the other side of the needle is considered, but it is not so; rather both sides are not considered, and by this what is in al-Tabyin is refuted. He narrated his proof and refuted it, which has an effect in lightening. End. His statement: 'And in al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriya...' I say in al-Qunyah: half of the light impurity and half of the heavy impurity are combined. End. And in al-Qahistani: the scattered impurities are combined, so the light is made heavy if it is half or less of the heavy, as in al-Munya. End. I say: and apparent is that what is in al-Dhahiriya is when they mix, then the heavy prevails even if it is less, like when mixed with water. And what is in al-Qunyah and al-Qahistani is when they are in two places and neither alone reaches the preventing amount. So if the heavy reaches half the preventing amount and the light half, it prevents, giving weight to the heavy; similarly if the heavy increases, contrary to when the light is more. This is what appears to me. His statement: 'and in al-Majma' up to his statement 'and both declared it pure' means Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them. His statement: 'the amount of heads of needles' was restricted by al-Allama al-Halabi to what the eye cannot perceive. Then he said: the restriction was mentioned by al-Ma'alla in al-Nawadir from Abu Yusuf who said: if something of urine splashes that shows its trace, it must be washed, and if he did not wash and prayed while in such a state that if collected it would be more than the amount of a dirham, he must repeat the prayer. He said: when some imams explicitly mention a condition that is not contradicted by others, it must be considered, especially if the place is one of caution, and there is no hardship in avoiding it, unlike what is not seen like the traces of flies' feet, for there is obvious hardship in avoiding it. End. Al-Qahistani similarly transmitted from al-Kirmani, but he said later: in al-Timirtashi: if its trace appears on the garment so that the eye sees it, or on water so that it parts or moves, then it is not considered; and from the two shaykhs that it is considered. His statement: 'both sides are not considered' like that in al-Mari'i: it is purified by removal of its trace except what is difficult; and other than that by washing three times and wringing each time, and by threefold. While the first statement in Fath al-Qadir al-Hindwani said: others from the mashayikh do not consider both sides to remove hardship. He indicated what they said: if one throws dung or urine into water and some water splashes on him from its fall, it does not become impure unless the color of impurity appears or he knows it is urine. And what splashes on the washer from the washing water of the deceased, which he cannot avoid as long as he is treating it, does not make him impure due to general affliction, unlike the three washes if they collect in a place and then touch something, they make it impure. Like this in Fath al-Qadir: 'urine' in al-Mukhtasar is a restrictive condition, and we have presented the correction regarding the washing water of the deceased recently. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, made pardon general for all these three, which are pure. Al-Sharih al-Zayla'i objected because pardon implies impurity. It may be answered that these were mentioned by way of digression and following, and there is no confusion because of his explicit statement in al-Kafi of purity, or because there is no agreement on their impurity as we have presented. And 'intadaha' means splashed. In al-Qunyah: urine that hits the garment like heads of needles, if it connects and spreads and exceeds the amount of a dirham, it should be like impure oil when it spreads. Fleas' urine does not prevent the validity of prayer. A person walking in the market whose feet become wet with water sprayed on the market prays, it is not valid because impurity is prevalent in our markets, and it is said it is valid. From Abu Nasr al-Dabusi: the mud of the street and the stepping places of dogs are pure, likewise the mud of the gutter and the puddle of the road containing impurity are pure unless one sees the substance of impurity. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: this is correct according to transmission and close to the explicit statements of our companions. End. His statement: 'and the visible impurity is purified by the removal of its trace except what is difficult' means its place is purified by the removal of its trace because the impurity of the place is due to the substance, so it goes away by its removal. By 'visible' is meant what is visible after drying like blood and feces; by 'non-visible' is meant what is not visible after drying like urine. Like this in Ghayat al-Bayan. That which has no body. What was differentiated by in al-Dhakhira: visible is that which has a body, and non-visible is meaning... (the text is unclear). His statement: 'unless the color of impurity appears or he knows it is urine' – it was said in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: if the water is stagnant it spoils it. So what he mentioned here is restricted to running water, but in al-Munya there is a difference of opinion in this issue and detail was transmitted from al-Khaniya, and absolute impurity from Abu Bakr ibn al-Fadl, and its opposite from Abu al-Layth, and the commentator chose it. He reasoned that the spray rising from hitting something is only from parts of water, not from parts of the hitting object, so judgment is by the dominant unless the opposite appears, according to the established rule that certainty is not removed by doubt. His statement: 'and what splashes up to his statement impure' is based on what Muhammad stated that the washing water of the deceased is impure. It was said in al-Siraj: the correct is that if there is no impurity on his body, the water becomes used but is not impure, but Muhammad only stated that because the body of the deceased is not free from impurity usually. Al-Fatawa. End. His statement: 'and puddle' – in al-Qamus: it is a water and mud and severe mire. The statement of the author: 'it is purified by removal of its trace' – and the body is purified by washing it, and the garment by washing it three times with pure water and wringing.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, covering two main topics: (1) what impurities are excused (ma'fu 'anhu), and (2) the general principle of purification of visible and non-visible impurities. The author follows the order of the matn. On excused impurities: The blood of fish is ruled pure (tahir) by Abu Hanifa and the apparent school, because it is not real blood—it whitens when dry and has cold properties like water. Abu Yusuf considers it impure, but his opinion is weak. The saliva of mule and donkey is considered a light impurity, and there is a narration from Abu Yusuf that it is pure. Urine that splatters in amounts like the heads of needles (very small drops) is pardoned due to necessity, even if it fills the garment; if it is larger than needle heads, it is not pardoned. There is discussion about whether both sides of the needle are considered, and the preferred view is that only the drop itself is considered, not its two sides. The passage then addresses the rule of combining light and heavy impurities: if half a heavy impurity and half a light impurity are present together, they combine to prevent prayer, giving weight to the heavy. Finally, the principle of purification: a visible impurity (like blood or feces) is purified simply by removing its substance; a non-visible impurity (like dried urine) requires washing three times with wringing. Exceptions are made for unavoidable splashes like from washing the deceased or from market water due to general affliction. The commentary ends with the rule that mud from streets and stepping places of dogs is pure unless the impurity is actually seen.

Key Terms
النجس المرئي (al-najis al-mari'i): Visible impurity that can be seen after drying, like blood and feces; purified by removal of its substance.
الغسل ثلاثًا والعصر (al-ghusl thalathan wa al-'asr): Washing three times with wringing each time; the method for purifying non-visible impurities.
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): General prevalence of difficulty; a legal principle that excuses certain impurities due to common unavoidable occurrence.
النجاسة الخفيفة والغليظة (al-najasah al-khafifah wa al-ghalizah): Light impurity (e.g., urine of animals whose meat is eaten) and heavy impurity (e.g., blood, feces). The combining rule affects their treatment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is a visible impurity (like blood) purified?
A) By washing three times with wringing
B) By removal of its substance
C) By simply drying it
D) It cannot be purified

Key Takeaway
Visible impurities are purified by removal; non-visible impurities require three washes with wringing; and unavoidable impurities are pardoned due to general affliction.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Purification of Visible and Invisible Impurities: Core Hanafi Ruling
Explaining the classification and purification methods of visible and invisible impurities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying visible and invisible impurities, and apply the proof that removal of substance suffices for visible impurity.

Core Idea
Visible impurity is purified by removal of its substance alone; invisible impurity requires three washes with wringing.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a fundamental distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the method of purification depends on whether the impurity is visible (having a physical substance) or invisible (like urine). The rule is practical and based on the effective cause ('illah): impurity attaches to the substance; when the substance is gone, the impurity is gone. However, for invisible impurities, as there is no substance to remove, washing with wringing ensures certainty of removal. We will walk through the ruling, its proof, and the subtle exception for hard-to-remove traces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of najasah
The passage divides impurities into visible (mar'i) like blood and stool, and invisible (ghayr mar'i) like urine. The classification is based on whether the impurity leaves a visible residue after drying.
Visible impurities have a physical body (jurm); invisible ones do not.
2
State the ruling for visible impurity
For visible impurity, purification is achieved simply by removing the substance (zawal al-'ayn). The author states: 'يطهر بزوال عينه' – it becomes purified by removal of its substance. This is the relied-upon position (mu'tamad).
This applies even if a trace of color or odor remains, as those are excused due to hardship (haraj).
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The proof is a qiyas jali (obvious analogy): 'لأن تنجس المحل باعتبار العين فيزول بزوالها' – because the impurity of the place is by virtue of the substance, so it is removed with its removal. The effective cause ('illah) is the presence of the physical impurity.
This is a straightforward reasoning: the ruling follows the cause.
4
State the ruling for invisible impurity
For invisible impurity, the place is purified by washing three times and wringing each time. The author explains that three washes are based on predominant practice (ghalabat al-zann), as three typically achieve certainty.
Wringing is wajib (obligatory) for each wash. The third wringing must be so thorough that no water drips even when squeezed forcefully.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on number of washes for visible impurity
Some Hanafi scholars (al-Khalasa) held that visible impurity also requires three washes after removal of substance, because the trace becomes like an invisible impurity. However, the author reports this view with 'qila' (it was said), indicating it is not the relied-upon position. The mufta bihi is that one wash suffices.
This ikhtilaf is resolved in favor of the more facilitative view.

بعد الجفاف كالبول، كذا في غاية البيان وهو التي لا جرم لها. ما فرق به في الذخيرة بأن المرئية هي التي لها جرم، وغير المرئية هي معنى للماء النسخ بالألف والصواب الجانبين بالياء كما هو في فتح القدير قوله : ( ما لم يظهر لون النجاسة أو يعلم أنه البول) قال في مختارات النوازل: وإن كان الماء راكداً يفسده .اهـ. فما ذكره هنا مقيد بالجاري لكن ذكر في المنية اختلافاً في هذه المسألة ونقل التفصيل عن الخانية والتنجيس مطلقاً عن أبي بكر بن الفضل وعكسه عن أبي الليث واختاره شارحها. وعلله بأن الرشاش المتصاعد من صدم شيء إنما هو من أجزاء الماء لا من أجزاء الشيء الصادم فيحكم بالغالب ما لم يظهر خلافه وللقاعدة المطردة أن اليقين لا يزول بالشك. قوله : (وما ترشش إلى قوله (نجسة مبني على ما أطلقه محمد في أن غسالة الميت نجسة. قال في السراج والأصح أنه إذا لم يكن على بدنه نجاسة يصير الماء مستعملاً ولا يكون نجساً إلا أن محمداً إنما أطلق ذلك لأن بدن الميت لا يخلو عن نجاسة غالباً. الفتاوى اهـ. قوله: (وردغة) قال في القاموس : محركة وتسكن الماء والطين والوحل الشديد. قول المصنف : (يطهر بزوال عينه الخ ويطهر البدن بغسله والثوب بغسله ثلاثاً بمياه طاهرة وعصره في كل مرة وكذا تطهيره في الإجانة والمياه الثلاثة نجسة وقيل في النجاسة المرئية يكفي زوالها بمرة. واعلم أن النجاسة المرئية على قسمين: مرئية كالعذرة، والدم وغير مرئية كالبول. فأما المرئية فطهارة محلها زوال عينها لأن تنجس المحل باعتبار العين فيزول بزوالها ولو بمرة كما جزم به في الكنز واعتمده الزيلعي، وقيل لا يطهر ما لم يغسله ثلاثاً بعد زوال العين لأنه بعد زوال العين التحق بنجاسة غير مرئية غسلت مرة .اهـ. قال في الخلاصة : إنه خلاف ظاهر الرواية وهذا هو الذي اعتمده المصنف كما تعطيه عبارته لأنه حكى ما جزم به صاحب الكنز وغيره بصيغة «قيل». وأما غير المرئية فطهارة محلها غسلها ثلاثاً والعصر كل مرة والمعتبر فيه غلبة الظن وإنما قدروه بالثلاث لأن غلبة الظن تحصل عندها غالباً. وفي شرح الدر شرط المبالغة في المرة الثالثة بحيث لو عصره بقدر طاقته لا يسيل منه الماء ولو لم يبالغ فيه صيانة للثوب لا يطهر .اهـ. ومثله في شرح المجمع ناقلا عن الخانية . وقوله : وكذا تطهيره في الإجانة يحتمل أن يكون الضمير في تطهيره راجعاً إلى الثوب، وهذا متفق عليه بين الإمامين، ويحتمل أن يعود إلى المتنجس المفهوم من السياق الشامل للبدن والثوب أو للبدن ويكون المصنف اعتمد في ذلك قول محمد والإمام معه كما في التقريب والبدائع خلافاً للإمام الثاني فإنه يشترط الصب لطهارة العضو، فلو غسل العضو في ثلاث إجانات - بكسر الهمزة وتشديد الجيم جمع إجانة أي ظروف - أو في إجانة واحدة بتجديد الماء لا يطهر عنده بخلاف الثوب الجريان العادة بغسل الثياب في الإجانات ولم يطهر لضاق على الناس والعضو ليس كذلك فيشترط فيه الصب وألحقه محمد بالثوب، فإذا غسل طهر العضو والثوب ويخرجان من الإجانة الثالثة طاهرين وما بعد ذلك طاهر وطهور في الثوب وطاهر غير طهور في العضو لعدم ملاقاة النجاسة وعدم التقرب
And the visible impurity becomes purified by removal of its substance except what is difficult. That is, its place becomes purified by removal of its substance because the impurity of the place is by virtue of the substance, so it is removed with its removal. What is meant by visible is what is visible after drying, like blood and stool. What is not visible is what is not visible after drying, like urine, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is that which has no body. The distinction made in al-Dhakhirah is that the visible is that which has a body, and the non-visible is that which has no body. ... And the non-visible impurity: its place becomes purified by washing it three times and wringing each time. What is considered is preponderance of opinion, and they estimated it as three because preponderance of opinion is usually achieved by that. And in Sharh al-Durr, it is conditioned that one must exert [wringing] in the third time such that if he were to wring it to the utmost of his strength, water would not drip from it, and if he does not exert himself, sparing the garment, it does not become purified. ... And his saying: 'And likewise its purification in a basin' — the pronoun in 'its purification' may refer to the garment, and this is agreed upon between the two Imams [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], and it may refer to the impure item understood from the context, encompassing body and garment, or just the body, and the author relied on the saying of Muhammad and the Imam [Abu Hanifa] with him, as in al-Taqrib and al-Bada'i', contrary to the second Imam [Abu Yusuf] who stipulates pouring for purification of a limb.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, elaborates the Hanafi ruling on purifying impurities. The passage type is a legal expansion (sharh) of the matn's statement. The author first explains the general rule: visible impurity (najas mar'i) is purified by removal of its substance (zawal al-'ayn) alone, without requiring a specific number of washes. This applies to impurities like blood and stool that have a physical form. The exception 'except what is difficult' refers to traces like color or odor that are hard to remove — these are excused due to hardship (haraj). Then the text contrasts invisible impurities (like urine), which require washing three times with wringing each time to achieve certainty of removal. The discussion includes several subsidiary issues: (1) water splashing from an impurity — if the color/taste changes it becomes impure, otherwise it remains pure due to the principle of certainty not being overridden by doubt; (2) wash water from a deceased (ghasalah) — considered impure by Muhammad because the deceased's body typically has impurity, but if known clean, it is merely used water (musta'mal) not impure; (3) the difference of opinion on whether a single wash suffices for visible impurity after removal of the substance — the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that one wash is sufficient, as stated by al-Zayla'i and al-Kanz, though some say three washes are needed because after removal the trace becomes like invisible impurity. The author sides with the view that one wash is enough, as indicated by his use of 'qila' (it was said) for the opposing view. For invisible impurities, the three-wash requirement is based on predominant practice (ghalabat al-zann). The text further distinguishes between washing a limb and a garment in a basin: for a garment, washing in three basins suffices due to common practice, while for a limb, pouring (sabb) is required according to Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad analogizes it to the garment, and the author follows Muhammad and Abu Hanifa. The passage is consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah positions.

Key Terms
مرئي (mar'i): Visible impurity that has a physical substance (jurm) and remains visible after drying, e.g., blood, stool.
زوال العين (zawal al-'ayn): Complete removal of the substance of the impurity from the place.
عصر (asr): Wringing the garment to extract water; required after each of three washes for invisible impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this passage, how many washes are required to purify a garment stained with blood (a visible impurity) after the blood itself has been removed?
A) One wash is sufficient.
B) Three washes with wringing each time.
C) Seven washes, one with earth.
D) Only if the stain remains, it must be washed until gone.

Key Takeaway
For visible impurity, removal of the substance suffices; for invisible impurity, three washes with wringing are required.

Washing Limbs and Garments in a Basin: Intra-Hanafi Difference
Explaining the intra-Hanafi difference on washing limbs vs garments in a basin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding washing impure limbs in a basin, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
For garments, washing in a basin suffices; for limbs, Abu Yusuf requires pouring, while Muhammad allows the basin method.

This portion of the passage addresses a practical issue: if an impure limb or garment is submerged and washed in a basin (or three basins), does it become pure? The two senior students of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differed. The author presents their views and then clarifies the relied-upon position, which follows Muhammad and Abu Hanifa. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps in applying Hanafi rulings to everyday washing scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is whether washing an impure limb (like a hand) or a garment in a container of water (إجانة) suffices for purification, or whether pouring (صب) is required for limbs.
Garments are usually washed in basins, so that is acceptable; limbs are typically washed under running water.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf (the second Imam) requires pouring for a limb. If a limb is washed in a basin (even with three changes of water), it does NOT become pure. He argues that limbs are not customarily washed in basins, while garments are.
His view is based on the custom ('urf) of washing garments in basins, but not limbs.
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani analogizes the limb to the garment: if a garment becomes pure by washing in a basin, so does a limb. Abu Hanifa agrees with Muhammad.
The author relies on Muhammad and Abu Hanifa, as indicated by 'اعتمد في ذلك قول محمد والإمام معه'.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Muhammad's view: both limbs and garments become pure by washing in three basins (or one basin with three water changes) followed by wringing. The author emphasizes that after the third basin, both the item and the water are pure (for garments, the water becomes tahir and mutahhir; for limbs, the water becomes tahir but not mutahhir because it was not used with intention).
This is the facilitative view, avoiding hardship.
