Purification from Visible and Non-Visible Impurities
Expansion on rules for purifying impurities with evidence and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for purifying visible and non-visible impurities and apply the exception for difficult traces.

Core Idea
Visible impurity: removal of substance suffices; non-visible: three washes with wringing; difficult traces excused.

This lesson clarifies the central rules for purification from impurities in the Hanafi school. The source text distinguishes between visible impurities (like blood or stool) where once the substance is gone, the object is pure, and non-visible impurities (like urine) which require three washes with wringing. We also explore the exception for traces of color or smell that are difficult to remove.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity type
Determine whether the impurity is visible (like blood) or non-visible (like urine). This classification determines the purification method.
Visible impurities are those that can be seen; non-visible are those that are not perceived by sight.
2
Apply the ruling for visible impurity
For visible impurity, simply removing the substance (e.g., wiping or scraping) suffices, even if done once. No specific number of washes is required.
This is the relied-upon view (Zahir al-Riwaya) as affirmed by the majority of Hanafi scholars.
3
Apply the ruling for non-visible impurity
For non-visible impurity, the object must be washed three times with wringing after each wash. Wringing is required to remove the impure water.
The number three is based on legal estimation to achieve predominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) of purification.
4
Check for difficult traces
If after removing the substance, color or smell remains and is difficult to remove (e.g., requires soap or boiling water), it is excused. The object is still considered pure.
Difficulty (shaqq) is determined by the need to use something other than plain water.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا زالت العين بمرة واحدة فإنه يكتفي بها وهذا هو الظاهر وفيه اختلاف المشايخ، وأفاد أنها لو لم تزل بالثلاث فإنه يزيد عليها إلى أن تزول العين. وإنما قال يطهر بزوال عينه ولم يقل بغسله ليشمل ما يطهر من غير غسل مما قدمه من طهارة الخف بالدلك والمني بالفرك والسيف بالمسح والأرض باليبس، ففي هذا كله لا يحتاج إلى الغسل بل يكفي في ذلك زوال العين من غير غسل كذا في السراج الوهاج والمراد بقوله إلا ما شق» استثناء ما شق إزالته من أثر النجاسة لا من عينها ولهذا قال في النهاية : ثم الذي وقع الاستثناء غير مذكور لفظاً لأن استثناء الأثر من العين لا يصح لأنه ليس من جنسه فكان تقديره فطهارته زوال عينه وأثره إلا أن يبقى من أثره، وحذف المستثنى منه في المثبت جائز إذا استقام المعنى كقولك قرأت إلا يوم . وفي العناية أنه استثناء العرض من العين فيكون منقطعاً اهـ. فقد أفاد صحته من غير هذا التقدير لأن الاستثناء المنقطع صحيح . أهل العربية كالمتصل، ومنهم من رجعه إلى المتصل بالتقدير ولعل صاحب النهاية مائل إليه. والمراد بالأثر اللون والريح فإن شق إزالتهما سقطت وتفسير المشقة أن يحتاج في إزالته إلى استعمال غير الماء كالصابون والأشنان أو الماء المغلي بالنار كذا في السراج. وظاهر مافي كل مرة وكذا تطهيره في الإجانة والمياه الثلاثة نجسة وقيل في النجاسة المرئية يكفي زوالها بمرة. واعلم أن النجاسة المرئية على قسمين: مرئية كالعذرة، والدم وغير مرئية كالبول. فأما المرئية فطهارة محلها زوال عينها لأن تنجس المحل باعتبار العين فيزول بزوالها ولو بمرة كما جزم به في الكنز واعتمده الزيلعي، وقيل لا يطهر ما الكنز وغيره بصيغة «قيل». وأما غير المرئية فطهارة محلها غسلها ثلاثاً والعصر كل مرة والمعتبر فيه غلبة الظن وإنما قدروه بالثلاث لأن غلبة الظن تحصل عندها غالباً. وفي شرح الدر شرط المبالغة في المرة الثالثة بحيث لو عصره بقدر طاقته لا يسيل منه الماء ولو لم يبالغ فيه صيانة للثوب لا يطهر .اهـ. ومثله في شرح المجمع ناقلا عن الخانية . وقوله : وكذا تطهيره في الإجانة يحتمل أن يكون الضمير في تطهيره» راجعاً إلى الثوب، وهذا متفق عليه بين الإمامين، ويحتمل أن يعود إلى المتنجس المفهوم من السياق الشامل للبدن والثوب أو للبدن ويكون المصنف اعتمد في ذلك قول محمد والإمام . معه كما في التقريب والبدائع خلافاً للإمام الثاني فإنه يشترط الصب لطهارة العضو، فلو غسل العضو في ثلاث إجانات - بكسر الهمزة وتشديد الجيم جمع إجانة أي ظروف - أو في إجانة واحدة بتجديد الماء لا يطهر عنده بخلاف الثوب الجريان العادة بغسل الثياب في الإجانات ولم يطهر لضاق على الناس والعضو ليس كذلك فيشترط فيه الصب وألحقه محمد بالثوب، فإذا غسل طهر العضو والثوب ويخرجان من الإجانة الثالثة طاهرين وما بعد ذلك طاهر وطهور في الثوب وطاهر غير طهور في العضو لعدم ملاقاة النجاسة وعدم التقربفي الثوب ولإقامة القربة في العضو. من شرح الغزي على زاد الفقير لابن الهمام. قوله: (وقد يشكل على الحكم المذكور (الخ أقول : الظاهر والله تعالى أعلم أن ما في التنجيس مبني على التفرقة ينعصر وبين ينعصر حيث لا يغتفر في الثاني بقاء الأثر وإن كان يشق كما سيأتي، وعليه فلا إشكال . قوله : (أفاد إن بقاء رائحتها فيه بقيام بعض أجزائها هذا يفيد أن استثناء الأثر من العين في كلام يبعده تعبير صاحب الفتح بقوله «قالوا فليتأمل. قوله: (تنجس العسل الخ) لم يذكر مقدار ما يصب عليه من الماء وظاهره عدم التقدير لكن في القهستاني ما نصه: وجدت بخط بعض الثقات من أهل الإفتاء أن المنوين كافيان لعشرة أمناء لأن في بعض الروايات قدراً من.
And he (the author) made it general, so it includes if the substance is removed in one wash, then it suffices, and this is apparent, and there is difference among the mashayikh. And it shows that if it does not go with three, he increases until the substance goes. He only said 'it becomes pure by removal of its substance' and did not say 'by washing it' to include what becomes pure without washing, such as the purification of the khuff by rubbing, and mani by scraping, and the sword by wiping, and the ground by drying. In all of this, washing is not needed, rather removal of the substance without washing suffices, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the meaning of 'except what is difficult' is an exception of what is difficult to remove from the trace of the impurity, not from its substance. Hence in al-Nihaya: the excepted thing is not mentioned verbally because excepting the trace from the substance is not valid since it is not of the same kind, so the implied meaning is: its purification is the removal of its substance and its trace except if something of its trace remains. And deletion of the excluded-from in an affirmative sentence is permissible if the meaning is sound, as in 'I read except a day'. And in al-Inaya: it is an exception of an accident from a substance, thus it is disconnected. So it shows its validity without this estimation because the disconnected exception is correct according to most Arabic grammarians like the connected. And some refer it to connected by estimation, and perhaps the author of al-Nihaya inclines to it. And the meaning of 'trace' is color and smell; if their removal is difficult, they are excused. And the interpretation of difficulty is that one needs to use something other than water, like soap and potash, or water boiled by fire, as in al-Siraj. And what is apparent is that in every time, and likewise its purification in the basin, and the three waters are impure. And it is said regarding visible impurity: its removal by one time suffices. Know that visible impurity is of two types: visible like stool and blood, and non-visible like urine. As for visible, the purification of its place is removal of its substance, because the place became impure by virtue of the substance, so it goes by its going, even in one time, as affirmed in al-Kanz and relied upon by al-Zaylai. And it is said: it does not become pure unless he washes it three times after removal of the substance, because after removal of the substance it joins the ruling of non-visible impurity. In al-Khulasa: this is against the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), and this is what the author relied upon as his expression shows, because he narrated what al-Kanz affirmed with the wording 'qil'. As for non-visible impurity, the purification of its place is washing it three times and wringing each time, and what is considered is the prevailing of opinion. They estimated it by three because the prevailing of opinion usually occurs by it. And in Sharh al-Durr, exaggeration in the third time is stipulated such that if he wrings it with all his might, water does not flow from it. If he does not exaggerate, preserving the garment, it does not become pure. Similar in Sharh al-Majma' quoting al-Khaniyya. And his saying: 'and likewise its purification in the basin' - the pronoun in 'its purification' may refer to the garment, and this is agreed upon between the two Imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and may refer to the impure thing understood from the context which includes the body and garment, or the body, and the author relied in that on the saying of Muhammad and the Imam with him as in al-Taqrib and al-Bada'i, contrary to the second Imam (Abu Yusuf) who stipulates pouring for the purification of the limb. So if one washes the limb in three basins - or in one basin by renewing water, it does not become pure according to him, unlike the garment due to the custom of washing clothes in basins, otherwise it would be difficult for people. And the limb is not like that, so pouring is stipulated for it. And Muhammad likened it to the garment; so if one washes, the limb and garment become pure, and they come out of the third basin pure, and what comes after that is pure and purifying for the garment, and pure but not purifying for the limb, due to not contacting the impurity and not having the purpose of worship for the limb. From Sharh al-Ghazzi on Zad al-Faqir of Ibn al-Humam. His saying: 'And it may be problematic for the mentioned ruling...' I say: The apparent, and Allah knows best, is that what is in al-Tanjis is based on the distinction between that which can be wrung and that which cannot be wrung, since for the second the persistence of the trace is not excused even if it is difficult, as will come. Thus there is no problem. His saying: 'He showed that the persistence of its smell in it is due to the existence of some of its parts.' This indicates that the exception of the trace from the substance in the author's words is a connected exception, so there is no need for what they burdened themselves with. Contemplate. His saying: 'And what is apparent in Fath al-Qadir...' He said in al-Nahr: The wording of al-Khaniyya indicates that what is affirmed in Fath al-Qadir is the research of Qadikhan, and that the first madhhab is the relied upon. But the expression of the author of al-Fath with 'qalu' distances it. Let it be contemplated. His saying: 'Impure honey...' He did not mention the amount of water poured on it, and apparent is no estimation. But in al-Qahstani is the text: I found in the handwriting of some reliable muftis that two manns suffice for ten ratls, because in some narrations an amount of ...
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion probe on the rules of purification from impurities (taharah min al-najasah). The author comments on the matn statement that purification from visible impurity is achieved by removal of the substance (zawal al-ayn), even with a single wash, and that non-visible impurities require three washes with wringing. 

The passage begins by discussing the general application of the rule: if the substance is removed in one wash, it suffices, and there is variance among scholars. It explains that the matn's phrasing 'becomes pure by removal of its substance' is intentional to cover cases where washing is not required, such as purification of leather socks by rubbing, seminal fluid by scraping, a sword by wiping, and ground by drying. 

Then the author addresses the exception of 'what is difficult' (illa ma shaqqa). The difficult trace refers to color and smell after removal of the substance. If removing them requires soap, potash, or hot water, they are excused. This is an exception of the trace (athar) from the substance (ayn). The author discusses grammatical points about the exception, confirming its validity whether considered disconnected or connected. 

The text continues by distinguishing visible vs. non-visible impurities. For visible (like stool, blood), the ruling is that removal of the substance suffices even once, according to the relied-upon view, though there is a contrary opinion requiring three washes. The author notes that the relied-upon view is from Zahir al-Riwaya. For non-visible (like urine), the place must be washed three times with wringing each time, based on prevalent opinion. The third wash should be squeezed thoroughly so that no water can be squeezed out further. 

There is a discussion about washing in a basin (ijanah) where the garment or limb is soaked rather than rinsed with poured water. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it suffices for both garment and limb, while Abu Yusuf stipulates pouring for the limb, though custom allows for garments. This intra-madhhab dispute is highlighted. 

The later part of the passage addresses potential objections: the ruling about persistent odor suggests parts of the impurity remain, making the exception connected, and no special interpretation is needed. Finally, a case of honey being impure and the estimation of water quantity for its purification is mentioned without final resolution. 

Overall, the passage clarifies the reliance on substance removal for visible impurities and three washes with wringing for non-visible, with careful attention to the exception of difficult traces and variant views within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
النجاسة المرئية (al-najasah al-mar'iyyah): Impurity that is visible to the eye, like stool, blood, etc.
النجاسة غير المرئية (al-najasah ghayr al-mar'iyyah): Impurity that is not visible, like urine.
العصر (al-'asr): Wringing the garment after each wash to remove the water containing impurity.
الأثر (al-athar): Residual trace of impurity, specifically color (lawn) and smell (rih) after the substance is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this lesson, what is the ruling for purifying a garment from urine (a non-visible impurity)?
A) It suffices to remove the urine by wiping or scraping.
B) It must be washed three times with wringing after each wash.
C) It must be soaked in water for a full day.
D) It becomes pure by drying in the sun.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between visible and non-visible impurities: removal of the substance suffices for visible; three washes with wringing are needed for non-visible; difficult traces are excused.

Excusing Difficult Traces and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on New Vessels
Commentary on excusing smell/color and intra-Hanafi dispute on new vessel purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on excusable traces (athar shāqq) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding new vessels that contained wine.

Core Idea
Difficult traces are excused in Hanafi fiqh, but a new vessel's absorption creates a genuine intra-madhhab dispute on whether it can ever become pure.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the principle of ‘afw (excuse) for traces of impurity that are difficult to remove. He then presents a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that a new earthenware pitcher (كوز جديد) becomes pure after three washes, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani maintains it never becomes pure because the impurity has been absorbed into the porous clay. Understanding this dispute and the broader ruling on excusable traces is essential for applying Hanafi tahārah correctly in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling on Trace Excuse
From Ghayat al-Bayan: smell is excused absolutely after the substance is removed; color is excused only if its removal is difficult. Note that this is the established position (zahir al-riwayah).
2
Examine the Wine Vessel Example and Its Nuances
From Fath al-Qadir: a vessel that contained wine – if washed three times and no smell remains, it is pure. If smell persists, only vinegar may be put in (to transform remaining wine into vinegar). An objection is raised: smell indicates some particles remain – still excused if difficult.
This shows the principle applied to a concrete case.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on New Vessels
From al-Khulasah: a new pitcher (كوز جديد) that had wine – Abu Yusuf says it becomes pure after three washes; Muhammad says it never becomes pure. The text notes that distinguishing (التفصيل) between persistence of smell or not is more cautious (أحوط). Understand the reasoning: absorption vs. surface cleaning.
4
Consider Analogous Cases (Henna, Oil, Honey)
The passage extends the rule to impure henna (color remains after washing – pure according to the madhhab), impure oil on hands (trace of oil does not harm), and impure honey/date syrup (boiling three times purifies). These all illustrate the 'difficult trace' being excused.
Notice how the same principle applies across different scenarios.
5
Conclude the Mufta Bihi Position
The author’s comment 'والتفصيل أحوط' suggests the cautious view is to differentiate based on difficulty. However, the majority of later Hanafi works (e.g., al-Kafi, al-Mujtaba) accept the excuse of difficult traces absolutely, and for new vessels, many fatwas adopt Abu Yusuf's view.
The madhhab is lenient to avoid hardship.

Source Text

غاية البيان أنه يعفى عن الرائحة بعد زوال العين مطلقاً، وأما اللون فإن شق إزالته يعفي أيضاً وإلا فلا. وفي فتح القدير : وقد يشكل على الحكم المذكور وهو أن بقاء الأثر الشاق لا يضر لما في التنجيس : حب فيه خمر غسل ثلاثاً يطهر إذا لم يبق فيه رائحة الخمر لأنه لم يبق فيه أثرها، فإن بقيت رائحتها لا يجوز أن يجعل فيه من المائعات سوى الخل لأنه بجعله فيه يطهر وإن لم يغسل لأن ما فيه من الخمر يتخلل بالخل إلا أن آخر كلامه أفاد أن بقاء رائحتها فيه بقيام بعض أجزائها، وعلى هذا قد يقال في كل ما فيه رائحة كذلك. وفي الخلاصة: الكوز إذا كان فيه خمر تطهيره أن يجعل فيه الماء ثلاث مرات كل مرة ساعة وإن كان جديداً عند يوسف يطهر، وعند محمد لا يطهر أبداً ! هـ. من غير تفصيل بين بقاء الرائحة أو لا والتفصيل أحوط . ا هـ . ما في فتح القدير. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : المرأة إذا اختضبت بحناء نجس فغسلت ذلك الموضع ثلاثاً بماء طاهر يطهر لأنها أتت بما في وسعها، وينبغي أن لا يكون طاهراً ما دام يخرج منه الماء الملون بلون الحناء ا هـ . وظاهره أن المذهب الطهارة وإن لم ينقطع اللون، وظاهر ما في فتح القدير أن ما ذكره بصيغة ينبغي هو المذهب فإنه قال : قالوا لو صبغ ثوبه أو يده بصبغ أو حناء نجسين فغسل إلى أن صفا الماء يطهر مع قيام اللون وقيل يغسل بعد ذلك ثلاثاً اهـ. وفي المجتبى غسل يديه من دهن نجس طهرت ولا يضر أثر الدهن على الأصح. تنجس العسل يلقى في قدر ويصب عليه الماء ويغلى حتى يعود إلى مقداره الأول هكذا ثلاثاً قالوا وعلى هذا الدبس ا.هـ. وأطلق الأثر الشاق فشمل ما إذا كان كثيراً فإنه معفو عنه كما في الكافي.
Ghayat al-Bayan: The smell is excused after the substance is removed absolutely. As for color, if its removal is difficult, it is also excused, otherwise no. In Fath al-Qadir: And it may be problematic on the mentioned ruling, that the persistence of a difficult trace does not harm because in al-Tanjis: a vessel containing wine, washed three times, becomes pure if no smell of wine remains, because no trace remains. If its smell remains, it is not permissible to put any liquid in it except vinegar, because by putting vinegar it becomes pure even if not washed, because the wine in it becomes vinegar by the vinegar, except that the end of his statement indicated that the persistence of its smell is due to the standing of some of its parts. And on this, it may be said about everything that has a smell similarly. In al-Khulasah: A pitcher (kuz) that had wine in it, its purification is to put water in it three times, each time for an hour. If it is new, according to Yusuf it becomes pure, but according to Muhammad it never becomes pure! Without distinction between the persistence of the smell or not, and distinguishing is more cautious. End of what is in Fath al-Qadir. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a woman dyed with impure henna and washed that spot three times with pure water, it becomes pure because she did what she could. But it should not be considered pure as long as colored water comes out. Its apparent meaning is that the madhhab is purity even if the color does not cease. And the apparent meaning of what is in Fath al-Qadir is that what he mentioned in the form of 'should' is the madhhab, for he said: They said: If he dyed his garment or hand with an impure dye or henna, then washed until the water becomes clear, it becomes pure despite the persistence of the color. And it was said: He should wash after that three times. End. In al-Mujtaba: He washed his hands from impure oil, they become pure, and the trace of the oil does not harm according to the most correct. Impure honey is thrown into a pot, water is poured over it, and it is boiled until it returns to its original amount, thus three times. They said: and similarly dibs (date syrup). End. And the absolute difficult trace includes even if it is much, for it is excused as in al-Kafi.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq discussing the ruling on excusable traces (العفو عن الأثر) after purifying from najasah. The author explains that after the actual substance (العين) of impurity is removed, the remaining smell is entirely excused. For color, if removal is difficult (شق إزالته), it is also excused; otherwise it must be removed. This is based on the principle of alleviating hardship. The commentary then quotes Fath al-Qadir discussing a vessel containing wine: after three washes, if no smell remains, it is pure; if smell remains, only vinegar may be poured into it, because the wine will transform into vinegar. A nuance is mentioned: the persistence of smell indicates some particles of wine remain, but still it is excused if difficult. Then a key intra-Hanafi dispute is brought from al-Khulasah regarding a new pitcher (كوز جديد) that contained wine: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it becomes pure after three washes; according to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, it never becomes pure (because new clay is porous and absorbs impurity). The author notes that not distinguishing between persistence of smell or not is the view of some, but differentiating is more cautious (والتفصيل أحوط). This is a genuine intra-madhhab difference. Then Fatawa Qadikhan discusses impure henna on a woman's hand: washing three times purifies, but as long as colored water comes out, it should be considered impure. The commentary infers that the relied-upon position (المذهب) is purity even if color remains, and that the phrase 'ينبغي' in Fath al-Qadir indicates it is the madhhab. The passage also covers impure oil on hands: the trace of oil does not harm. Finally, the method for purifying impure honey or date syrup (دبس) is to boil it with water three times until it returns to its original volume. The overall rule concluded is that a 'difficult trace' is excused even if it is abundant.

Key Terms
عفا ('afā): To be excused, pardoned; legally, the impurity trace is overlooked and does not prevent purity.
أثر شاق (athar shāqq): A trace (smell or color) that is difficult to remove, such that removing it causes hardship.
كوز جديد (kūz jadīd): A new earthenware pitcher that has not been used or has not absorbed liquid before.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It becomes pure according to both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
B) It becomes pure only if the smell of wine is completely gone.
C) Abu Yusuf says it becomes pure; Muhammad says it never becomes pure.
D) It never becomes pure according to all Hanafi imams.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, difficult traces are excused after proper washing, and the intra-madhhab dispute on new vessels is resolved by adopting Abu Yusuf's view with caution.

Purification of Non-Absorbent Items: Three Washes or Predominant Conjecture?
Expansion on the ruling and its intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on purifying non-absorbent items and distinguish between the apparent narration (three washes) and the mufta bihi (reliance on ghalib al-zann).

Core Idea
The mufta bihi is ghalib al-zann, not a fixed number; three washes is a guideline for the waswas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding purification of items other than the mari' (absorbent item). The apparent ruling prescribes three washes with squeezing each time, but an intra-madhhab dispute arises over whether this number is binding or whether predominant conjecture (ghalib al-zann) suffices. We will explore the proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its initial basis
The matn states: 'And other than it by washing three times and squeezing each time.' Understand that this applies to non-absorbent items. The commentator explains that repetition is needed for extraction, and since certainty is impossible, the law uses predominant conjecture.
The key term is 'ghair al-mari'' – items that are not like the esophagus, i.e., can be wrung.
2
Examine the proof from hadith
The hadith of the waking person commands three washes when suspecting impurity. By a fortiori reasoning (qiyas al-ula), confirmed impurity requires at least three. However, the purpose is removal, and removal can be achieved with fewer if conjecture is strong.
The hadith is about suspicion, not confirmed impurity; this opens the door for flexibility.
3
Analyze the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Two views among Hanafis: (1) Iraqis (Karkhi, Asbijabi) rely on ghalib al-zann without fixed number; (2) Bukharis and the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) insist on three. The text quotes al-Siraj that the first view is more apparent for non-waswas, the second for waswas.
The difference stems from whether the hadith is taken as a strict measure or as a guideline.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is to consider predominant conjecture without a fixed number, as stated in Munyat al-Musalli and chosen by Imam al-Karkhi. For the waswas, three washes are recommended to avoid doubt.
This shows the Hanafi fiqh's practicality: the rule adapts to the person's state.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a non-waswas person washes a najis cloth once and is sure it is clean, the purification is valid according to the mufta bihi. A waswas should wash three times.
Also note the squeezing dispute: the apparent narration requires squeezing each time, but some narrations suffice with one squeeze, and Abu Yusuf does not require it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وغيره بالغسل ثلاثاً وبالعصر في كل مرة أي غير المريء من النجاسة يطهر بثلاث غسلات وبالعصر في كل مرة لأن التكرار لا بد منه للاستخراج، ولا يقطع بزواله فاعتبر غالب الظن كما في أمر القبلة وإنما قدروا بالثلاث لأن غالب الظن يحصل عنده فأقيم السبب الظاهر مقامه تيسيراً، ويتأيد ذلك بحديث المستيقظ من منامه حيث شرط الغسل ثلاثاً عند توهم النجاسة فعند التحقق أولى. ولم يشترط الزيادة في المتحقق لأن الثلاث لو لم تكن لإزالة النجاسة حقيقة لم تكن رافعة للتوهم .ضرورة كذا في الهداية والكافي. وفي غاية البيان أن التقدير بالثلاث ظاهر الرواية وظاهره أنه لو غلب على ظنه زوالها بمرة أو مرتين لا يكفي. وظاهر أن ما في الهداية أولاً أنه يكفي لأنه اعتبر غلبة الظن وآخراً أنه لا بد من الزيادة على الواحدة حيث قال : لأن التكرار لا بد منه للاستخراج والمفتى به اعتبار غلبة الظن من غير تقدير بعدد كما صرح به في منية المصلي. وصرح الإمام الكرخي في مختصره بأنه لو غلب على ظنه أنها قد زالت بمرة أجزأه واختاره الإمام الاسبيجابي. وذكر في البدائع أن التقدير بالثلاث ليس بلازم بل هو مفوض إلى رأيه وفي السراج: اعتبار غلبة الظن مختار العراقيين، والتقدير بالثلاث مختار البخاريين والظاهر الأول إن لم يكن موسوساً وإن كان موسوساً فالثاني ا هـ . واشتراط العصر في كل مرة هو ظاهر الرواية لأنه هو المستخرج. كذا في الهداية. وفي غير رواية الأصول يكتفي بالعصر مرة واحدة وهو أرفق. وعن أبي يوسف : العصر ليس بشرط كذا في الكافي .
His saying: 'And other than it by washing three times and squeezing each time' means: other than the artery (mari') from the impurity becomes pure by three washes and squeezing each time, because repetition is necessary for extraction, and one cannot be certain of its removal, so predominant conjecture (ghālib al-ẓann) is considered, as in the matter of the qibla. They estimated it as three because predominant conjecture is achieved by it, so the apparent cause was placed in its position for ease. This is supported by the hadith of the one who wakes from sleep, where he made washing three times a condition when suspecting impurity, so in confirmed impurity it is more appropriate. And he did not require increase in the confirmed case because if the three were not for removing the impurity in reality, they would not remove the suspicion. Necessarily, this is in al-Hidayah and al-Kafi. In Ghayat al-Bayan, that the estimation by three is the apparent narration (zāhir al-riwāya), and its apparent meaning is that if his predominant conjecture is that it has been removed by once or twice, it is not sufficient. And it is apparent that what is in al-Hidayah first that it is sufficient because he considered predominant conjecture, and later that increase over one is necessary where he said: because repetition is necessary for extraction. And the muftā bihi is consideration of predominant conjecture without estimation by a number, as stated in Munyat al-Musalli. Imam al-Karkhi stated in his Mukhtasar that if his predominant conjecture is that it has been removed by once, it suffices him; Imam al-Asbījābī chose this. In al-Badā'i', it is mentioned that the estimation by three is not necessary but is delegated to his opinion. In al-Sirāj: Consideration of predominant conjecture is the choice of the Iraqis, and estimation by three is the choice of the Bukharis, and the first is more apparent if he is not a waswas, otherwise the second. And the condition of squeezing each time is the apparent narration because it is the extractor. Similarly in al-Hidayah. And in other than the principles (ghayr riwāyat al-usūl), one squeezing suffices, and it is more lenient. And from Abu Yusuf: Squeezing is not a condition, as in al-Kafi.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā'iq: 'And other than it (i.e., other than the mari' - the esophagus or absorbent thing) by washing three times and squeezing each time.' The commentator explains that the phrase refers to non-absorbent items (or items that can be wrung) that become pure by three washes and a squeeze each time. The reason is that najasah is absorbed, and repetition is needed for extraction. Since certainty is impossible, the Lawgiver based it on preponderant conjecture (ghālib al-ẓann), similar to determining the qibla. The number three was chosen because it typically achieves such conjecture, making it a practical standard. This is supported by the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ commanded the person who wakes from sleep to wash his hands three times when suspecting impurity, so a fortiori for certain impurity. The commentary then presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: some scholars (like those from Balkh) hold that three is the fixed number and cannot be reduced; others (the Iraqis, like Imam al-Karkhi) hold that غلبة الظن is the criterion, and if one is reasonably sure after one or two washes, that suffices. The relied-upon position (المفتى به) according to Munyat al-Musalli and others is to base it on غلبة الظن without a fixed number, especially for non-waswas persons. However, for a waswas (one prone to doubts), the fixed number of three is recommended. The passage also discusses squeezing (عصر): the apparent narration (zāhir al-riwāya) requires squeezing each time, but in some weaker narrations, one general squeeze suffices. Abu Yusuf even said squeezing is not a condition at all. The overall teaching is that purification is achieved through reasonable effort, and the law provides flexibility.

Key Terms
مريء (mari'): The esophagus or a type of absorbent item; here, the context distinguishes between something that absorbs and something that does not (or something that can be wrung).
غالب الظن (ghālib al-ẓann): Preponderant conjecture; a high probability that falls short of certainty. In purification, it is a valid basis for rule.
عصر ('aṣr): Squeezing or wringing out water from washed fabric to remove absorbed impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (المفتى به) mentioned in this passage, what is the minimum number of times a najis cloth must be washed to become pure?
A) Exactly three times, no less.
B) Once, if غلبة الظن is achieved.
C) Three times only if the cloth is absorbent.
D) Seven times, like in the case of dogs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position for purifying non-absorbent items is based on predominant conjecture (ghalib al-zann), not a fixed number of washes.

When Squeezing is Not Required in Purification
Rulings on when squeezing is required for purification in various water conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which squeezing (عصر) is not required in Hanafi taharah and apply the chosen view (المختار) for pond and pouring.

Core Idea
Squeezing is not required in flowing water; for a pond, three dips suffice; for pouring, abundant flow counts.

In previous lessons, we learned that upon washing a najis garment, squeezing is necessary to expel the najasah. However, this requirement has exceptions based on the type of water and the method of washing. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the conditions that dispense with squeezing, drawing distinctions between flowing water, standing ponds, and pouring. It also presents the intra-Hanafi differences and the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its exception
The general rule is that squeezing is required when washing in a basin. The exception is flowing water: dipping and letting water flow over the garment purifies without squeezing.
Flow of water acts as substitute for squeezing.
2
Distinguish wringable vs. non-wringable items
For items that cannot be wrung (e.g., leather, carpet), squeezing is never required, nor is drying.
Non-absorbent materials are already exempt.
3
Understand the pond (ghadīr) ruling
For a pond of standing water, the chosen view (المختار) is that dipping three times suffices; no squeezing is needed. Some earlier scholars required squeezing each time, but the more lenient view prevails.
The Balkhi scholars are the source of this leniency.
4
Apply the pouring (ṣabb) ruling
Pouring water over the najis garment three times abundantly, such that the water runs off and is replaced, purifies without squeezing. The flow is analogous to repetition and squeezing.
Abu Yusuf added: if impurity is wet, no squeeze needed; if dry, squeeze required.
5
Recognize the fatwa hierarchy
The more lenient views (Balkhis for pond, Abu Yusuf for pouring) are adopted in fatwa. The strict view of Imam Muhammad is not followed.
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Tatar Khaniyya confirm the fatwa on the lenient side.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اشتراط العصر فيما ينعصر إنما هو فيما إذا غسل الثوب في الإجانة، أما إذا غمس الثوب في ماء جار حتى جرى عليه الماء طهر، وكذا ما لا ينعصر . ولا يشترط العصر فيما لا ينعصر ولا التجفيف فيما لا ينعصر، ولا يشترط تكرار الغمس وكذا الإناء النجس إذا جعله في النهر وملأه وخرج منه طهر. ولو تنجست يده بسمن نجس فغمسها في الماء الجاري وجرى عليها طهرت ولا يضره بقاء أثر الدهن لأنه طاهر في نفسه وإنما ينجس بمجاورة النجاسة بخلاف ما إذا كان الدهن ودك ميتة فإنه يجب عليه إزالة أثره. وأما حكم الغدير فإن غمس الثوب به فإنه يطهر وإن لم ينعصر وهو المختار، وأما حكم الصب فإنه إذا صب الماء على الثوب النجس إن أكثر الصب بحيث يخرج ما أصاب الثوب من الماء وخلفه غير ثلاثاً فقد طهر لأن الجريان بمنزلة التكرار والعصر والمعتبر غلبة الظن هو الصحيح، وعن أبي يوسف إن كانت النجاسة رطبة لا يشترط العصر، وإن كانت يابسة فلا بد منه وهذا هو المختار، كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي التبيين : والمعتبر ظن الغاسل إلا أن يكون الغاسل صغيراً أو مجنوناً فيعتبر ظن المستعمل لأنه الماء وهذا كله عند الشيخين وأما عنده فلا يطهر أبداً .اهـ. قوله : (والظاهر الأول إن لم يكن موسوساً الخ) قال في النهر : وهو توفيق حسن قوله : (وهو أرفق) في قال التتارخانية، وفي النوازل: وعليه الفتوى. قوله: (وأما حكم الغدير الخ) عبارة السراج: وأما حكم الغدير فإن غمس الثوب فيه ثلاثاً وقلنا بقول البلخيين وهو المختار فقد روي عن أبي حفص الكبير أنه يطهر وإن لم يعصر. وقال بعضهم : يشترط العصر في كل مرة. وعن أبي نصر : الصفار يكفيه العصر مرة واحدة اهـ فأفاد أنه عند البلخيين يغمس ثلاثاً وأن قولهم هو المختار لكنهم اختلفوا فيما بينهم في العصر على ثلاثة
Then the condition of squeezing for items that can be wrung is only when washing in a basin. As for when he dips the garment in flowing water until it runs over it, it becomes pure. Similarly for what cannot be wrung. Squeezing is not required for what cannot be wrung, nor drying for what cannot be wrung, nor is repetition of dipping required. Similarly a najis vessel if placed in a river, filled and emptied, it becomes pure. If his hand becomes impure with impure ghee, and he dips it in flowing water and it flows over it, it becomes pure, and the trace of the ghee does not harm because it is pure in itself, only impure by contact with najasah, unlike if the ghee is fat of a carcass, then removal of its trace is obligatory. As for the ruling of a pond (ghadīr): if he dips the garment in it, it becomes pure even if he does not squeeze, and this is the chosen view. As for the ruling of pouring (ṣabb): if he pours water on the najis garment, if he pours abundantly such that the water that hit the garment emerges and changes (or goes away) three times, it becomes purified because the flowing is like repetition and squeezing, and consideration of predominant conjecture is correct. From Abu Yusuf: if the impurity is wet, squeezing is not required; if dry, it is necessary, and this is the chosen view; similarly in al-Sirāj al-Wahhāj. In al-Tabyīn: what is considered is the opinion of the washer, unless the washer is a child or insane, then consider the opinion of the user because he is the water. All this according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), but according to him (Muhammad al-Shaybani?), it never becomes pure. End. His saying: (And the first is more apparent if not a waswas) – al-Nahr said: that is a good reconciliation. His saying: (it is more lenient) – al-Tatar Khaniyya and al-Nawāzil: upon it is the fatwa. His saying: (As for the ruling of the pond) – the wording of al-Sirāj: As for the ruling of the pond, if he dips the garment in it three times and we say according to the opinion of the Balkhis, which is the chosen view, it is narrated from Abu Hafs al-Kabir that it becomes pure even if he does not squeeze. Some say squeezing is required each time. From Abu Nasr al-Saffār: one squeezing suffices. End. So he indicates that according to the Balkhis, he dips three times, and their view is the chosen one, but they differed among themselves on squeezing in three ways.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the ruling of squeezing (عصر). It explains that the requirement of squeezing each time only applies when washing in a basin (إجانة), not in flowing water. If one immerses a garment in a river or canal and water flows over it, it purifies without squeezing. Similarly, items that cannot be wrung (non-absorbent) do not require squeezing or drying. Even a vessel placed in a river and filled and emptied becomes pure. For hands soiled with impure ghee, dipping in flowing water suffices, and the remaining trace of ghee is not harmful because ghee is pure in itself; only the contact made it najis. But if the fat is from a carcass (غير مذكى), then the trace must be removed because the fat itself is impure. The ruling for standing water (غدير - pond): the chosen view (المختار) of the Balkhi scholars is that dipping three times suffices without squeezing. For pouring water over the garment (صب), if one pours abundantly until the water that touched the garment runs off and is replaced three times, it purifies because the flow acts like repetition and squeezing. The overriding criterion is still غلبة الظن. Abu Yusuf distinguished: if the impurity is wet (rāṭiba), squeezing is not needed; if dry (yābisa), it is required. This is the chosen view. Al-Tabyīn adds that the opinion of the washer is considered, except if the washer is a child or insane, then the opinion of the user (the one who will use the garment) is considered; this is the view of the two shaykhs (Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf), but according to Imām Muḥammad, it never purifies (a very strict view). The passage concludes by quoting al-Sirāj: the Balkhi view is the chosen one, and they themselves differed on squeezing: some say no squeeze; others say squeeze each time; one view says one squeeze suffices. The author notes that this reconciliation is good and that the fatwa is on the more lenient view.

Key Terms
ماء جار (mā' jārin): Flowing water, such as a river or tap, where water moves continuously.
غدير (ghadīr): A pond or pool of standing water, not flowing.
صب (ṣabb): Pouring water over an object; a method of purification by letting water run over the impurity.
عصر (ʿaṣr): Squeezing or wringing a garment to expel water containing impurity; a required act in certain washing methods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (المختار) in this passage, what is required to purify a garment by dipping it in a pond (غدير)?
A) Dip it once and squeeze thoroughly.
B) Dip it three times without squeezing.
C) Dip it three times and squeeze after each dip.
D) Dip it seven times.

Key Takeaway
Squeezing is not an absolute requirement; its necessity depends on the type of water and method of washing, with more lenient views preferred for fatwa.

Number of Washes and Wringing for Impure Garments
Explains the ruling on number of washes and wringing, with internal Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of washes required to purify an impure garment and explain the difference between the Zahir al-Riwaya and the mufta bihi view, including the role of wringing.

Core Idea
Washing three times is not an absolute requirement; the mufta bihi view relies on strong probability of purity.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a key question in purification: how many times must an impure garment be washed, and must it be wrung each time? While the Zahir al-Riwaya (core transmitted ruling) specifies three washes with wringing each time, later Hanafi scholars adopted a more practical approach based on strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) and dispensation in wringing. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is washing an impure garment. According to the passage, the basic ruling is that three washes are required when impurity is suspected, and even more so when certain. But the fatwa relies on strong probability, not a fixed number.
Three washes are a means, not an end.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the Iraqis (e.g., Imam al-Karkhi) favor considering strong probability without a fixed number; the Bukharans (e.g., later scholars) insist on three washes. The passage also notes a dispute about wringing: Zahir al-Riwaya requires wringing each time, but a more lenient view allows one wringing at the end, and Abu Yusuf said wringing is not a condition.
The 'Iraqis' and 'Bukharans' refer to schools of Hanafi scholarship.
3
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon fatwa is that strong probability of purity suffices, and wringing once is sufficient for convenience. However, for an obsessive person (muswas), the three-wash rule is recommended to cut off doubt.
See Munyat al-Musalli and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
If a non-obsessive person washes a garment once and is strongly convinced the impurity is gone, the garment is pure. If he is obsessive, he must wash three times regardless of his conviction.
This accommodates people's circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلاثاً عند توهم النجاسة فعند التحقق أولى. ولم يشترط الزيادة في المتحقق لأن الثلاث لو لم تكن لإزالة النجاسة حقيقة لم تكن رافعة للتوهم ضرورة كذا في الهداية والكافي. وفي غاية البيان أن التقدير بالثلاث ظاهر الرواية وظاهره أنه لو غلب على ظنه زوالها بمرة أو مرتين لا يكفي. وظاهر أن ما في الهداية أولاً أنه يكفي لأنه اعتبر غلبة الظن وآخراً أنه لا بد من الزيادة على الواحدة حيث قال: لأن التكرار لا بد منه للاستخراج والمفتى به اعتبار غلبة الظن من غير تقدير بعدد كما صرح به في منية المصلي. وصرح الإمام الكرخي في مختصره بأنه لو غلب على ظنه أنها قد زالت بمرة أجزأه واختاره الإمام الاسبيجابي. وذكر في البدائع أن التقدير بالثلاث ليس بلازم بل هو مفوض إلى رأيه وفي السراج: اعتبار غلبة الظن مختار العراقيين، والتقدير بالثلاث مختار البخاريين والظاهر الأول إن لم يكن موسوساً وإن كان موسوساً فالثاني. واشتراط العصر في كل مرة هو ظاهر الرواية لأنه هو المستخرج. كذا في الهداية. وفي غير رواية الأصول يكتفي بالعصر مرة واحدة وهو أرفق. وعن أبي يوسف: العصر ليس بشرط كذا في الكافي. ثم اشتراط العصر فيما ينعصر إنما هو فيما إذا غسل الثوب في الإجانة، أما إذا غمس الثوب في ماء جار حتى جرى عليه الماء طهر، وكذا ما لا ينعصر. ولا يشترط العصر فيما لا ينعصر ولا التجفيف فيما لا ينعصر، ولا يشترط تكرار الغمس وكذا الإناء النجس إذا جعله في النهر وملأه وخرج منه طهر. ولو تنجست يده بسمن نجس فغمسها في الماء الجاري وجرى عليها طهرت ولا يضره بقاء أثر الدهن لأنه طاهر في نفسه وإنما ينجس بمجاورة النجاسة بخلاف ما إذا كان الدهن ودك ميتة فإنه يجب عليه إزالة أثره. وأما حكم الغدير فإن غمس الثوب به فإنه يطهر وإن لم ينعصر وهو المختار، وأما حكم الصب فإنه إذا صب الماء على الثوب النجس إن أكثر الصب بحيث يخرج ما أصاب الثوب من الماء وخلفه غير ثلاثاً فقد طهر لأن الجريان بمنزلة التكرار والعصر والمعتبر غلبة الظن هو الصحيح، وعن أبي يوسف إن كانت النجاسة رطبة لا يشترط العصر، وإن كانت يابسة فلا بد منه وهذا هو المختار، كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي التبيين: والمعتبر ظن الغاسل إلا أن يكون الغاسل صغيراً أو مجنوناً فيعتبر ظن المستعمل لأنه الماء وهذا كله عند الشيخين وأما عنده فلا يطهر أبداً.
Three times when impurity is suspected; when it is certain, it is even more appropriate. Increase was not stipulated for the certain case because if three times do not actually remove the impurity, they would not remove the doubt out of necessity. Thus in al-Hidaya and al-Kafi. In Ghayat al-Bayan: Limiting to three is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), and its apparent meaning is that if he is strongly convinced of its removal with one or two times, it is not sufficient. And it is apparent that what is in al-Hidaya first is that it is sufficient because it considered strong probability, but later that increase over one is necessary, where he said: 'Repetition is necessary for extraction.' The fatwa is on considering strong probability without a fixed number, as stated in Munyat al-Musalli. Imam al-Karkhi stated in his Mukhtasar that if he is strongly convinced it has been removed with one time, it suffices him, and Imam al-Isbijabi chose it. In al-Bada'i: Limiting to three is not necessary; rather it is left to his opinion. In al-Siraj: Considering strong probability is the choice of the Iraqis, and limiting to three is the choice of the Bukharans; the first is apparent if he is not obsessive, but if he is obsessive, then the second. The condition of wringing each time is the apparent narration because it is the extractor. Thus in al-Hidaya. In non-principle transmissions, wringing once suffices, and it is more convenient. From Abu Yusuf: Wringing is not a condition, thus in al-Kafi. Then the condition of wringing for items that can be wrung is only when washing the garment in a basin; if he immerses the garment in flowing water until water runs over it, it becomes pure, similarly for what cannot be wrung. Wringing is not required for what cannot be wrung, nor drying, nor repetition of immersion. Likewise, if an impure vessel is placed in a river and filled and emptied, it becomes pure. If his hand is contaminated with impure ghee and he immerses it in flowing water and water runs over it, it becomes pure, and the residue of grease does not harm because it is pure in itself and becomes impure only by contact with impurity, unlike if the grease is from the fat of a carcass, then removal of its trace is obligatory. As for the ruling of a pond: if he immerses the garment in it, it becomes pure even if not wrung, and that is the chosen view. As for the ruling of pouring: if he pours water on the impure garment, if he pours abundantly such that the water that touched the garment exits and is replaced by other water three times, it becomes pure, because flowing is like repetition and wringing, and the considered factor is strong probability, which is the correct view. From Abu Yusuf: If the impurity is wet, wringing is not required; if dry, then it is necessary, and this is the chosen view, thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Tabyin: The considered factor is the washer's presumption, unless the washer is a child or insane, then the presumption of the user (of the water) is considered, because it is water. All this according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), but according to him (Muhammad), it never becomes pure.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the purification of impure garments. The author opens by stating the ruling: washing three times is required when impurity is only suspected (tawahhum), and even more so when it is certain. He then explains an apparent contradiction: earlier in al-Hidaya it was said that strong probability of purity suffices, but later it says increase over one is necessary. The fatwa adopted is that strong probability is considered without a fixed number, as per the Iraqis. However, for an obsessive person (muswas, one prone to waswasa), limiting to three is recommended to cut off doubt. The condition of wringing (asr) each time is the Zahir al-Riwaya (core transmitted ruling), but there is a more lenient view that one wringing after the last wash suffices, and Abu Yusuf had a view that wringing is not a condition at all. The author then explains exceptions: for flowing water (like a river), wringing is not needed; immersion suffices. Similarly, for a pond (ghadir), the chosen view (mukhtar) is that it purifies without wringing. For pouring (sabb) a large quantity of water on the garment, three pours with the water being replaced each time suffices, as the flow acts like wringing. The passage also covers the case of a hand contaminated with impure ghee, and the need to remove the trace of impure fat (like dead meat fat) but not pure fat. Finally, the author notes that according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the washer's presumption of purity is considered, whereas according to Imam Muhammad, the garment never becomes pure unless certain conditions are met. This passage shows the Hanafi methodology of balancing rigorous textual rulings (Zahir al-Riwaya) with practical concessions (rukhsa) based on custom and necessity.

Key Terms
عصر (asr): Wringing or squeezing the garment after each wash to extract impure water.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Strong probability or overwhelming presumption that impurity has been removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is required for purifying a garment after removing visible impurity?
A) Washing three times with wringing each time.
B) Achieving strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) that the impurity is removed, regardless of number of washes.
C) Washing three times without wringing.
D) Wringing once after the last wash only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi view for purifying impure garments is to rely on strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) without a fixed number of washes, with wringing once sufficient for convenience.

Purification Methods: Flowing Water, Ponds, and Pouring
Explains the exceptions to wringing for different water sources and methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the specific conditions under which wringing is not required and apply the rulings for purification in flowing water, a pond, and by pouring water.

Core Idea
Wringing is not needed when water flows over the item; immersion in a pond suffices without wringing.

The previous lesson focused on washing in a basin. This lesson covers the practical exceptions: when the garment is washed in flowing water, a pond, or by pouring water, the rules change. The passage also discusses the case of an impure hand with ghee and the difference between pure and impure fatty residues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the alternative methods
The passage lists three alternatives to basin washing: immersion in flowing water, immersion in a pond (ghadir), and pouring water over the garment (sabb). Each has its own conditions.
Note that a pond (ghadir) is still water, but the chosen view purifies without wringing.
2
Determine the ruling for each method
For flowing water: immersing the garment until water runs over it suffices without wringing. For a pond: the chosen view is that immersion purifies even without wringing. For pouring: three pours with replacement of water suffice, as the flow acts like wringing.
For pouring, the water must be replaced three times; this mimics the three washes.
3
Apply the principle of strong probability
In all methods, the criterion is strong probability (ghalabat al-zann). The pouring method explicitly states that strong probability is the correct view.
This unifies the ruling across methods.
4
Address the hand and ghee case
If the hand is contaminated with impure ghee, immersing it in flowing water suffices, and the residue of pure grease does not prevent purification. However, if the fat is from a carcass (impure itself), the trace must be removed.
This distinguishes between externally impure substances and inherently pure but contaminated ones.
5
Note the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf differentiates between wet and dry impurity for wringing. Imam Muhammad holds a stricter view that the garment never becomes pure (according to the two Shaykhs' view it can).
Remember: the mufta bihi is the view of the two Shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثلاثاً عند توهم النجاسة فعند التحقق أولى. ولم يشترط الزيادة في المتحقق لأن الثلاث لو لم تكن لإزالة النجاسة حقيقة لم تكن رافعة للتوهم ضرورة كذا في الهداية والكافي. وفي غاية البيان أن التقدير بالثلاث ظاهر الرواية وظاهره أنه لو غلب على ظنه زوالها بمرة أو مرتين لا يكفي. وظاهر أن ما في الهداية أولاً أنه يكفي لأنه اعتبر غلبة الظن وآخراً أنه لا بد من الزيادة على الواحدة حيث قال: لأن التكرار لا بد منه للاستخراج والمفتى به اعتبار غلبة الظن من غير تقدير بعدد كما صرح به في منية المصلي. وصرح الإمام الكرخي في مختصره بأنه لو غلب على ظنه أنها قد زالت بمرة أجزأه واختاره الإمام الاسبيجابي. وذكر في البدائع أن التقدير بالثلاث ليس بلازم بل هو مفوض إلى رأيه وفي السراج: اعتبار غلبة الظن مختار العراقيين، والتقدير بالثلاث مختار البخاريين والظاهر الأول إن لم يكن موسوساً وإن كان موسوساً فالثاني. واشتراط العصر في كل مرة هو ظاهر الرواية لأنه هو المستخرج. كذا في الهداية. وفي غير رواية الأصول يكتفي بالعصر مرة واحدة وهو أرفق. وعن أبي يوسف: العصر ليس بشرط كذا في الكافي. ثم اشتراط العصر فيما ينعصر إنما هو فيما إذا غسل الثوب في الإجانة، أما إذا غمس الثوب في ماء جار حتى جرى عليه الماء طهر، وكذا ما لا ينعصر. ولا يشترط العصر فيما لا ينعصر ولا التجفيف فيما لا ينعصر، ولا يشترط تكرار الغمس وكذا الإناء النجس إذا جعله في النهر وملأه وخرج منه طهر. ولو تنجست يده بسمن نجس فغمسها في الماء الجاري وجرى عليها طهرت ولا يضره بقاء أثر الدهن لأنه طاهر في نفسه وإنما ينجس بمجاورة النجاسة بخلاف ما إذا كان الدهن ودك ميتة فإنه يجب عليه إزالة أثره. وأما حكم الغدير فإن غمس الثوب به فإنه يطهر وإن لم ينعصر وهو المختار، وأما حكم الصب فإنه إذا صب الماء على الثوب النجس إن أكثر الصب بحيث يخرج ما أصاب الثوب من الماء وخلفه غير ثلاثاً فقد طهر لأن الجريان بمنزلة التكرار والعصر والمعتبر غلبة الظن هو الصحيح، وعن أبي يوسف إن كانت النجاسة رطبة لا يشترط العصر، وإن كانت يابسة فلا بد منه وهذا هو المختار، كذا في السراج الوهاج. وفي التبيين: والمعتبر ظن الغاسل إلا أن يكون الغاسل صغيراً أو مجنوناً فيعتبر ظن المستعمل لأنه الماء وهذا كله عند الشيخين وأما عنده فلا يطهر أبداً.
Three times when impurity is suspected; when it is certain, it is even more appropriate. Increase was not stipulated for the certain case because if three times do not actually remove the impurity, they would not remove the doubt out of necessity. Thus in al-Hidaya and al-Kafi. In Ghayat al-Bayan: Limiting to three is the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwaya), and its apparent meaning is that if he is strongly convinced of its removal with one or two times, it is not sufficient. And it is apparent that what is in al-Hidaya first is that it is sufficient because it considered strong probability, but later that increase over one is necessary, where he said: 'Repetition is necessary for extraction.' The fatwa is on considering strong probability without a fixed number, as stated in Munyat al-Musalli. Imam al-Karkhi stated in his Mukhtasar that if he is strongly convinced it has been removed with one time, it suffices him, and Imam al-Isbijabi chose it. In al-Bada'i: Limiting to three is not necessary; rather it is left to his opinion. In al-Siraj: Considering strong probability is the choice of the Iraqis, and limiting to three is the choice of the Bukharans; the first is apparent if he is not obsessive, but if he is obsessive, then the second. The condition of wringing each time is the apparent narration because it is the extractor. Thus in al-Hidaya. In non-principle transmissions, wringing once suffices, and it is more convenient. From Abu Yusuf: Wringing is not a condition, thus in al-Kafi. Then the condition of wringing for items that can be wrung is only when washing the garment in a basin; if he immerses the garment in flowing water until water runs over it, it becomes pure, similarly for what cannot be wrung. Wringing is not required for what cannot be wrung, nor drying, nor repetition of immersion. Likewise, if an impure vessel is placed in a river and filled and emptied, it becomes pure. If his hand is contaminated with impure ghee and he immerses it in flowing water and water runs over it, it becomes pure, and the residue of grease does not harm because it is pure in itself and becomes impure only by contact with impurity, unlike if the grease is from the fat of a carcass, then removal of its trace is obligatory. As for the ruling of a pond: if he immerses the garment in it, it becomes pure even if not wrung, and that is the chosen view. As for the ruling of pouring: if he pours water on the impure garment, if he pours abundantly such that the water that touched the garment exits and is replaced by other water three times, it becomes pure, because flowing is like repetition and wringing, and the considered factor is strong probability, which is the correct view. From Abu Yusuf: If the impurity is wet, wringing is not required; if dry, then it is necessary, and this is the chosen view, thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. In al-Tabyin: The considered factor is the washer's presumption, unless the washer is a child or insane, then the presumption of the user (of the water) is considered, because it is water. All this according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), but according to him (Muhammad), it never becomes pure.

غدير (ghadir): A pond or still body of water. In this context, immersion purifies without wringing according to the chosen view (mukhtar).
صبّ (sabb): Pouring water over the garment. The method requires three pours with fresh water, acting like wringing.

The Obsessive Person and Strong Probability in Tahara
Commentary on the obsessive person exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling for the muswas from the non-obsessive and apply the strong probability criterion.

Core Idea
For the non-obsessive, strong probability suffices; for the obsessive, three washes are wajib to cut off doubt.

In this passage, the commentator reconciles earlier rulings by clarifying that the requirement of three washes only applies to the muswas. For the average person, strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) is sufficient. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi tahara to prevent hardship while maintaining purity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Recognize that the text distinguishes between a person who is obsessive (muswas) and one who is not. The ruling for each is different.
The muswas is someone who has excessive doubts about purity.
2
Understand the baseline ruling
The first apparent ruling (from Zahir al-Riwayah) required three washes and wringing for everyone. The commentator refines this by linking it to the non-obsessive.
The phrase 'the first is apparent if he is not obsessive' indicates the refinement.
3
Apply the fatwa
The fatwa (mufta bihi) is that for the non-obsessive, strong probability that the impurity is removed suffices. For the obsessive, the strict three washes are wajib to prevent doubt.
This is based on al-Nawazil and affirmed by al-Nahr.
4
Recognize the legal consequence
In practice, a non-obsessive person can stop washing when he is fairly sure the impurity is gone, even if only once or twice. The obsessive must wash three times, wringing each time.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school among other madhahib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والظاهر الأول إن لم يكن موسوساً الخ) قال في النهر: وهو توفيق حسن قوله : (وهو أرفق) في قال التتارخانية، وفي النوازل: وعليه الفتوى. قوله: (وأما حكم الغدير الخ) عبارة السراج: وأما حكم الغدير فإن غمس الثوب فيه ثلاثاً وقلنا بقول البلخيين وهو المختار فقد روي عن أبي حفص الكبير أنه يطهر وإن لم يعصر. وقال بعضهم: يشترط العصر في كل مرة. وعن أبي نصر: الصفار يكفيه العصر مرة واحدة اهـ فأفاد أنه عند البلخيين يغمس ثلاثاً وأن قولهم هو المختار لكنهم اختلفوا فيما بينهم في العصر على ثلاثة أقوال: لا يشترط أصلاً، يشترط في كل مرة يشترط في مرة واحدة قوله : (وتعتبر قوة كل عاصر الخ) قال في فتح القدير: حتى إذا انقطع تقاطره بعصره ثم قطر يعصر رجل آخر أقوى منه يحكم بطهارته .اهـ. أي يحكم بطهارته بالنسبة إلى صاحبه ولا يظهر بالنسبة إلى الشخص الأقوى كما ذكره البرهان الحلبي. قال: لأن كل أحد مكلف بقدرته ووسعه ولا يكلف أحد أن يطلب من هو أقوى منه ليعصر ثوبه عند غسله قوله : (ولا يخفى الخ) أقره على هذا البحث أخوه في النهر وكذلك الشيخ إسمعيل في شرح الدرر قوله : ( والخزف والآجر والخشب الجديد أقول: لم يذكر هذه الثلاثة صاحب الفتح في هذا القسم بل ذكر الطرفين في القسم الأول الآتي مقيدين بكونهما جديدين كما
His statement: (And the first is apparent if he is not obsessive etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is a good reconciliation. His statement: (And it is more convenient) has a statement in al-Tatarkhaniyya, and in al-Nawazil: The fatwa is upon it. His statement: (As for the ruling of the pond etc.) The expression of al-Siraj: As for the ruling of the pond, if he immerses the garment in it three times and we say with the Balkhians' view, which is the chosen, it has been related from Abu Hafs al-Kabir that it becomes pure even if not wrung. And some said: Wringing is required each time. From Abu Nasr: al-Saffar, one wringing suffices. So it informs that according to the Balkhians, he immerses three times, and that their view is the chosen, but they differed among themselves regarding wringing into three opinions: not required at all, required each time, required once. His statement: (And the strength of each wringer is considered etc.) He said in Fath al-Qadeer: So if its dripping stops by his wringing, then a stronger man wrings it and it drips, it is ruled pure. That is, it is ruled pure with respect to its owner, but not with respect to the stronger person, as stated by Burhan al-Halabi. He said: Because each person is obligated according to his ability and capacity, and no one is required to seek someone stronger to wring his garment when washing it. His statement: (And it is not hidden etc.) His brother in al-Nahr affirmed this research, as did Shaykh Isma'il in Sharh al-Durar. His statement: (And the pottery, brick, and new wood) I say: The author of al-Fath did not mention these three in this section; rather, he mentioned the two sides in the previous section, qualified as being new.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya-style) of the earlier ruling. It starts with a comment on the phrase 'the first is apparent if he is not obsessive.' The author of Bahr al-Ra'iq quotes from al-Nahr that this is a good reconciliation between the Iraqis and Bukharans. The fatwa is on the view that strong probability suffices, as stated in al-Nawazil. Then it discusses the pond (ghadir) ruling in more detail, noting that the Balkhians (scholars from Balkh) hold that immersion three times without wringing suffices, though they differ on wringing within their own school. The author then delves into the consideration of the wringer's strength: if a man wrings and the dripping stops, then a stronger man wrings and it drips again, the garment is ruled pure for the first man but not for the stronger one? Actually, the text says it is ruled pure with respect to its owner, but not with respect to the stronger person. This is a subtle point: each person is judged by his own capacity; if he extracts as much as he can, it suffices for him, even if a stronger person could extract more. The author affirms this reasoning, citing Burhan al-Halabi. Finally, there is a note on terminology: the author of Fath al-Qadeer did not include 'pottery, brick, and new wood' in his discussion; he only mentioned the two categories (new and old) qualified as new. This shows the detailed nature of Hanafi legal commentary.

Key Terms
موسوس (muswas): A person prone to excessive doubt (waswasa) regarding purity, requiring stricter rules to prevent obsession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which statement about the non-obsessive person is true?
A) He must wash three times regardless.
B) He may rely on strong probability (ghalabat al-zann) to determine purity.
C) He must wring the garment after each wash.
D) He must wash exactly once.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between obsessive and non-obsessive persons in tahara: three washes are wajib only for the former to cut off doubt.

The Pond Ruling and Balkhian Dispute on Wringing
Detailed ruling on the pond and Balkhian dispute on wringing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Balkhian view on purifying a garment in a pond and identify the three opinions on wringing among them.

Core Idea
According to the Balkhians, immersion three times suffices; wringing is not required according to Abu Hafs al-Kabir.

This passage addresses the ruling for purifying a garment in a pond (ghadir). The Balkhian scholars, led by Abu Hafs al-Kabir, hold that immersing the garment three times without wringing makes it pure. However, other Balkhians disagree on the necessity of wringing, leading to three opinions. This intra-Hanafi dispute is important for understanding regional variations within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The case is a garment that becomes impure and is then immersed in a pond (standing water not flowing). The question is how to purify it.
The pond is considered pure water as long as it is not changed by najasa.
2
State the Balkhian view
The Balkhians (e.g., Abu Hafs al-Kabir) say that immersing the garment three times purifies it, even without wringing.
This is the chosen view according to the passage.
3
Recognize the dispute on wringing
Within the Balkhian camp, there are three opinions: (1) wringing not required at all, (2) wringing required each time, (3) wringing required once.
The passage lists these from Abu Hafs, some unspecified scholars, and Abu Nasr al-Saffar.
4
Understand the significance
This shows that even within a regional group, there can be differences. The mufta bihi may vary depending on circumstances.
The passage does not give a final tarjih, but notes the chosen view of the Balkhians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والظاهر الأول إن لم يكن موسوساً الخ) قال في النهر: وهو توفيق حسن قوله : (وهو أرفق) في قال التتارخانية، وفي النوازل: وعليه الفتوى. قوله: (وأما حكم الغدير الخ) عبارة السراج: وأما حكم الغدير فإن غمس الثوب فيه ثلاثاً وقلنا بقول البلخيين وهو المختار فقد روي عن أبي حفص الكبير أنه يطهر وإن لم يعصر. وقال بعضهم: يشترط العصر في كل مرة. وعن أبي نصر: الصفار يكفيه العصر مرة واحدة اهـ فأفاد أنه عند البلخيين يغمس ثلاثاً وأن قولهم هو المختار لكنهم اختلفوا فيما بينهم في العصر على ثلاثة أقوال: لا يشترط أصلاً، يشترط في كل مرة يشترط في مرة واحدة قوله : (وتعتبر قوة كل عاصر الخ) قال في فتح القدير: حتى إذا انقطع تقاطره بعصره ثم قطر يعصر رجل آخر أقوى منه يحكم بطهارته .اهـ. أي يحكم بطهارته بالنسبة إلى صاحبه ولا يظهر بالنسبة إلى الشخص الأقوى كما ذكره البرهان الحلبي. قال: لأن كل أحد مكلف بقدرته ووسعه ولا يكلف أحد أن يطلب من هو أقوى منه ليعصر ثوبه عند غسله قوله : (ولا يخفى الخ) أقره على هذا البحث أخوه في النهر وكذلك الشيخ إسمعيل في شرح الدرر قوله : ( والخزف والآجر والخشب الجديد أقول: لم يذكر هذه الثلاثة صاحب الفتح في هذا القسم بل ذكر الطرفين في القسم الأول الآتي مقيدين بكونهما جديدين كما
His statement: (And the first is apparent if he is not obsessive etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is a good reconciliation. His statement: (And it is more convenient) has a statement in al-Tatarkhaniyya, and in al-Nawazil: The fatwa is upon it. His statement: (As for the ruling of the pond etc.) The expression of al-Siraj: As for the ruling of the pond, if he immerses the garment in it three times and we say with the Balkhians' view, which is the chosen, it has been related from Abu Hafs al-Kabir that it becomes pure even if not wrung. And some said: Wringing is required each time. From Abu Nasr: al-Saffar, one wringing suffices. So it informs that according to the Balkhians, he immerses three times, and that their view is the chosen, but they differed among themselves regarding wringing into three opinions: not required at all, required each time, required once. His statement: (And the strength of each wringer is considered etc.) He said in Fath al-Qadeer: So if its dripping stops by his wringing, then a stronger man wrings it and it drips, it is ruled pure. That is, it is ruled pure with respect to its owner, but not with respect to the stronger person, as stated by Burhan al-Halabi. He said: Because each person is obligated according to his ability and capacity, and no one is required to seek someone stronger to wring his garment when washing it. His statement: (And it is not hidden etc.) His brother in al-Nahr affirmed this research, as did Shaykh Isma'il in Sharh al-Durar. His statement: (And the pottery, brick, and new wood) I say: The author of al-Fath did not mention these three in this section; rather, he mentioned the two sides in the previous section, qualified as being new.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya-style) of the earlier ruling. It starts with a comment on the phrase 'the first is apparent if he is not obsessive.' The author of Bahr al-Ra'iq quotes from al-Nahr that this is a good reconciliation between the Iraqis and Bukharans. The fatwa is on the view that strong probability suffices, as stated in al-Nawazil. Then it discusses the pond (ghadir) ruling in more detail, noting that the Balkhians (scholars from Balkh) hold that immersion three times without wringing suffices, though they differ on wringing within their own school. The author then delves into the consideration of the wringer's strength: if a man wrings and the dripping stops, then a stronger man wrings and it drips again, the garment is ruled pure for the first man but not for the stronger one? Actually, the text says it is ruled pure with respect to its owner, but not with respect to the stronger person. This is a subtle point: each person is judged by his own capacity; if he extracts as much as he can, it suffices for him, even if a stronger person could extract more. The author affirms this reasoning, citing Burhan al-Halabi. Finally, there is a note on terminology: the author of Fath al-Qadeer did not include 'pottery, brick, and new wood' in his discussion; he only mentioned the two categories (new and old) qualified as new. This shows the detailed nature of Hanafi legal commentary.

Key Terms
بلخيون (Balkhiyun): Scholars from Balkh (e.g., Abu Hafs al-Kabir) who held a lenient view on wringing for the pond.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the chosen view among the Balkhians regarding wringing?
A) Wringing is required each time.
B) One wringing suffices.
C) No wringing is required.
D) Wringing is not mentioned.

Key Takeaway
The Balkhian chosen view holds that immersion three times in a pond purifies a garment without wringing, though there is internal disagreement on wringing.

Consideration of the Wringer's Strength
Ruling on individual capacity in wringing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that each person's capacity determines the sufficiency of wringing, even if a stronger person could extract more water.

Core Idea
Each person is judged by his own strength; if his wringing stops dripping, it suffices for him even if another could wring more.

This passage discusses a subtle point: when a person wrings his garment and the dripping stops, it is considered pure for him, even if a stronger person could wring it further and cause more dripping. The ruling is based on individual capacity and the principle that no one is required to seek someone stronger to help. This demonstrates the Hanafi attention to individual circumstances in tahara rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
A man wrings his garment after washing until it stops dripping. Then a stronger man wrings it again and it drips. The question is: is the garment pure for the first man?
The dripping indicates that water containing impurity could be expelled.
2
Apply the ruling
The garment is ruled pure with respect to the first man because he exerted his full effort. It is not ruled pure with respect to the stronger man if he uses it.
Each person is judged by his own ability.
3
Identify the principle
The principle is that each person is obligated according to his capacity. No one is required to seek out a stronger person to wring for him.
This is based on the Quranic principle of 'la yukallifu nafsan illa wus'aha'.
4
Recognize the source
This ruling is from Fath al-Qadeer and affirmed by Burhan al-Halabi and other Hanafi commentators.
It is a practical application of capacity-based obligation.

Source Text

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a garment to be considered pure after wringing?
A) The dripping must stop completely regardless of who wrings it.
B) The person must wring it until it stops dripping according to his own strength.
C) The garment must be wrung by a person of average strength.
D) Wringing is not necessary if the garment is immersed in a pond.

Key Takeaway
Each person's wringing is sufficient to achieve purity for himself if he wrings to the best of his ability and the dripping stops.
