Drying for Non-Wringable Items and Strength of Wringing
Rules for drying non-wringable items and consideration of wringer's strength.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the method of purifying non-wringable items and explain how the wringer's strength is considered in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Non-wringable items require washing and drying until dripping stops; each person is judged by his own strength.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two related rules for purification: how to handle items that cannot be wrung, and how to assess the wringer's effort. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi method of taharah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of the item
Determine whether the item is non-wringable (la yan'asir) such as leather, khuff, pottery, or new wood, or wringable. This affects the purification method.
Non-wringable items are those that cannot be squeezed by hand, like solid objects.
2
Apply the washing and drying rule
For non-wringable items, wash them three times and dry each time until the dripping stops (jifaf). Complete dryness is not required. For old items, washing three times at once without drying suffices.
Drying helps extract impurity; the ruling is limited to necessity per Fath al-Qadeer.
3
Consider the wringer's strength
Each person is judged by his own physical capacity when wringing. If a person has more strength but refrains to protect the garment, two opinions exist: some say it remains impure, but the more apparent view is that it becomes pure due to necessity.
The fatwa is on considering each person's capacity, not an objective standard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبتثليث الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر) أي ما لا ينعصر فطهارته غسله ثلاثاً وتجفيفه في كل مرة لأن للتجفيف أثراً في استخراج النجاسة وهو أن يتركه حتى ينقطع التقاطر، ولا يشترط فيه اليبس. أطلقه فشمل ما تداخله أجزاء النجاسة أولاً. أما الثاني فيغسل ويجفف في كل مرة كالجلد والخف والمكعب والجرموق والخزف والآجر والخشب الجديد، وأما القديم فيطهر بالغسل ثلاثاً دفعة واحدة وإن لم يجف. كذا ذكروه. وفي فتح القدير : وينبغي تقييده بالمحتاج إليه ا هـ . وتعتبر قوة كل عاصر دون غيره خصوصاً على قول أبي حنيفة أن قدرة الغير غير معتبرة وعليه الفتوى، فلو كانت قوته أكثر من ذلك إلا أنه لم يبالغ في العصر صيانة لثوبه عن التمزيق لرقته قال بعضهم لا يطهر، وقال بعضهم يطهر لمكان الضرورة وهو الأظهر. كذا في السراج الوهاج لكن اختار قاضيخان في فتاواه عدم الطهارة. وفي فتح القدير : إن اشتراط العصر فيما ينعصر مخصوص منه ما قال أبو يوسف في إزار الحمام إذا صب عليه ماء كثير وهو عليه يطهر بلا عصر حتى ذكر الحلواني : لو كانت النجاسة دماً أو بولاً وصب عليه الماء كفاه على قياس قول أبي يوسف في إزار الحمام لكن لا يخفى أن ذلك لضرورة ستر العورة فلا يلحق به غيره وتترك الروايات الظاهرة فيه. وقالوا في البساط النجس : إذا جعل في نهر ليلة ظهر، وفي أنه إذا لم يتهيأ له عصر الكرباس طهر كالبساط ا هـ.
His statement: (And with three-time drying for what cannot be wrung) i.e., what cannot be wrung, its purification is washing it three times and drying it each time, because drying has an effect in extracting the impurity, which is leaving it until the dripping stops, and complete dryness is not required. He made it absolute, so it includes what the parts of impurity have penetrated first. As for the second, it is washed and dried each time, like leather, khuff, muka'ab, jarmuq, earthenware, brick, and new wood. As for the old (wood), it becomes pure by washing three times at once, even if it is not dried. Thus they stated. In Fath al-Qadeer: It should be limited to what is needed. And the strength of each wringer is considered, not another, especially according to Abu Hanifa that the ability of another is not considered, and the fatwa is upon it. So if his strength is more than that, but he did not exert himself in wringing to preserve his garment from tearing due to its thinness, some said it does not become pure, and some said it becomes pure due to necessity, and it is the more apparent. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, but Qadi Khan chose in his Fatawa the lack of purity. In Fath al-Qadeer: The condition of wringing for what can be wrung is excluded from what Abu Yusuf said regarding the basin of the bathhouse: if water is poured on it abundantly while it is on him, it becomes pure without wringing, even al-Halwani mentioned: if the impurity is blood or urine and water is poured on it, it suffices by analogy to Abu Yusuf's statement about the basin of the bathhouse, but it is not hidden that that is due to the necessity of covering the private parts, so nothing else is compared to it, and the apparent transmissions are abandoned in it. And they said regarding the impure carpet: if it is placed in a river for a night, it becomes pure, and if wringing of the Karbas cannot be done, it becomes pure like the carpet.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with two sub-topics: drying for non-wringable items and the strength of wringing. First, for items that cannot be wrung (like leather, khuff, etc.), the method is to wash three times and dry each time by allowing the water to drip off until it stops. This is because drying helps extract the impurity. Importantly, complete dryness (yubs) is not required; only stopping of dripping (inqita' al-taqatur) suffices. The author distinguishes between two types: items that have been penetrated by impurity (al-mutadakhil) require drying three times, while old items that are less absorbent can be washed three times once without drying in between. The author of Fath al-Qadeer suggests the ruling should be limited to necessity. Second, the passage discusses the strength of the wringer: each person is judged by his own strength when wringing, because according to Abu Hanifa, another person's ability is not considered (i.e., a person is not required to wring beyond his capacity). Thus, if a person has the strength to wring more but refrains to protect the fabric, two opinions exist: some say it does not become pure because he could have extracted more, while others say it does become pure due to necessity, and this is the more apparent view. However, Qadi Khan in his Fatawa chose the view of non-purity. The passage then addresses an exception: Abu Yusuf allowed the basin of the bathhouse to be purified by pouring water without wringing, but this is only due to the necessity of covering the private parts and cannot be extended to other cases. Similarly, the impure carpet (bisat) placed in a river overnight becomes pure, and if the carpet cannot be wrung, it is treated like a carpet. This shows the Hanafi method of balancing general rules with specific exceptions based on custom and necessity.

Key Terms
جفاف (jifaf): Drying by allowing water to drip off until it stops; not complete dryness.
لا ينعصر (la yan'asir): Items that cannot be wrung out, such as leather, khuff, pottery, etc.
قوة العاصر (quwwat al-'asir): The physical strength of the person wringing, which is considered according to his individual ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for purifying a leather khuff (sock) that has become impure?
A) Wash once and dry completely.
B) Wash three times and dry each time until dripping stops.
C) Immerse in flowing water only.
D) Wring it three times.

Key Takeaway
Non-wringable items must be washed three times and dried each time until dripping stops; the wringer's strength is judged by his own capacity, with necessity allowing leniency.

Taharah — Purification

Consideration of Wringer's Strength and Necessity Exceptions in Purification
Commentary on wringer's strength and necessity exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that only the wringer's own strength is considered for purification, and evaluate the exceptions for necessity such as the bathhouse waist-wrapper and flowing water for a carpet.

Core Idea
Wringing requires one's own strength; necessity can suspend it, but exceptions are narrowly confined.

This lesson examines a subtle point in Hanafi taharah: the condition of wringing (asr) for absorbent materials and whose strength counts. While the base ruling requires the wringer's own effort, later fatawa and necessity-based exceptions (like the bathhouse izar) create nuances. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores these exceptions and reconciles them with the original rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling regarding wringer's strength
Recognize that only the person's own strength is considered, not that of others, according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the fatwa position.
This is the default rule for all absorbent materials.
2
Analyse the dispute when wringing is omitted to protect the garment
Two positions: some say impure (non-purification), others say pure due to necessity (al-azhar). Qadikhan chooses non-purification.
The 'most apparent' view allows purification due to necessity.
3
Examine the exception of the bathhouse waist-wrapper (izar al-hammam)
Abu Yusuf ruled that pouring abundant water on the worn izar purifies it without wringing. Al-Halwani extends this to blood and urine cases.
The commentator limits this exception to the necessity of covering 'awrah.
4
Reconcile the exception with the base rule
The commentator argues that three-time pouring substitutes wringing, so the izar case is not a true exception. Thus, no difference between izar and other garments if abundant water is used.
This rebuts the claim that necessity alone justifies the exception.
5
Evaluate the carpet (bisat) case and the role of flowing water
If a carpet is placed in a river for a night, it becomes pure because flowing water replaces wringing. The 'night' is to cut off waswasa; otherwise, flowing water until perceived purity suffices.
This aligns with the principle that running water can substitute wringing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المحتاج إليه ا هـ . وتعتبر قوة كل عاصر دون غيره خصوصاً على قول أبي حنيفة أن قدرة الغير غير معتبرة وعليه الفتوى، فلو كانت قوته أكثر من ذلك إلا أنه لم يبالغ في العصر صيانة لثوبه عن التمزيق لرقته قال بعضهم لا يطهر، وقال بعضهم يطهر لمكان الضرورة وهو الأظهر. كذا في السراج الوهاج لكن اختار قاضيخان في فتاواه عدم الطهارة. وفي فتح القدير : إن اشتراط العصر فيما ينعصر مخصوص منه ما قال أبو يوسف في إزار الحمام إذا صب عليه ماء كثير وهو عليه يطهر بلا عصر حتى ذكر الحلواني : لو كانت النجاسة دماً أو بولاً وصب عليه الماء كفاه على قياس قول أبي يوسف في إزار الحمام لكن لا يخفى أن ذلك لضرورة ستر العورة فلا يلحق به غيره وتترك الروايات الظاهرة فيه. وقالوا في البساط النجس : إذا جعل في نهر ليلة ظهر، وفي أنه إذا لم يتهيأ له عصر الكرباس طهر كالبساط ا هـ. ولا يخفى أنّ الإزار المذكور إن كان متنجساً فقد جعلوا الصب الكثير بحيث يخرج ما أصاب الثوب من الماء ويخلفه غيره ثلاثاً قائماً مقام العصر كما قدمناه عن السراج، فحينئذ لا فرق بين إزار الحمام وغيره وليس الاكتفاء به في الإزار لأجل ضرورة الستر كما فهمه المحقق بل لما ذكرناه وظاهر ما في فتاوى قاضيخان أن الإزار ليس متنجساً وإنما أصابه ماء الاغتسال من الجنابة فعلى رواية نجاسة الماء المستعمل طاهر وعليه بنى هذا الفرع، وأما على طهارته فلا حاجة إلى غسله أصلاً كما لا يخفى والتقدير بالليلة في مسألة البساط لقطع الوسوسة وإلا فالمذكور في المحيط قالوا البساط إذا تنجس فأجرى عليه الماء إلى أن يتوهم زوالها طهر لأن إجراء الماء يقوم مقام العصر ا هـ . ولم يقيده بالليلة.
The part needed [from the text] ends. And the strength of each wringer is considered without others, especially according to Abu Hanifa that the ability of others is not considered, and upon this is the fatwa. If his strength is more than that except he did not exert in wringing to protect his garment from tearing due to its delicacy, some said it is not purified, and some said it is purified due to necessity, which is the most apparent. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, but Qadikhan chose in his Fatawa non-purification. And in Fath al-Qadir: The condition of wringing in what is wrung is excluded by what Abu Yusuf said about the waist-wrapper of the bathhouse: if much water is poured on it while he is wearing it, it becomes pure without wringing; until al-Halwani mentioned: If the impurity was blood or urine and water is poured on it, it suffices by analogy with Abu Yusuf's statement about the bathhouse waist-wrapper, but it is not hidden that that is due to the necessity of covering the private parts, so nothing else is attached to it, and the apparent transmissions are abandoned in it. And they said about the impure carpet: If placed in a river for a night it becomes pure, and concerning that if wringing of the thick cloth is not feasible, it becomes pure like the carpet, end. And it is not hidden that if the mentioned waist-wrapper is contaminated, they have made the plentiful pouring such that the water that reaches the garment comes out and is replaced three times, standing in place of wringing as we presented from al-Siraj. So then there is no difference between the bathhouse waist-wrapper and others, and the sufficiency in the waist-wrapper is not due to the necessity of covering as the investigator understood, but rather due to what we mentioned. And the apparent from the Fatawa of Qadikhan is that the waist-wrapper is not contaminated but rather it is affected by the water of bathing from janabah; according to the narration of the impurity of used water it is pure, and upon this he built this branch. As for its purity, there is no need to wash it at all, as is not hidden. And the estimation of a night in the issue of the carpet is to cut off waswasa; otherwise, what is mentioned in al-Muhit: They said that if the carpet becomes impure and water is run over it until it is assumed that it has gone, it becomes pure because running water stands in place of wringing, end. And he did not restrict it to a night.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, dealing with the consideration of the wringer's strength (quwwat al-'asir) in purifying absorbent materials from filth. The base ruling is that only the strength of the person himself is considered, not that of others, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is the fatwa position. If someone has sufficient strength but refrains from fully wringing due to fear of tearing the garment, there is a difference of opinion: some say it remains impure, while others deem it pure due to necessity; the latter is deemed more apparent. Qadikhan, however, chooses non-purification in his Fatawa. The text then discusses an exception reported from Abu Yusuf regarding the waist-wrapper (izar) in the bathhouse: pouring abundant water on it while worn purifies it without wringing. Al-Halwani extends this to blood or urine, but the commentator clarifies that this exception is limited to the necessity of covering the private parts and cannot be generalized. The carpet (bisat) is also discussed: if placed in a river for a night, it becomes pure; flowing water suffices as substitute for wringing. The commentator reconciles the bathhouse izar case, arguing that abundant pouring three times replaces wringing, so there is no real exception. The mention of 'night' for the carpet is merely to cut off obsessive doubts (waswasa); otherwise, the condition is that water flows until impurity is assumed gone.

Key Terms
عصر (asr): Wringing or squeezing to extract water from an absorbent material to remove impurity.
قوة العاصر (quwwat al-'asir): The physical strength of the person wringing; only his own strength is considered, not a stronger person's.
إزار الحمام (izar al-hammam): The waist-wrapper worn in the bathhouse; subject to a special ruling from Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person has sufficient strength to wring his garment but refrains to avoid tearing, what is the most apparent ruling?
A) The garment remains impure in all cases.
B) The garment becomes pure due to necessity.
C) The garment becomes pure only if wrung by a stronger person.
D) The garment becomes pure if washed three times without wringing.

Key Takeaway
Wringing requires the wringer's own strength, but necessity and flowing water can substitute; the exceptions are limited and reasoned.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Purification of Non-Absorbent Materials: Three Washes and Drying
Commentary on the matn ruling for non-absorbent materials requiring three washes and drying each time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for purifying non-absorbent materials and apply the distinction between new and old materials regarding the obligation of drying.

Core Idea
For non-absorbent materials, drying between washes is wajib when impurity penetrates; old materials are purified without drying.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on purifying objects that cannot be wrung, such as leather, wood, and pottery. The key factor is whether impurity has penetrated the material: new (or absorbent) surfaces require drying after each wash, while old materials can be purified by three successive washes without drying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the ruling concerns 'ma la yun'asir' (non-absorbent materials) like leather, wood, and pottery.
2
State the general rule
Purification requires washing three times, and between each wash the object must be left until dripping stops (drying).
Complete dryness is not required; cessation of dripping suffices.
3
Understand the talil
Drying helps extract impurity from the material; this is the reasoning behind the requirement.
4
Distinguish new vs old
New materials (impurity penetrates) require drying each time; old materials (impurity does not penetrate) are purified by three washes at once.
Examples of new: new wood, new pottery. Old: materials that have been saturated by use.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Three opinions exist on drying: not required, required each time, or required once. The relied-upon position is drying each time for new materials.
From Fath al-Qadir: 'Statements: It is not required at all, required each time, required once.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبتثليث الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر) أي ما لا ينعصر فطهارته غسله ثلاثاً وتجفيفه في كل مرة لأن للتجفيف أثراً في استخراج النجاسة وهو أن يتركه حتى ينقطع التقاطر، ولا يشترط فيه اليبس. أطلقه فشمل ما تداخله أجزاء النجاسة أولاً. أما الثاني فيغسل ويجفف في كل مرة كالجلد والخف والمكعب والجرموق والخزف والآجر والخشب الجديد، وأما القديم فيطهر بالغسل ثلاثاً دفعة واحدة وإن لم يجف. كذا ذكروه. وفي فتح القدير : وينبغي تقييد أقوال: لا يشترط أصلاً، يشترط في كل مرة يشترط في مرة واحدة
His saying: (And by threefold drying in what is not wrung) meaning what is not wrung, so its purification is washing it three times and drying it each time because drying has an effect in extracting impurity, and that is to leave it until the dripping stops, and dryness is not required in it. He gave it absolutely so it includes what the parts of impurity enter first. As for the second, it is washed and dried each time, like leather, khuff, square, jarmuq, pottery, brick, and new wood. As for the old, it is purified by washing three times at once even if not dried. Thus they mentioned it. And in Fath al-Qadir: It should be restricted. Statements: It is not required at all, required each time, required once.
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage parses the matn phrase 'By threefold drying for what is not wrung' (wa bi tathlith al-jafaf fima la yun'asir). The author explains that for materials which cannot be wrung (e.g., leather, khuff, wood), purification requires three washes, each followed by drying (allowing dripping to stop). Dryness (yubs) is not required; cessation of dripping suffices. The ruling is general and covers two cases: (1) if impurity has penetrated the material (like new pottery or wood), it must be washed and dried each time; (2) if it is old (already saturated), three washes at once without drying suffice. The commentator then notes from Fath al-Qadir that this should be restricted, and three different opinions are summarized: drying is not required at all, required each time, or required only once. This reflects intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
تثليث الجفاف (tathlith al-jafaf): Threefold drying: washing the object three times and allowing it to dry (dripping stop) between each wash.
ما لا ينعصر (ma la yun'asir): An object that cannot be wrung or squeezed, such as leather, wood, pottery, etc.
تقاطر (taqattur): Dripping of water; cessation of dripping indicates the drying requirement is met.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for purifying an old clay pot that is non-absorbent?
A) Three washes with drying each time.
B) Three washes at once without drying.
C) One wash only.
D) It cannot be purified.

Key Takeaway
Non-absorbent materials require three washes; drying between washes is wajib for new materials but not for old.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Purification of Solid Objects (Pottery, Stone, Wood)
Commentary on purification of solid objects with ghalabat al-zann

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of ghalabat al-zann to purify solid objects and identify when trace (athar) invalidates purification.

Core Idea
For solid surfaces, purification depends on predominant opinion, but any remaining trace of impurity is unforgivable.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between absorbent and non-absorbent materials in purification. For solid objects like pottery, stone, and wood, the ruling hinges on whether any trace of impurity—taste, smell, or color—remains. This lesson unpacks the majority position that uses ghalabat al-zann (predominant opinion) and explains why even a slight trace is not forgiven on hard surfaces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn and its expansion
Locate the commentator's treatment of the matn phrase 'wal-khazaf wal-ajar wal-khashab al-jadid'. Note that the author of Fath al-Qadir did not include these three in this section, but the commentator expands with rulings from al-Asbijabi and others.
This is an expansion probe; the commentator builds on prior texts.
2
Understand the ghalabat al-zann criterion
Al-Asbijabi states that for solid objects, washing is done until one's strongest opinion (akbar ra'y) indicates purity, with no fixed number. This is the majority view attributed by al-Muhit.
Ghalabat al-zann is a probabilistic standard, not certainty.
3
Recognize the trace (athar) rule
If any taste, smell, or color of impurity remains, the object is not pure, even if removal is difficult. The commentator explains that on hard surfaces, trace indicates residual substance, unlike cloth where adjacency may cause stain.
This is reinforced by al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah's example of wine trace in a vessel.
4
Distinguish new vs. old pottery (and analogies)
Al-Hawi al-Qudsi provides different methods: new pottery/stone must be burned if impurity penetrated; old pottery is washed. For wood, new is scraped, old is washed. For metals/glass, smooth surfaces are wiped, rough ones washed.
The dryness of the object matters: if left to dry after use, it is treated like new.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتعتبر قوة كل عاصر الخ) قال في فتح القدير : حتى إذا انقطع تقاطره بعصره ثم قطر يعصر رجل آخر أقوى منه يحكم بطهارته .اهـ. أي يحكم بطهارته بالنسبة إلى صاحبه ولا يظهر بالنسبة إلى الشخص الأقوى كما ذكره البرهان الحلبي . قال : لأن كل أحد مكلف بقدرته ووسعه ولا يكلف أحد أن يطلب من هو أقوى منه ليعصر ثوبه عند غسله قوله : (ولا يخفى الخ) أقره على هذا البحث أخوه في النهر وكذلك الشيخ إسمعيل في شرح الدرر قوله : ( والخزف والآجر والخشب الجديد أقول : لم يذكر هذه الثلاثة صاحب الفتح في هذا القسم بل ذكر الطرفين في القسم الأول الآتي مقيدين بكونهما جديدين كما يوجد بعد ذلك خشب الخزفة بما إذا تنجست وهي رطبة أما لو تركت بعد الاستعمال حتى جفت فإنها كالجديدة لأنه يشاهد اجتذابها حتى يظهر من ظاهرها اهـ. وذكر الإمام الاسبيجابي : وإن كان ذلك الشيء الذي أصابه النجاسة صلباً كالحجر والآجر والخشب والأواني فإنه يغسل مقدار ما يقع في أكبر رأيه أنه قد طهر ولا توقيت فيه، وإنما حكم بطهارته إذا كان لا طعم النجاسة ولا رائحتها ولا لونها، فإذا وجد منها أحد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة فلا يحكم بطهارتها، سواء كانت الآنية من الخزف أو من غيره ، جديداً كان أو غير جديد. وعزاه صاحب المحيط إلى أكثر المشايخ وهو بإطلاقه يفيد أن الأثر فيه غير مغتفر وإن كان يشق زواله بخلاف ما ذكروا في الثوب ونحوه والتفرقة بينهما في هذه لا تعرى عن شيء ولعل وجه ذلك أن بقاء الأثر هنا دال على قيام شيء من العين بخلاف الثوب ونحوه لجواز أن يكون الاكتساب فيه بسبب المجاورة واستمرت قائمة بعد اضمحلال العين منه . كذا في شرح المنية . ويدل للتفرقة ما في الفتاوى الظهيرية وإن بقي أثر الخمر يجعل فيه الخل حتى لا يبقى أثرها فيطهر اهـ. وفي الحاوي القدسي والأواني ثلاثة أنواع : خزف وخشب وحديد ونحوها، وتطهيرها على أربعة أوجه حرق ونحت ومسح وغسل. فإن كان الإناء من خزف أو حجر وكان جديداً ودخلت النجاسة في أجزائه يحرق، وإن كان عتيقاً يغسل، وإن كان من خشب وكان جديداً ينحت وإن كان عتيقاً يغسل، وإن كان من حديد أو صفر أو زجاج أو رصاص وكان صقيلاً . يمسح وإن كان خشناً يغسل ا هـ . وفي الذخيرة: وحكي عن الفقيه أبي اسحق الحافظ أنه إذا أصابت النجاسة البدن يطهر بالغسل ثلاث مرات متواليات لأن العصر متعذر فقام التوالي في الغسل مقام العصر، وفي شرح المنية والأظهر أن كلاً من التوالي والترك ليس بشرط في البدن وما يجري مجراه بعد التفريع على اشتراط الثلاث في ذلك، وقد صرح به في النوازل وفي الذخيرة ما يوافقه وأما على أن الاعتبار بغلبة الظن فعدم اشتراط . كل منهما أظهر ا هـ . وفي عمدة الفتاوى : نجاسة يابسة على الحصيرة تفرك وفي الرطبة يجرى عليها الماء ثلاثاً والإجراء كالعصر. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: البردي إذا تنجس إن كانت النجاسة رطبة تغسل بالماء ثلاثاً ويقوم الحصير حتى يخرج الماء من أثقابه، وإن كانت النجاسة فد يبست في الحصر تدلك حتى تلين النجاسة فتزول بالماء، ولو كان الحصير من القصب ذكرنا أنه يغسل ثلاثاً فيطهر ا.هـ. وحمله في فتح القدير على الحصير الصقيلة كأكثر مصر، أما الجديدة المتخذة مما يتشرب فسيأتي . سيذكره الشارح أيضاً وذكر الوسط هنا مقيداً بالقديم وجعل حكمه كالخزفة القديمة فتأمل. قوله : والسكين المموهة الخ) قال في المنية : ولو موّه الحديد النجس بالماء النجس ثم يموّه بالماء الطاهر ثلاث مرات فيظهر . قال البرهان الحلبي : عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد فإن عنده لا يطهر أبداً بناء
His saying: (And the strength of each wringer is considered, etc.) He said in Fath al-Qadir: Such that when its dripping stops by his wringing, then if it drips and another stronger person wrings it, it is ruled pure, end. Meaning it is ruled pure for its owner, but not apparent for the stronger person as al-Burhan al-Halabi mentioned. He said: Because each person is obligated according to his ability and capacity, and one is not obligated to seek someone stronger to wring his garment when washing it. His saying: (And it is not hidden, etc.) His brother in al-Nahr affirmed this research, as did Shaykh Isma'il in Sharh al-Durar. His saying: (And pottery, brick, and new wood) I say: The author of al-Fath did not mention these three in this section, but mentioned the two categories in the first section below, restricted to being new, as will follow later. Pottery is when it becomes impure while moist; but if left after use until dry, it is like new because its absorption is observed until it appears from its exterior, end. And Imam al-Asbijabi mentioned: And if that thing which the impurity afflicted is solid like stone, brick, wood, and vessels, then it is washed an amount that falls in his strongest opinion that it has become pure, and there is no timing in it. It is only ruled pure when there is no taste, smell, or color of impurity. If any of these three exist, it is not ruled pure, whether the vessel is of pottery or other, new or not new. The author of al-Muhit attributed this to the majority of mashayikh, and its generality indicates that the trace is not forgiven even if its removal is difficult, contrary to what they mentioned for cloth and the like. The distinction between them in this is not without something, and perhaps the reason is that the presence of the trace here indicates remnant of the substance, unlike cloth because the acquisition may be due to adjacency and remains after the substance has dissipated. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah. And what supports the distinction is what is in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If the trace of wine remains, vinegar is placed in it until its trace disappears, then it becomes pure, end. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Vessels are of three types: pottery, wood, iron and the like, and their purification is on four modes: burning, scraping, wiping, and washing. If the vessel is of pottery or stone and is new, and impurity entered its parts, it is burned; if old, it is washed. If of wood and new, it is scraped; if old, it is washed. If of iron, brass, glass, or lead, and is polished, it is wiped; if rough, it is washed, end. And in al-Dhakhirah: It is narrated from al-Faqih Abu Ishaq al-Hafiz that if impurity afflicts the body, it is purified by washing three times consecutively because wringing is impossible, so consecutiveness in washing stands in place of wringing. In Sharh al-Munyah, the most apparent is that each of consecutiveness and leaving is not a condition for the body and what is analogous to it, after branching on requiring three times in that. It has been explicitly stated in al-Nawazil and in al-Dhakhirah something that agrees. As for considering predominant opinion, non-requirement of each is more apparent, end. In 'Umdat al-Fatawa: Dry impurity on a mat is rubbed, and for wet impurity, water is run over it three times, and running water is like wringing. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a rush mat becomes impure, if the impurity is wet, it is washed three times and the mat is raised until water comes out of its holes; if the impurity has dried on the mat, it is rubbed until the impurity softens and is removed by water. If the mat is of reed, we mentioned that it is washed three times and becomes pure, end. And he (the author of Fath al-Qadir) interpreted it as referring to the smooth mat like most of Egypt; as for the new one made of absorbent material, it will come later. The commentator will also mention it, and he mentioned the middle here restricted to old, and made its ruling like old pottery, so reflect. His saying: (And the gilded knife, etc.) He said in al-Munyah: And if impure iron is gilded with impure water, then gilded with pure water three times, it appears. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: According to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, for according to him it never becomes pure, based on...
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on several matn phrases. First, it revisits the wringer's strength: if dripping stops after one wrings, but then another stronger person wrings and it drips again, the garment is ruled pure for the first owner (since he did his utmost), but the stronger person's wringing does not affect the ruling. This is based on the principle that each person is only obligated according to his capacity. The text then discusses purification of pottery, brick, wood, and solid objects. For new pottery that is wet when impurity hits, it must be dried and then treated as new; if left to dry, it becomes like old. Imam al-Asbijabi states that solid objects (stone, pottery, wood, vessels) are purified by washing until one's predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) holds that it is clean; there is no fixed number. However, if any trace (taste, smell, color) remains, it is not pure. This is the view of the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, and the trace is not forgiven even if difficult to remove, unlike cloth where residual stain is forgiven. The distinction is that on hard surfaces, trace indicates actual substance, while on cloth it may be only adjacency. The text then cites al-Hawi al-Qudsi on three types of vessels: pottery/stone (burn if new, wash if old), wood (scrape if new, wash if old), metal/glass (wipe if smooth, wash if rough). Next, purification of the body: three consecutive washes suffice since wringing is impossible; but the most apparent view is that neither consecutiveness nor leaving is a condition—only the requirement of three washes. For a mat (hasir), dry impurity is rubbed off, wet impurity requires running water three times. Qadikhan adds details for rush and reed mats. Finally, the knife: if impure iron is gilded with impure water, then gilded with pure water three times, it becomes pure according to Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad says it never becomes pure; the text cuts off here.

Key Terms
غالب الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or overwhelming conjecture; used to determine purity when no fixed number is given.
الأثر غير مغتفر (al-athar ghayru maghtafir): The trace (of impurity) is not forgiven; if any taste, smell, or color remains, purification is not complete.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Asbijabi and the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, how is a solid object (like old stone) purified?
A) Wash it three times and squeeze dry.
B) Burn it to remove impurity.
C) Wash it until no taste, smell, or color remains, with no fixed number.
D) Wipe it once with a wet cloth.

Key Takeaway
For solid objects, purification requires washing until predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) of cleanliness, and any remaining trace of impurity is unforgivable.

Taharah — Purification
beginner

Wringer Strength and Personal Capacity
Commentary on the matn regarding wringer strength and the principle of personal capacity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the ruling on wringer strength is tied to individual capacity and apply it to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Each person is only obligated to wring according to his own strength; another's greater strength does not affect the ruling.

The passage revisits the wringer's strength, a topic from earlier in the chapter. Here, the commentator clarifies that if after a person wrings his garment and the dripping stops, but then a stronger person wrings it and water drips out, the garment is considered pure for the original owner. This is because each person is only required to do what is within their ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn phrase and its expansion
The matn says: 'And the strength of each wringer is considered.' The commentator cites Fath al-Qadir and al-Burhan al-Halabi to explain the scenario.
The matn is about the effectiveness of wringing according to one's strength.
2
Understand the hypothetical scenario
If a person wrings his garment and no more water drips, then another stronger person wrings it and water drips, the garment is ruled pure for the first person.
The dripping from the stronger person does not retroactively make the first person's effort insufficient.
3
Extract the principle
The basis is that each person is obligated according to his ability (al-taklif bi-hasab al-wus'). No one is required to seek a stronger person to wring for them.
This principle is found elsewhere in Hanafi fiqh, e.g., in ablution and prayer.
4
Note the limits of the ruling
The ruling is for the original owner's perspective; the stronger person's wringing does not make the garment impure for the owner, but the stronger person himself may need to wash his hands if he touches the garment? Not stated here.
Al-Burhan al-Halabi notes it is not apparent for the stronger person.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتعتبر قوة كل عاصر الخ) قال في فتح القدير : حتى إذا انقطع تقاطره بعصره ثم قطر يعصر رجل آخر أقوى منه يحكم بطهارته .اهـ. أي يحكم بطهارته بالنسبة إلى صاحبه ولا يظهر بالنسبة إلى الشخص الأقوى كما ذكره البرهان الحلبي . قال : لأن كل أحد مكلف بقدرته ووسعه ولا يكلف أحد أن يطلب من هو أقوى منه ليعصر ثوبه عند غسله قوله : (ولا يخفى الخ) أقره على هذا البحث أخوه في النهر وكذلك الشيخ إسمعيل في شرح الدرر قوله : ( والخزف والآجر والخشب الجديد أقول : لم يذكر هذه الثلاثة صاحب الفتح في هذا القسم بل ذكر الطرفين في القسم الأول الآتي مقيدين بكونهما جديدين كما يوجد بعد ذلك خشب الخزفة بما إذا تنجست وهي رطبة أما لو تركت بعد الاستعمال حتى جفت فإنها كالجديدة لأنه يشاهد اجتذابها حتى يظهر من ظاهرها اهـ. وذكر الإمام الاسبيجابي : وإن كان ذلك الشيء الذي أصابه النجاسة صلباً كالحجر والآجر والخشب والأواني فإنه يغسل مقدار ما يقع في أكبر رأيه أنه قد طهر ولا توقيت فيه، وإنما حكم بطهارته إذا كان لا طعم النجاسة ولا رائحتها ولا لونها، فإذا وجد منها أحد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة فلا يحكم بطهارتها، سواء كانت الآنية من الخزف أو من غيره ، جديداً كان أو غير جديد. وعزاه صاحب المحيط إلى أكثر المشايخ وهو بإطلاقه يفيد أن الأثر فيه غير مغتفر وإن كان يشق زواله بخلاف ما ذكروا في الثوب ونحوه والتفرقة بينهما في هذه لا تعرى عن شيء ولعل وجه ذلك أن بقاء الأثر هنا دال على قيام شيء من العين بخلاف الثوب ونحوه لجواز أن يكون الاكتساب فيه بسبب المجاورة واستمرت قائمة بعد اضمحلال العين منه . كذا في شرح المنية . ويدل للتفرقة ما في الفتاوى الظهيرية وإن بقي أثر الخمر يجعل فيه الخل حتى لا يبقى أثرها فيطهر اهـ. وفي الحاوي القدسي والأواني ثلاثة أنواع : خزف وخشب وحديد ونحوها، وتطهيرها على أربعة أوجه حرق ونحت ومسح وغسل. فإن كان الإناء من خزف أو حجر وكان جديداً ودخلت النجاسة في أجزائه يحرق، وإن كان عتيقاً يغسل، وإن كان من خشب وكان جديداً ينحت وإن كان عتيقاً يغسل، وإن كان من حديد أو صفر أو زجاج أو رصاص وكان صقيلاً . يمسح وإن كان خشناً يغسل ا هـ . وفي الذخيرة: وحكي عن الفقيه أبي اسحق الحافظ أنه إذا أصابت النجاسة البدن يطهر بالغسل ثلاث مرات متواليات لأن العصر متعذر فقام التوالي في الغسل مقام العصر، وفي شرح المنية والأظهر أن كلاً من التوالي والترك ليس بشرط في البدن وما يجري مجراه بعد التفريع على اشتراط الثلاث في ذلك، وقد صرح به في النوازل وفي الذخيرة ما يوافقه وأما على أن الاعتبار بغلبة الظن فعدم اشتراط . كل منهما أظهر ا هـ . وفي عمدة الفتاوى : نجاسة يابسة على الحصيرة تفرك وفي الرطبة يجرى عليها الماء ثلاثاً والإجراء كالعصر. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان: البردي إذا تنجس إن كانت النجاسة رطبة تغسل بالماء ثلاثاً ويقوم الحصير حتى يخرج الماء من أثقابه، وإن كانت النجاسة فد يبست في الحصر تدلك حتى تلين النجاسة فتزول بالماء، ولو كان الحصير من القصب ذكرنا أنه يغسل ثلاثاً فيطهر ا.هـ. وحمله في فتح القدير على الحصير الصقيلة كأكثر مصر، أما الجديدة المتخذة مما يتشرب فسيأتي . سيذكره الشارح أيضاً وذكر الوسط هنا مقيداً بالقديم وجعل حكمه كالخزفة القديمة فتأمل. قوله : والسكين المموهة الخ) قال في المنية : ولو موّه الحديد النجس بالماء النجس ثم يموّه بالماء الطاهر ثلاث مرات فيظهر . قال البرهان الحلبي : عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد فإن عنده لا يطهر أبداً بناء
His saying: (And the strength of each wringer is considered, etc.) He said in Fath al-Qadir: Such that when its dripping stops by his wringing, then if it drips and another stronger person wrings it, it is ruled pure, end. Meaning it is ruled pure for its owner, but not apparent for the stronger person as al-Burhan al-Halabi mentioned. He said: Because each person is obligated according to his ability and capacity, and one is not obligated to seek someone stronger to wring his garment when washing it. His saying: (And it is not hidden, etc.) His brother in al-Nahr affirmed this research, as did Shaykh Isma'il in Sharh al-Durar. His saying: (And pottery, brick, and new wood) I say: The author of al-Fath did not mention these three in this section, but mentioned the two categories in the first section below, restricted to being new, as will follow later. Pottery is when it becomes impure while moist; but if left after use until dry, it is like new because its absorption is observed until it appears from its exterior, end. And Imam al-Asbijabi mentioned: And if that thing which the impurity afflicted is solid like stone, brick, wood, and vessels, then it is washed an amount that falls in his strongest opinion that it has become pure, and there is no timing in it. It is only ruled pure when there is no taste, smell, or color of impurity. If any of these three exist, it is not ruled pure, whether the vessel is of pottery or other, new or not new. The author of al-Muhit attributed this to the majority of mashayikh, and its generality indicates that the trace is not forgiven even if its removal is difficult, contrary to what they mentioned for cloth and the like. The distinction between them in this is not without something, and perhaps the reason is that the presence of the trace here indicates remnant of the substance, unlike cloth because the acquisition may be due to adjacency and remains after the substance has dissipated. Thus in Sharh al-Munyah. And what supports the distinction is what is in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If the trace of wine remains, vinegar is placed in it until its trace disappears, then it becomes pure, end. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Vessels are of three types: pottery, wood, iron and the like, and their purification is on four modes: burning, scraping, wiping, and washing. If the vessel is of pottery or stone and is new, and impurity entered its parts, it is burned; if old, it is washed. If of wood and new, it is scraped; if old, it is washed. If of iron, brass, glass, or lead, and is polished, it is wiped; if rough, it is washed, end. And in al-Dhakhirah: It is narrated from al-Faqih Abu Ishaq al-Hafiz that if impurity afflicts the body, it is purified by washing three times consecutively because wringing is impossible, so consecutiveness in washing stands in place of wringing. In Sharh al-Munyah, the most apparent is that each of consecutiveness and leaving is not a condition for the body and what is analogous to it, after branching on requiring three times in that. It has been explicitly stated in al-Nawazil and in al-Dhakhirah something that agrees. As for considering predominant opinion, non-requirement of each is more apparent, end. In 'Umdat al-Fatawa: Dry impurity on a mat is rubbed, and for wet impurity, water is run over it three times, and running water is like wringing. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a rush mat becomes impure, if the impurity is wet, it is washed three times and the mat is raised until water comes out of its holes; if the impurity has dried on the mat, it is rubbed until the impurity softens and is removed by water. If the mat is of reed, we mentioned that it is washed three times and becomes pure, end. And he (the author of Fath al-Qadir) interpreted it as referring to the smooth mat like most of Egypt; as for the new one made of absorbent material, it will come later. The commentator will also mention it, and he mentioned the middle here restricted to old, and made its ruling like old pottery, so reflect. His saying: (And the gilded knife, etc.) He said in al-Munyah: And if impure iron is gilded with impure water, then gilded with pure water three times, it appears. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: According to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, for according to him it never becomes pure, based on...
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on several matn phrases. First, it revisits the wringer's strength: if dripping stops after one wrings, but then another stronger person wrings and it drips again, the garment is ruled pure for the first owner (since he did his utmost), but the stronger person's wringing does not affect the ruling. This is based on the principle that each person is only obligated according to his capacity. The text then discusses purification of pottery, brick, wood, and solid objects. For new pottery that is wet when impurity hits, it must be dried and then treated as new; if left to dry, it becomes like old. Imam al-Asbijabi states that solid objects (stone, pottery, wood, vessels) are purified by washing until one's predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) holds that it is clean; there is no fixed number. However, if any trace (taste, smell, color) remains, it is not pure. This is the view of the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, and the trace is not forgiven even if difficult to remove, unlike cloth where residual stain is forgiven. The distinction is that on hard surfaces, trace indicates actual substance, while on cloth it may be only adjacency. The text then cites al-Hawi al-Qudsi on three types of vessels: pottery/stone (burn if new, wash if old), wood (scrape if new, wash if old), metal/glass (wipe if smooth, wash if rough). Next, purification of the body: three consecutive washes suffice since wringing is impossible; but the most apparent view is that neither consecutiveness nor leaving is a condition—only the requirement of three washes. For a mat (hasir), dry impurity is rubbed off, wet impurity requires running water three times. Qadikhan adds details for rush and reed mats. Finally, the knife: if impure iron is gilded with impure water, then gilded with pure water three times, it becomes pure according to Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad says it never becomes pure; the text cuts off here.

Key Terms
غالب الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Predominant opinion or overwhelming conjecture; used to determine purity when no fixed number is given.
الأثر غير مغتفر (al-athar ghayru maghtafir): The trace (of impurity) is not forgiven; if any taste, smell, or color remains, purification is not complete.
السكين المموهة (al-sikkin al-mumawwahah): A gilded or plated knife; the ruling concerns its purification after contact with impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the garment ruled pure for the original owner even after a stronger person wrings out more water?
A) Because the stronger person's wringing is not considered legally.
B) Because each person is only obligated according to his ability.
C) Because the water from the stronger person is considered pure.
D) Because the owner did not need to wring the garment at all.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on wringer strength demonstrates that purity is judged by individual capacity, not an absolute standard.

Taharah — Purification

Purification of the Body, Mats, and Gilded Knife
Commentary on purification of body, mats, and gilded knife with intra-Hanafi disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for purifying the body, mats, and gilded objects, and identify the intra-madhhab disagreements.

Core Idea
The body needs three washes without requiring consecutiveness; mats are washed three times with water running through; a gilded knife is purified by three times gilding with pure water (Abu Yusuf's view).

This passage covers three distinct purification cases: the body (when wringing is impossible), mats (made of reeds or rushes), and a gilded knife that has been contaminated. For each, there is a ruling and sometimes an intra-Hanafi disagreement. The commentator brings together sources from al-Dhakhirah, Sharh al-Munyah, 'Umdat al-Fatawa, and Fatawa Qadikhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for body purification
The passage mentions from al-Dhakhirah a narration that the body is purified by three consecutive washes because wringing is impossible. But the more apparent view in Sharh al-Munyah is that consecutiveness is not a condition—only three washes are required.
This is a dispute between al-Faqih Abu Ishaq and the majority.
2
Apply the rule to mats and similar objects
For a mat (hasir) with dry impurity, simply rub it off; for wet impurity, run water over it three times, and that running water substitutes for wringing. For rush mats, raise the mat so water drains through holes.
Clarification from Fatawa Qadikhan on different types of mats.
3
Understand the case of the gilded knife
If a knife's iron is impure and then gilded with pure water three times, Abu Yusuf says it becomes pure, whereas Muhammad says it never becomes pure. The passage cuts off before giving the majority view.
This ikhtilaf is based on whether gilding acts as a new covering that seals the impurity.

And what supports the distinction is what is in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If the trace of wine remains, vinegar is placed in it until its trace disappears, then it becomes pure, end. And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Vessels are of three types: pottery, wood, iron and the like, and their purification is on four modes: burning, scraping, wiping, and washing. If the vessel is of pottery or stone and is new, and impurity entered its parts, it is burned; if old, it is washed. If of wood and new, it is scraped; if old, it is washed. If of iron, brass, glass, or lead, and is polished, it is wiped; if rough, it is washed, end. And in al-Dhakhirah: It is narrated from al-Faqih Abu Ishaq al-Hafiz that if impurity afflicts the body, it is purified by washing three times consecutively because wringing is impossible, so consecutiveness in washing stands in place of wringing. In Sharh al-Munyah, the most apparent is that each of consecutiveness and leaving is not a condition for the body and what is analogous to it, after branching on requiring three times in that. It has been explicitly stated in al-Nawazil and in al-Dhakhirah something that agrees. As for considering predominant opinion, non-requirement of each is more apparent, end. In 'Umdat al-Fatawa: Dry impurity on a mat is rubbed, and for wet impurity, water is run over it three times, and running water is like wringing. In Fatawa Qadikhan: If a rush mat becomes impure, if the impurity is wet, it is washed three times and the mat is raised until water comes out of its holes; if the impurity has dried on the mat, it is rubbed until the impurity softens and is removed by water. If the mat is of reed, we mentioned that it is washed three times and becomes pure, end. And he (the author of Fath al-Qadir) interpreted it as referring to the smooth mat like most of Egypt; as for the new one made of absorbent material, it will come later. The commentator will also mention it, and he mentioned the middle here restricted to old, and made its ruling like old pottery, so reflect. His saying: (And the gilded knife, etc.) He said in al-Munyah: And if impure iron is gilded with impure water, then gilded with pure water three times, it appears. Al-Burhan al-Halabi said: According to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, for according to him it never becomes pure, based on...
Source pages p. 413

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on several matn phrases. First, it revisits the wringer's strength: if dripping stops after one wrings, but then another stronger person wrings and it drips again, the garment is ruled pure for the first owner (since he did his utmost), but the stronger person's wringing does not affect the ruling. This is based on the principle that each person is only obligated according to his capacity. The text then discusses purification of pottery, brick, wood, and solid objects. For new pottery that is wet when impurity hits, it must be dried and then treated as new; if left to dry, it becomes like old. Imam al-Asbijabi states that solid objects (stone, pottery, wood, vessels) are purified by washing until one's predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) holds that it is clean; there is no fixed number. However, if any trace (taste, smell, color) remains, it is not pure. This is the view of the majority of Hanafi mashayikh, and the trace is not forgiven even if difficult to remove, unlike cloth where residual stain is forgiven. The distinction is that on hard surfaces, trace indicates actual substance, while on cloth it may be only adjacency. The text then cites al-Hawi al-Qudsi on three types of vessels: pottery/stone (burn if new, wash if old), wood (scrape if new, wash if old), metal/glass (wipe if smooth, wash if rough). Next, purification of the body: three consecutive washes suffice since wringing is impossible; but the most apparent view is that neither consecutiveness nor leaving is a condition—only the requirement of three washes. For a mat (hasir), dry impurity is rubbed off, wet impurity requires running water three times. Qadikhan adds details for rush and reed mats. Finally, the knife: if impure iron is gilded with impure water, then gilded with pure water three times, it becomes pure according to Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad says it never becomes pure; the text cuts off here.

Key Terms
السكين المموهة (al-sikkin al-mumawwahah): A gilded or plated knife; the ruling concerns its purification after contact with impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most apparent view in Sharh al-Munyah, what is the condition for purifying the body from impurity?
A) Three consecutive washes without drying.
B) Three washes without any condition of consecutiveness.
C) One thorough wash with soap.
D) Washing until no trace remains, using ghalabat al-zann.

Key Takeaway
Body purification requires three washes without consecutiveness; mats require three washes with effective drainage; gilded knife purification is disputed between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Purification of Solid Objects: Trace Impurity is Not Excused
Ruling on purifying hard, non-porous objects with a proof from Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for purifying hard objects and distinguish when a residual trace prevents purity.

Core Idea
On hard surfaces, any trace of impurity indicates remaining substance, so it is not excused unlike cloth.

In this passage from Bahr al-Raiq, we learn how to purify solid objects like stone, wood, and pottery. Unlike cloth, where traces may be overlooked due to difficulty, hard objects require removal of all vestiges. The ruling hinges on one's best judgment (akbar ra'y) and the absence of taste, smell, or color. The distinction is supported by a practical example from Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object's material
Determine if the object is solid (stone, wood, pottery) or porous (cloth). The ruling differs based on material type.
Hanafi law treats hard, non-absorbent objects strictly regarding traces.
2
Apply the standard of purification
Wash the object until your best judgment (akbar ra'y) indicates purity. No fixed number of washes is required; it depends on subjective certainty.
The method is qualitative, not quantitative.
3
Check for traces
After washing, ensure no taste, smell, or color of impurity remains. If any of these three persists, the object is not pure and must be rewashed.
These three criteria are from the text.
4
Recognize the exception for hard objects
Unlike cloth, traces on hard objects are not excused even if difficult to remove. The persistence of a trace indicates residual impurity substance.
The text provides a rationale: on cloth, traces may be due to adjacency after substance has dissipated.
5
Apply the supporting evidence
Consider the example from Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: if the trace of wine remains in a vessel, vinegar must be added until the trace disappears. This proves that traces must be eliminated for purity.
This analogy confirms the strict rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خشب الخزفة بما إذا تنجست وهي رطبة أما لو تركت بعد الاستعمال حتى جفت فإنها كالجديدة لأنه يشاهد اجتذابها حتى يظهر من ظاهرها اهـ. وذكر الإمام الاسبيجابي : وإن كان ذلك الشيء الذي أصابه النجاسة صلباً كالحجر والآجر والخشب والأواني فإنه يغسل مقدار ما يقع في أكبر رأيه أنه قد طهر ولا توقيت فيه، وإنما حكم بطهارته إذا كان لا طعم النجاسة ولا رائحتها ولا لونها، فإذا وجد منها أحد هذه الأشياء الثلاثة فلا يحكم بطهارتها، سواء كانت الآنية من الخزف أو من غيره ، جديداً كان أو غير جديد. وعزاه صاحب المحيط إلى أكثر المشايخ وهو بإطلاقه يفيد أن الأثر فيه غير مغتفر وإن كان يشق زواله بخلاف ما ذكروا في الثوب ونحوه والتفرقة بينهما في هذه لا تعرى عن شيء ولعل وجه ذلك أن بقاء الأثر هنا دال على قيام شيء من العين بخلاف الثوب ونحوه لجواز أن يكون الاكتساب فيه بسبب المجاورة واستمرت قائمة بعد اضمحلال العين منه . كذا في شرح المنية . ويدل للتفرقة ما في الفتاوى الظهيرية وإن بقي أثر الخمر يجعل فيه الخل حتى لا يبقى أثرها فيطهر اهـ.
Regarding fired clay vessels (khazaf): If impure while wet, but if left after use until dry, they are like new because it is observed that it absorbs such that [impurity] appears on its surface. End quote. Imam al-Asbijabi mentioned: If that object which impurity hit is solid like stone, brick, wood, and vessels, it is washed as much as is in his best judgment that it has become pure, without a set limit. It is judged pure only if there is no taste, smell, or color of impurity. If any of these three is found, it is not judged pure, whether the vessel is khazaf or other, new or old. Al-Muhit attributed this to most shaykhs, and its absolute wording indicates that the trace is not forgiven even if its removal is difficult, contrary to what they mentioned for cloth and the like. The distinction between them here is not free from something; perhaps its reason is that the persistence of the trace here indicates the existence of some of the substance, unlike cloth and the like, because it is possible that the acquisition [of impurity] is due to adjacency and the [trace] remained existing after the substance dissipated. Thus in Sharh al-Munya. And supporting the distinction is what is in Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: If the trace of wine remains, vinegar is placed in it until its trace disappears, then it is purified. End quote.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage addresses the purification of hard, non-porous objects such as stone, wood, and pottery. The key ruling is that when such objects become impure, they must be washed until one is confident of purity, with no fixed number of washes. Purity is judged by the absence of taste, smell, and color of the impurity. The critical point here is that in contrast to cloth (where traces of impurity may be excused due to difficulty of removal), on hard objects any remaining trace is not excused. The rationale is that on hard surfaces a trace indicates actual residual substance, whereas on cloth the trace may be due to adjacent spread even after the substance is gone. The text concludes with a corroborating example from Fatawa al-Zahiriyyah: if wine's trace remains in a vessel, one must add vinegar until the trace disappears; only then is it pure. This underscores that traces are not tolerated on hard objects.

Key Terms
الخزفة (al-khazaf): A fired clay vessel or pottery.
أكبر رأيه (akbar ra'yihi): One's dominant or best judgment based on likely certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a hard object like a stone or vessel considered ritually pure after impurity?
A) After one wash with water
B) When no taste, smell, or color of the impurity remains
C) When dried after washing
D) When washed three times consecutively

Key Takeaway
On solid objects, any residual trace of impurity is not excused; the object must be washed until all taste, smell, and color are gone.

Vessel Types and Purification Methods in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumeration of vessel types and purification methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of vessels and identify the correct purification method for each based on material and condition.

Core Idea
Three vessel types, four methods: burning for new pottery, scraping for new wood, wiping for smooth metal, washing for everything else.

In Hanafi tahara, the purification of vessels varies by material and age. This passage from al-Hawi al-Qudsi provides a concise classification that helps you apply the correct method. Understanding these categories ensures that rulings on impurity removal are applied correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three vessel types
List the three categories mentioned: pottery/stone (khazaf), wood, and metals (iron, brass, glass, lead).
Note that 'and the like' indicates other similar materials.
2
List the four purification methods
The methods are burning (حرق), scraping (نحت), wiping (مسح), and washing (غسل).
These cover all possible scenarios.
3
Match method to vessel type and condition
For new pottery/stone: burning. For new wood: scraping. For smooth metal/glass/lead: wiping. For all old vessels or rough surfaces: washing.
New means impurity is fresh and has seeped into porous material.
4
Note the default method for old vessels
Regardless of material, if the vessel is old (meaning impurity has set in), the only effective method is washing.
Old vessels are those where impurity has penetrated deeply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحاوي القدسي والأواني ثلاثة أنواع : خزف وخشب وحديد ونحوها، وتطهيرها على أربعة أوجه حرق ونحت ومسح وغسل. فإن كان الإناء من خزف أو حجر وكان جديداً ودخلت النجاسة في أجزائه يحرق، وإن كان عتيقاً يغسل، وإن كان من وكان جديداً ينحت وإن كان عتيقاً يغسل، وإن كان من حديد أو صفر أو زجاج أو رصاص وكان صقيلاً . يمسح وإن كان خشناً يغسل ا هـ .
And in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Vessels are of three types: khazaf (pottery/clay), wood, and iron and the like. Their purification is by four methods: burning, scraping, wiping, and washing. If the vessel is of khazaf or stone and is new and impurity entered its parts, it is burned; if it is old, it is washed. If it is of wood and is new, it is scraped; if old, it is washed. If it is of iron, brass, glass, or lead, and is smooth, it is wiped; if it is rough, it is washed. End quote.
Source pages p. 414

Commentary
This passage from al-Hawi al-Qudsi provides a concise ruling on how to purify different types of vessels. Vessels are categorized into three types: pottery/clay (khazaf), wood, and metals (iron, brass, etc.). Purification methods are four: burning (for porous new pottery where impurity seeped in), scraping (for new wood), wiping (for smooth metal), and washing (for all old vessels or rough surfaces). The key distinction is based on the material and whether the vessel is new (porous) or old (saturated). This is a practical classification for hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الخزف (al-khazaf): Fired clay pottery or earthenware.
النحت (al-nahth): Scraping off the surface layer to remove impurity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The purification method for a vessel depends on its material and whether it is new or old, smooth or rough, with burning, scraping, wiping, and washing as the four prescribed methods.

The Three Imams' Positions on Purifying Absorbed Impurities
Lays out the three imams' positions on absorbed impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on purifying items that have absorbed impurity, and identify which view is the mufta bihi for different cases.

Core Idea
Absorbed impurity divides the Hanafi school: Muhammad denies purification, Abu Yusuf allows it with washing, Abu Hanifa splits based on the source.

When impure liquid penetrates a solid object, does it ever become pure? The Hanafi imams gave three distinct answers. This lesson lays out their foundational disagreement and its practical consequences for everyday items like pottery, wood, and wheat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the item category
Determine whether the item is non-absorbent (e.g., mirror, stone, mat) or absorbent (e.g., new pottery, wood, wheat, leather). Non-absorbent items are purified by wiping; absorbent items require washing and drying.
The text explicitly distinguishes 'first' (absorbent) from non-absorbent.
2
Recall each imam's ruling for absorbent items
Muhammad says never purified. Abu Yusuf says can be purified by washing three times and drying each time. Abu Hanifa agrees with Abu Yusuf for items like wheat swollen in impurity, but for items cooked in wine he rules they never purify.
The text gives examples: new pottery, wood, papyrus, leather tanned with impure substance.
3
Identify the mufta bihi for each scenario
For wine-cooked items, Abu Hanifa's view (never purifies) is the fatwa. For items like the knife coated with impure water, Abu Yusuf's view (purification by tamwih) is the fatwa.
The text explicitly says 'wa bihi yufata' for Abu Hanifa on wine, and 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' for Abu Yusuf on tamwih.
4
Apply to a new case
Given a scenario (e.g., bread kneaded with wine), determine which imam's ruling applies and what the operative fatwa would be. Use the principle that the source of impurity and degree of absorption matter.
Bread kneaded with wine: according to the text, washing alone does not purify; only adding vinegar to remove traces works.

And in al-Mujtaba, attributed to Salat al-Baqqali: The mat (hasir) is purified by wiping like a mirror and a stone. As for the first—I mean that into which the parts of impurity penetrate—it is never purified according to Muhammad, and is purified according to Abu Yusuf, like a new piece of pottery, a new piece of wood, papyrus, leather tanned with impure substance, and wheat that has swollen from impurity. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is washed three times and dried each time as we mentioned, and it is said only the last time. The knife coated (mumawwah) with impure water is coated three times with pure water. Meat into whose broth impurity fell while boiling is boiled three times and becomes purified; it is said it does not become apparent. In the non-boiling state, it is washed three times. Thus in al-Zahiriyyah. The broth is not good unless that impurity is wine, for if vinegar is poured into it until it becomes sour like vinegar, it purifies it. And in al-Tanjis: Wheat cooked in wine—Abu Yusuf said: it is cooked with water three times and dried each time, and similarly meat. Abu Hanifa said: if cooked in wine, it never becomes purified, and this is the fatwa. End. And everything according to Muhammad never becomes purified. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If wine is poured into a pot containing meat, if before boiling it purifies the meat by washing three times; if after boiling, it does not purify. And it is said it is boiled three times, each time with pure water, and dried each time, and its drying is by cooling. Bread kneaded with wine is not purified by washing. And if vinegar is poured into it and its trace goes away, it purifies. Impure oil is purified by washing three times, and its stratagem is to pour water on it so the oil rises; thus do three times. A woman cooking broth whose drunken husband poured wine into it—the woman poured vinegar into it; if the broth becomes like vinegar in sourness, it becomes purified. A chicken roasted from whose stomach some grains emerge—the place of the grains becomes impure and its purification is to cook and cool it each time three times with pure water; similarly, dung if found in a roasted lamb. End. What is in al-Zahiriyyah. And in Fath al-Qadir: If a chicken is thrown into water while boiling before its belly is split, or a stomach before washing, it never becomes purified; but according to Abu Yusuf, it must be purified according to the earlier rule regarding meat. I say: And Allah knows best. It is reasoned by their absorption of the penetrated impurity through boiling. On this, it is famous that the meat called samit in Egypt is impure and not purified; but the mentioned cause is not established until the water reaches the boiling point as earlier. And the fruit of that appears in the burden of prayer. As for use and other than it, if it is washed after coating with impurity three times, even consecutively, then watermelon or other is cut with it, the cut thing does not become impure; and similarly if it falls into a little water or other, it does not make it impure, as with henna and the like as passed. As for prayer with it, if it is before coating three times with pure water, his prayer is not valid by agreement; and if after, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf. For washing purifies its exterior by consensus, and coating (tamwih) purifies its interior also according to Abu Yusuf, and that is the fatwa; rather, if it were said that coating suffices because fire removes the parts of impurity entirely then pure water replaces them, but repetition removes doubt from the origin. His statement: (And if) wine is poured into a pot containing meat etc. Al-Khayr al-Ramli said: It is understood from this and from the earlier meat that fell into impure broth that the ruling differs between when it is cooked with wine and when it fell into broth once? would have an aspect.
Source pages p. 415

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a detailed intra-madhhab discussion on purifying items that have absorbed impurities. The text first distinguishes between items that can be purified by wiping (like a mat, mirror, stone) and those into which impurity penetrates. For the latter, Imam Muhammad holds that such items never become purified, while Imam Abu Yusuf maintains purification is possible—using examples like new pottery, wood, and papyrus. For items like wheat that have swollen with impurity, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf agree on washing three times with drying each time. The discussion then moves to specific cases: a knife coated with impure water requires three coatings with pure water; meat that falls into impure broth while boiling is boiled three times to purify (but not if not boiling—then washed three times). The ruling on broth depends on whether the impurity is wine—if vinegar turns it sour, it becomes pure. A key dispute arises regarding cooking with wine: Abu Yusuf says cooking with water three times purifies wheat or meat, while Abu Hanifa says it never purifies (and this is the fatwa). Imam Muhammad says nothing purifies. Later cases include pouring wine into a pot with meat (different rulings before/after boiling), bread kneaded with wine (not purified by washing alone, only if vinegar removes its traces), impure oil (purified by washing three times with a stratagem), and a chicken whose stomach contents become impure (purified by cooking and cooling three times). The passage also discusses the concept of 'tamwih' (coating) and its effectiveness: according to Abu Yusuf, coating with pure water after impurity purifies both exterior and interior, and this is the relied-upon position. The overall principle is that purification depends on whether the item absorbs impurity, the presence of boiling, and the nature of the impurity.

Key Terms
تمويه (tamwīh): Coating or glazing a surface with water; here, coating a knife with pure water after impurity.
تشرب (tasharrub): The penetration and absorption of impurity into the substance of an item.
السميط (al-samīṭ): A type of meat (possibly roasted) that is not fully cooked through boiling; here, meat that is boiled briefly so only the surface is affected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on wheat cooked in wine according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) It can be purified by cooking with water three times.
B) It never becomes purified.
C) It is purified by drying only.
D) It is purified if vinegar is added.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has three positions on purifying absorbed impurities; the mufta bihi depends on whether the impurity is wine-cooked (Abu Hanifa) or other absorbed cases (Abu Yusuf).

Purification of Non-Squeezable Items: Absorbent vs. Non-Absorbent
Refinement of non-squeezable purification with absorbency distinction and three-water impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi classification of non-squeezable items (absorbent vs. non-absorbent) and state the required purification method for each, including the role of drying and the impurity status of successive wash-waters.

Core Idea
Non-squeezable items that absorb impurity require drying; those that do not absorb do not need drying after three washes.

In this passage, the commentator refines a general ruling from the matn by introducing a critical distinction among non-squeezable items: those that absorb impurity (like meat) and those that do not (like certain leathers). The method of purification differs accordingly. Additionally, the passage clarifies that the three wash-waters themselves become impure to varying degrees—a nuance that affects subsequent purification. Understanding this refinement prevents overgeneralization and ensures correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish non-squeezable items by absorbency
Identify the two categories from al-Muhit: (1) items that do not absorb impurity (e.g., wood that does not soak) and (2) items that do absorb impurity (e.g., meat left in hot water only briefly, where impurity penetrates).
Non-squeezable means the item cannot be wrung out, but it may still absorb liquid through pores.
2
Determine the purification method for each category
For non-absorbent items: wash three times without drying. For absorbent items: wash three times and then dry (tajfif) because drying helps remove the embedded impurity.
Drying is not required for non-absorbent items as impurity stays on the surface and three washes suffice.
3
Analyze the three waters' impurity levels
The first wash-water that touches the object is najis (impure). If it then splashes onto another object, that object needs three washes to become pure. The second wash-water is less impure: it can purify another object with two washes. The third is least impure: it purifies with one wash.
This cascading effect shows that each successive water carries less residual impurity.
4
Apply the rule to garments washed in sequence
If a garment is washed with water that was used to wash another impure garment, the ruling for the second garment mirrors that for the first regarding the number of washes needed.
The same cascading applies: first garment after its wash, second garment requires fewer washes.
5
Note the ruling on istinja' water
If one performs istinja' with water three times, the water becomes impure (najis). However, if water is used after the area is already clean (after removing impurity), that water becomes musta'mal (used) – pure but not purifying.
This distinguishes between removing active impurity and rinsing a clean area.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر وسن الاستنجاء بنجو حجر منق وما سن فيه عدد وغسله بالماء ويمكث فيه اللحم بعد ذلك زماناً يقع في مثله التشرب والدخول في باطن اللحم، وكل من الأمرين غير متحقق في السميط الواقع حيث لا يصل الماء إلى حد الغليان ولا يترك فيه إلا مقدار ما تصل الحرارة إلى سطح الجلد فتنحل مسام السطح من الصوف، بل ذلك الترك يمنع من وجوده انقلاع الشعر فالأولى في السميط أن يطهر بالغسل ثلاثاً لتنجس سطح الجلد بذلك الماء فإنهم لا يحترسون فيه من المنجس، وقد قال شرف الأئمة بهذا في الدجاجة والكرش والسميط مثلهما اهـ. واعلم أن صاحب المحيط فصل فيما لا ينعصر بين ما لا يتشرب فيه النجس وما يتشرب، فالأول يطهر بالغسل ثلاثاً من غير تجفيف والثاني يحتاج إلى التجفيف، وبهذا علم المتن ليس على عمومه كما لا يخفى وفيه أيضاً والمياه الثلاث نجسة متفاوته، فالأول إذا أصاب شيئاً يطهر بالثلاث، والثاني بالمثنى والثالث بالواحد ويكون حكمه في الثوب الثاني مثل حكمه في الأول. وإذا استنجى بالماء ثلاثاً كان نجساً وإن استعمل الماء بعد الإنقاء صار مستعملاً.
Drying for what does not squeeze out, and the sunna of istinja' with a stone that retains water, and what is sunna therein regarding number and washing it with water. And the meat stays therein after that for a time in which like absorption and entry into the interior of the meat occurs, and neither of the two matters is actualized in the actual samit where the water does not reach the boiling point and it is left only for the amount that heat reaches the skin's surface, so the pores of the surface of the wool dissolve; rather, that leaving prevents the occurrence of hair removal, so the better (al-awla) regarding samit is that it is purified by washing three times because the skin's surface is impure with that water, for they do not guard against impurity therein. And Sharf al-A'imma has said this regarding chicken, stomach, and samit is like them. End. And know that the author of al-Muhit classified among what does not squeeze out between what does not absorb impurity and what does absorb: the first is purified by washing three times without drying; the second requires drying. And by this it is known that the matn is not general, as is not hidden. And in it also: the three waters are impure, varying. So the first (water) when it touches something, it is purified by three (washes); the second by two; the third by one. And its ruling regarding the second garment is like its ruling regarding the first. And if one performs istinja' with water three times, it is impure; and if one uses water after cleaning, it becomes used (musta'mal).

Commentary
Page 416 continues with a refinement of the earlier general ruling from the matn. The commentator explains that the rule of drying (jafaf) applies specifically to items that do not squeeze out water when wrung. He then discusses the case of 'samit' meat: since it is only briefly exposed to heat, the impurity does not fully penetrate, so it can be purified by washing three times without drying. This is the view of Sharf al-A'imma. The passage then cites al-Muhit's distinction among non-squeezable items: those that do not absorb impurity (purified by washing three times without drying) and those that do (require drying). This shows the matn is not absolute. Additionally, the three wash-waters themselves become impure to varying degrees: the first is most impure and can purify an object only after three washes; the second purifies with two; the third with one. The same applies to garments washed in succession. The text ends with a note on istinja': washing three times with water renders the water impure, and if water is used after cleaning, it becomes musta'mal (used water, which is pure but not purifying).

Key Terms
لا ينعصر (lā yanʿaṣir): Items that do not release water when squeezed, like leather, wood, or meat that has been boiled.
المياه الثلاث (al-miyāh al-thalāth): The three successive wash-waters used to purify an impure object; each becomes impure to a different degree.
مستعمل (mustaʿmal): Water that has been used for worship (like istinja') after the impurity is removed; it is pure but not purifying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Non-squeezable items are classified by absorbency: non-absorbent require three washes without drying, absorbent require three washes with drying.
