Ruling on Istinja': Sunna Acts and Method
Defines istinja', lists its sunna acts, and discusses water purification after use.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istinja' according to the Hanafi school, identify its sunna acts, and distinguish between valid and invalid uses of water after istinja'.

Core Idea
Istinja' is sunna only for tangible impurity; wind does not trigger it.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author defines istinja' — the removal of impurity from the private parts — and clarifies that it is a sunna act, not obligatory. Understanding when istinja' applies and the status of the water used is crucial for proper taharah. Let's break down the definition and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Find the definition of istinja' in the text. What does it involve? Wiping or washing?
2
Determine the triggering event
According to the passage, istinja' is sunna only for tangible impurity from the two passages, not for wind. Why is it bid'a for wind?
Because no impurity remains on the passage.
3
Classify the ruling
The passage states the sunna acts of istinja'. What is the hukm level? Is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
It is sunnah muakkadah.
4
Analyze the water usage
The text discusses water used after cleaning (musta'mal). What is its ruling? Does it become pure or not?
Musta'mal water is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr mutahhir).
5
Resolve the gravel objection
The passage addresses an exception: gravel exiting the passage. Does it require istinja'? The text clarifies that if no impurity accompanies it, istinja' is not sunna.
This shows the precise scope of the ruling.

And if one performs istinja' with water three times, it is impure; and if one uses water after cleaning, it becomes musta'mal. His statement: (And sunna is istinja' with something like a stone that retains water) - he mentioned it here and did not mention it in the sunan of wudu', because istinja' is removal of tangible impurity, and it is removal of what is on the passage of impurity. And not from sleep or phlebotomy - to that he pointed in Sharh al-Wiqaya, but is countered by gravel exiting from one of the two passages, for it enters under its rule, while the situation is that istinja' is not sunna for it; declared in al-Siraj: impure, so reflect on that. Reflect. End. Thus, the first basin (ijana) is not purified except by washing three times, the second basin by two times, the third basin by one time. But in it also with the code of Shihab al-A'imma al-Imami: Washing the impure garment in the basin, so he washes the basin three times each time after wringing the garment. And in it also: 'Abd al-Rahim al-Khantanī said: The apparent of what is indicated in al-Jami' is that there is no need to wash the basin, like the rope and bucket in drawing water from a well. End. His statement: 'But is countered by gravel...' - It is not hidden from you its refutation, for the statement of al-Siraj that istinja' is not sunna for it because nothing is emitted with it that is to be removed, so it did not enter under its rule. Yes, it is countered by the definition of al-Maghrib. His statement: (And if something...) i.e., if there is something on the exit, and his statement: it is from the chapter of removal of real impurity in meaning, and for this, if he said 'and if'...
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines istinja' and clarifies its sunna nature. Istinja' is defined as removing the impurity (najw) that exits from the belly or private parts, either by wiping or washing. The sin in 'istinja' may denote seeking (talab). Importantly, istinja' is sunna only when something solid (like stool) exits, not for wind, as wind leaves no trace. Making istinja' for wind is bid'a. Sleep or phlebotomy do not require it either. A potential objection regarding gravel (hasah) exiting is addressed: if gravel comes out alone without impurity, istinja' is not sunna; if accompanied by impurity, the istinja' is for the impurity, not the gravel. The passage also discusses the three wash-waters and their purification power: the first basin used for washing an impure garment must itself be washed thrice, the second twice, the third once. However, some scholars (like 'Abd al-Rahim al-Khantanī) hold that the basin need not be washed, akin to the bucket and rope in well purification. The text ends by warning of an error in al-Bahr regarding this issue and points to a refined understanding from al-Nahr.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinjāʾ): Removing impurity (najw) that exits from the belly or private parts, either by wiping with a solid object or washing with water.
النجو (al-najw): The impurity that exits from the belly (i.e., feces and possibly urine).
مستعمل (mustaʿmal): Water that has been used for istinja' after the impurity is removed; it is pure (tahir) but not purifying (ghayr mutahhir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
Istinja' is a sunna act for tangible impurity from the two passages; the water used becomes musta'mal (pure but not purifying).

Purification of Non-Squeezable Items: When Drying is Required
Explains the ruling on drying non-squeezable items, with specific application to samit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between non-squeezable items that require drying for purification and those that do not, and apply the Hanafi ruling for samit.

Core Idea
Purification by drying is required only when the impurity penetrates; otherwise, washing suffices.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on purifying items that do not squeeze out liquid. While the matn states that drying is the method for such items, the commentator explains that this is not absolute: if the impurity does not penetrate, washing three times is sufficient, as in the case of samit. The differentiation is based on the reasoning (talil) of penetration versus non-penetration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
The matn states that drying is the method of purification for items that do not squeeze out liquid. This is the starting point.
The matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Note the exception for samit
Samit is a type of meat where the skin is scalded but water does not penetrate. The commentator says it is purified by washing three times without drying, based on Sharaf al-A'imma's statement.
Samit is prepared by dipping in hot water until hair comes off, but water does not reach the interior.
3
Understand the reasoning
The impurity does not penetrate into the samit; it only contaminates the surface. Therefore, washing removes the impurity and drying is unnecessary.
This is a talil (reasoning by cause).
4
Apply the broader principle from al-Muhit
Al-Muhit differentiates: if the impurity does not penetrate, wash three times without drying; if it penetrates, drying is required.
This shows that the matn's generality is limited.
5
Conclude the correct ruling
For any non-squeezable item, determine whether the impurity penetrates. If it does not, washing three times suffices; if it does, drying must be added.
This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling) as per the explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر وسن الاستنجاء بنحو حجر منق وما سن فيه عدد وغسله بالماء ويمكث فيه اللحم بعد ذلك زماناً يقع في مثله التشرب والدخول في باطن اللحم، وكل من الأمرين غير متحقق في السميط الواقع حيث لا يصل الماء إلى حد الغليان ولا يترك فيه إلا مقدار ما تصل الحرارة إلى سطح الجلد فتنحل مسام السطح من الصوف، بل ذلك الترك يمنع من وجوده انقلاع الشعر فالأولى في السميط أن يطهر بالغسل ثلاثاً لتنجس سطح الجلد بذلك الماء فإنهم لا يحترسون فيه من المنجس، وقد قال شرف الأئمة بهذا في الدجاجة والكرش والسميط مثلهما اهـ. واعلم أن صاحب المحيط فصل فيما لا ينعصر بين ما لا يتشرب فيه النجس وما يتشرب، فالأول يطهر بالغسل ثلاثاً من غير تجفيف والثاني يحتاج إلى التجفيف، وبهذا علم المتن ليس على عمومه كما لا يخفى
Drying for what does not squeeze out, and the sunnah of istinja with a porous stone and what is sunnah its number and washing with water. And the meat remains in it for a time in which such absorption and entry into the interior of the meat occurs, and both matters are not verified in the samit that occurs where water does not reach the boiling point and is not left except for a duration that heat reaches the surface of the skin so the pores of the surface of the wool dissolve, rather that leaving prevents the sprouting of hair, so the preferred in samit is that it is purified by washing three times due to the impurity of the surface of the skin with that water as they do not guard against the impure. And Sharaf al-A'imma said this regarding the chicken, stomach, and samit is like them. And know that the author of al-Muhit differentiated regarding what does not squeeze out between what the impurity does not penetrate and what it penetrates: the first is purified by washing three times without drying, and the second requires drying. And by this it is known that the matn is not general, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn phrase 'الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر' (drying for non-squeezable items). The author discusses the ruling for samit, a type of lightly cooked meat where the water does not penetrate deeply. Since the impurity only contaminates the surface, it is sufficient to wash three times without needing to dry. This is based on the statement of Sharaf al-A'imma that the same applies to chicken and stomach. However, al-Muhit differentiates: if the impurity does not penetrate, washing three times is enough; if it does penetrate, drying is required. This shows that the matn's general ruling about drying is not absolute.

Key Terms
جفاف (jafāf): Drying as a method of purification for items that do not squeeze out liquid.
سميط (samīṭ): A type of meat preparation where the animal is scalded in hot water to remove hair, but the water does not penetrate deeply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Washing three times without drying
B) Drying only
C) Washing once
D) Drying and then washing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on purifying non-squeezable items is not monolithic; it depends on whether the impurity penetrates—if not, washing suffices; if yes, drying is added.

The Three Ranks of Impure Water in Purification
States the rules for the three ranks of impure water and their effect on items washed in them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three ranks of impure water and determine how many washes each requires to purify an item.

Core Idea
Three successive washes: first water najis requires three, second requires two, third requires one.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text introduces a practical classification of waters used in washing impure items. It teaches that not all wash waters are equal; each successive wash has a lower degree of impurity. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly purifying garments and other objects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three waters
The first, second, and third water used to wash an impure item are classified with decreasing impurity.
2
Note the number of washes each requires
The first water requires three washes to purify, the second requires two, and the third requires one.
These washes refer to the number of times the item must be washed with that particular water.
3
Apply the same rule to subsequent garments
If a second garment is washed with the same waters, the ruling is identical: first water requires three washes, etc.
4
Understand the istinja and used water rule
Water used for istinja three times becomes impure. If water is used after the area is clean, it becomes musta'mal (used water) and is no longer suitable for purification.
This is a separate ruling from the three-wash rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيه أيضاً والمياه الثلاث نجسة متفاوته، فالأول إذا أصاب شيئاً يطهر بالثلاث، والثاني بالمثنى والثالث بالواحد ويكون حكمه في الثوب الثاني مثل حكمه في الأول. وإذا استنجى بالماء ثلاثاً كان نجساً وإن استعمل الماء بعد الإنقاء صار مستعملاً.
And in it also: The three waters are impure with varying degree. So the first, if it touches something, it is purified by three (washes), the second by two, the third by one; and its ruling in the second garment is like its ruling in the first. And if one performs istinja with water three times, it becomes impure, and if one uses water after cleanliness, it becomes used water.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage presents a rule about three successive waters used in washing an impure item. The first water is considered najis and requires three washes to purify the item; the second water is less impure and requires two washes; the third requires one. The rule applies similarly to subsequent garments. Additionally, if water is used for istinja three times, it becomes impure. Once the area is clean, using additional water makes that water 'used' (musta'mal) for purification purposes.

Key Terms
المياه الثلاث (al-miyāh al-thalāth): Three successive waters used in washing an impure item, each with a decreasing degree of impurity.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification and is no longer valid for further purification.
استنجى (istinjā): The act of cleaning the private parts with water after using the toilet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Three
B) Two
C) One
D) None

Key Takeaway
The first of the three waters is the most impure and requires three washes; each subsequent water is less impure and requires fewer washes.

Istinja is Sunnah Mu'akkadah, Not Fard
Corrects a previous categorization of istinja into fard and sunnah types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of istinja and explain why the five-type division in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is incorrect.

Core Idea
Istinja is only sunnah mu'akkadah; it is never fard.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the legal ruling of istinja (cleaning the private parts after relieving oneself). He affirms that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and not an obligatory act (fard). He then corrects a mistaken categorization found in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that divides istinja into five types—four fard and one sunnah. The correction shows that three of the claimed fard categories are actually acts of ghusl (removing ritual impurity) or general removal of najasah, not istinja, and the only genuine istinja is the sunnah category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling of Istinja
Determine the legal classification of istinja in the Hanafi school as stated in the text: it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard.
The text explicitly says 'لا يكون إلا سنة' (it is only sunnah) and 'سنة مؤكدة' (confirmed sunnah).
2
Recall the Five-Type Division from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj
Summarize the five categories claimed: (1) from menses, (2) from postpartum bleeding, (3) from janabah, (4) when impurity exceeds the outlet, (5) sunnah when impurity is within the outlet.
The first four were claimed as fard, the fifth as sunnah.
3
Analyze Why Categories 1-3 Are Not Istinja
Understand that the first three (menses, postpartum, janabah) involve ghusl (removal of hadath), not istinja. If there is actual physical impurity (najasah) on the body, that is removal of impurity from the body, not from the passages specifically.
Ghusl removes ritual impurity; istinja concerns only the two passages.
4
Analyze Category 4: Impurity Exceeding the Outlet
When impurity spreads beyond the outlet, cleaning it becomes removal of najasah from the body (a fard act for prayer), but this is not istinja because it is not limited to the two passages.
Thus, it is a general obligation, not a specific category of istinja.
5
Conclude: Only the Sunnah Category Remains
Since the first four categories fall under other acts (ghusl or general impurity removal), the only act that qualifies as istinja is the fifth—when impurity is confined to the outlet—and that is sunnah mu'akkadah.
Therefore, all istinja is sunnah; there is no fard istinja.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفاد أن الاستنجاء لا يكون إلا سنة وصرح في النهاية بأنه سنة مؤكدة فلا يكون فرضاً. وعلى هذا فما ذكر في السراج الوهاج من أن الاستنجاء خمسة أنواع : أربعة فريضة و واحد سنة فالأول من الحيض والنفاس والجنابة وإذا تجاوزت النجاسة مخرجها، وواحد سنة وهو ما إذا كانت النجاسة مقدار المخرج فتسامح فإن الثلاثة الأول من باب إزالة الحدث إن لم يكن شيء على المخرج، وإن كان شيء فهو من باب إزالة النجاسة الحقيقية من البدن غير السبيلين فلا يكون من باب الاستنجاء وإن كان على أحد السبيلين شيء فهي سنة لا فرض . وأما الرابع فهو من باب إزالة النجاسة عن البدن، وقد علمت أنه ليس من باب الاستنجاء فلم يبق إلا القسم المسنون.
And he indicated that istinja is only sunnah, and he explicitly stated in al-Nihayah that it is a confirmed sunnah, so it is not fard. Based on this, what is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that istinja is five types: four fard and one sunnah; the first (fard) from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, sexual impurity, and when impurity exceeds the outlet; and one sunnah which is when the impurity is within the area of the outlet — is lenient. So the first three are from removal of hadath if there is nothing on the outlet, and if there is something, it is from removal of true impurity from the body other than the two passages, so it is not from istinja; and if there is something on one of the two passages, it is sunnah, not fard. As for the fourth, it is from removal of impurity from the body, and you know it is not from istinja. So nothing remains except the sunnah category.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a ruling clarification. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq has already stated that istinja is only sunnah, and al-Nihayah explicitly says it is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard. The passage then corrects a mistaken categorization found in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, which claimed that istinja comprises five types: four fard and one sunnah. The alleged fard types are: (1) from menses, (2) from postpartum bleeding, (3) from janabah, and (4) when impurity exceeds the outlet. However, the first three are actually acts of ghusl (removal of ritual impurity/hadath), not istinja. If there is actual physical impurity on the body, that is removal of najasah, not istinja. Only the fifth type—when impurity is confined to the outlet—is genuinely istinja, and it is sunnah. Thus, the only correct category for istinja is sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
استنجاء (istinja): Cleaning the two passages (front and back) after relieving oneself, typically with stones or water.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A regularly performed act of the Prophet that one is encouraged to maintain; omitting it is disliked but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of istinja?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah Mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Istinja is exclusively sunnah mu'akkadah; any claim that it is fard confuses it with ghusl or general impurity removal.

Etiquettes of Istinja: Inqa' and Istibra'
Definition and rulings on istinja etiquettes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of istinja (inqa'), state the ruling of istibra', and apply the etiquettes for istinja according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Istibra' is wajib; the goal of istinja is thorough cleanliness (inqa'), not a specific posture.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the fundamental objective of istinja: complete removal of impurity (inqa'). It emphasizes that no particular posture or method is required—only effectiveness. The text also establishes the ruling of istibra' (ensuring the urine stream has ceased) as wajib, and provides practical etiquettes for performing istinja correctly, including considerations for fasting individuals and those troubled by waswasa.

Guided Path
1
Define the goal of istinja
Recognize that the primary purpose is inqa' (complete cleanliness). The passage states that no specific posture (like facing the stone in winter) is mandated; rather, one should choose the most effective method to achieve cleanliness.
This is a key point: flexibility is allowed as long as the impurity is fully removed.
2
Determine the ruling of istibra'
Note that istibra' (ensuring no urine remains) is explicitly stated as wajib in al-Mubtagha. This sets the Hanafi position apart from schools that consider it merely recommended.
Wajib means omission is sinful and requires compensation if possible.
3
List the etiquettes of istinja
Identify the mustahabb (recommended) practices: sitting completely relaxed, drying the area before standing, protecting clothing from used water, washing hands before and after, taking steps before starting, and using cold water in winter after removal.
These are sunnah, not obligatory.
4
Address the issue of waswasa (whispers)
Understand the Hanafi advice: if Satan makes one doubtful about impurity, one should not pay attention but sprinkle water on the private part or trousers. Then any doubt is attributed to the sprinkling unless certainty of impurity arises.
This is a practical solution to prevent obsessive doubts from invalidating wudu.
5
Apply gender considerations
Note that the same rules apply to women: they wash what is visible, and using the palm suffices. A woman must not insert her finger into the vagina for istinja.
The prohibition of finger insertion applies to both genders to avoid harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله منق) إلى أن المقصود هو الإنقاء وإلى أنه لا حاجة إلى التقييد بكيفية من المذكورة في الكتب نحو إقباله بالحجر في الشتاء وإدباره به في الصيف لاسترخاء الخصيتين فيه لا في الشتاء. وفي المجتبى المقصود الإنقاء فيختار ما هو الأبلغ والأسلم عن زيادة التلويث .اهـ. فالأولى أن يقعد مسترخياً كل الاسترخاء إلا أن يكون صائماً وكان الاستنجاء بالماء، ولا يتنفس إذا كان صائماً ويحترز من دخول الاصبع المبتلة كل ذلك يفسد الصوم. وفي كتاب الصوم من الخلاصة : إنما يفسد إذا وصل إلى موضع المحقنة وقلما يكون ذلك اهـ. وللمخافة ينبغي أن ينشف المحل قبل أن يقوم، ويستحب لغير الصائم أيضاً حفظ الثوب من الماء المستعمل ويغسل يديه قبل الاستنجاء وبعده، وينبغي أن يخطو قبله خطوات والمقصود أن يستبرىء. وفي المبتغى والاستبراء ،واجب ولو عرض له الشيطان كثيراً لا يلتفت إليه بل ينضح فرجه بماء أو سراويله حتى إذا شك حمل البلل على ذلك النضح ما لم يتيقن خلافه، وبالماء البادرد في الشتاء أفضل بعد تحقق الإزالة به. ولا يدخل الأصبع قيل يورث الباسور، والمرأة كالرجل تغسل ما ظهر منها ، ولو غسلت المرأة براحتها كفاها. كذا في فتح القدير. ولا تدخل المرأة أصبعها في قبلها للاستنجاء كما في الخانية.
And he indicated by his saying 'minq' (cleansing) that the intended purpose is cleanliness, and that there is no need to restrict it to a specific manner mentioned in books, such as facing the stone in winter and turning away from it in summer due to the relaxation of the testicles in winter but not in summer. In al-Mujtaba: the intended purpose is cleanliness, so one should choose what is most effective and safest from increasing soiling. End. So it is best to sit completely relaxed unless one is fasting and istinja is with water, and he should not breathe if fasting, and should be careful not to insert the wet finger; all of that spoils the fast. In the Book of Fasting from al-Khulasa: it only spoils if it reaches the site of the enema, which rarely happens. End. And out of caution, he should dry the area before standing. And it is recommended even for a non-fasting person to protect the garment from used water, and to wash his hands before and after istinja. And he should take steps before it, and the purpose is istibra'. In al-Mubtagha: istibra' is wajib. And if Satan troubles him frequently, he should not pay attention, but rather sprinkle water on his private part or his trousers, so that if he doubts, he attributes the moisture to that sprinkling as long as he is not certain otherwise. And using cold water in winter is better after confirming removal with it. And he should not insert the finger; it is said it causes hemorrhoids. And the woman is like the man; she washes what is visible. If a woman washes with her palm, it suffices. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And a woman should not insert her finger into her vagina for istinja as mentioned in al-Khaniyyah.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling explanation. It first clarifies that the goal of istinja is inqa' – thorough cleanliness. Therefore, specific postures mentioned in some books (e.g., facing the stone in winter due to relaxation of the testicles) are not required; one should choose the most effective method. The text then gives practical etiquettes: sit fully relaxed, but if fasting and using water, avoid breathing and inserting wet finger as it may break the fast (the ruling is nuanced: it only breaks if water reaches deep inside). It is recommended to dry the area before standing and protect clothing from used water. Washing hands before and after istinja is recommended. One should take a few steps before starting, and the intention is istibra' (ensuring the urine stream has stopped). Istibra' is wajib. If one experiences frequent whispers (waswasa), he should not pay attention but sprinkle water on the area to resolve doubts. In winter, using cold water is better after removal of impurity. Inserting the finger is discouraged as it may cause hemorrhoids. Women also wash what is visible; using the palm suffices, and they should not insert the finger into the vagina.

Key Terms
إنقاء (inqa'): Complete removal of impurity from the area; the goal of istinja.
استبراء (istibra'): Ensuring that the urine stream has completely stopped before beginning istinja; it is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Sunnah Status of Istinja: Proof and Linguistic Nuance
Establishes the sunnah status of istinja using the hadith of Anas and linguistic analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istinja, explain the hadith evidence, and analyze the linguistic debate over 'kana yaf'al'.

Core Idea
Istinja is sunnah mu'akkadah; the proof is valid even if 'kana' does not imply repetition.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that istinja is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation. We analyze the hadith of Anas that serves as proof and address a key linguistic point: does the phrase 'kana yaf'al' indicate habitual action? Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly deriving the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
State the Hanafi hukm for istinja: sunnah mu'akkadah. Note that omission does not invalidate prayer because small impurity is excused.
The ruling is found in the source text explicitly.
2
Understand the consequence of omission
If a person omits istinja, the prayer is still valid. The source explains that a small amount of impurity (najasah qalilah) is overlooked (afw) in the Hanafi school.
Distinguish between impurity on the exit (not disliked) and elsewhere (disliked).
3
Examine the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Anas (muttafaq alayh): the Prophet used water for istinja. This is a zanni thubut and dalala proof.
The hadith is quoted in the source: 'kana Rasulullah … yastanji bil-ma'.
4
Analyze the linguistic argument
The phrase 'kana yaf'al' is debated. The chosen Hanafi view is that 'kana' does not entail repetition; it only indicates occurrence. Evidence is given from 'A'ishah's statement used for a single event.
Al-Nawawi and al-Muhaqqiq support this view.
5
Apply the principle
Despite the linguistic nuance, the hadith still proves the Prophet's practice, establishing it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
The regularity is inferred from usage and context, not from the word itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأراد المصنف بالسنة السنة المؤكدة كما هو مذكور في الأصل، ولو تركه صحت صلاته قال في الخلاصة : بناء على أن النجاسة القليلة عفو عندنا وعلماؤنا فصلوا بين النجاسة التي على موضع الحدث والتي على غيره في غير موضع الحدث إذا تركها يكره، وفي موضعه إذا تركها لا يكره، وما عن أنس كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يدخل الخلاء فأحمل أنا وغلام نحوي إداوة من ماء وعنزة فيستنجي بالماء. متفق عليه . ظاهر في المواظبة بالماء ومقتضاه كراهة تركه . كذا في فتح القدير. وهو مبني على أن صيغة كان يفعل مفيدة للتكرار وفيه خلاف بين الأصوليين والمختار الذي عليه الأكثرون والمحققون من الأصوليين أن لفظة كان لا يلزم منها الدوام ولا التكرار وإنما هي فعل ماض تدل على وقوعه فإن دل دليل على التكرار عمل به وإلا فلا تقتضيه بوضعها، وقد قالت عائشة رضي الله عنها ؛ كنت أطيب رسول الله الحله قبل أن يطوف، ومعلوم أنه لم يحج بعد صحبته عائشة إلا حجة واحدة وهي حجة الوداع فاستعملت كان في مرة واحدة، ولا يقال لعلها طيبته في إحرامه لأن المعتمر لا يحل له التطيب قبل الطواف بالإجماع فثبت أنها استعملت «كان» في مرة واحدة كما قال الأصوليون ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم من باب الوتر، واختاره المحقق في التحرير فإنه اختار أن إفادتها للتكرار من جهة الاستعمال لا من الوضع لكن الاستعمال مختلف كما رأيت.
And the author intended by 'sunnah' the confirmed sunnah as mentioned in the original text. If one omits it, his prayer is valid. He said in al-Khulasa: based on the fact that a small amount of impurity is overlooked (afw) in our school; and our scholars distinguished between impurity on the place of the event (exit) and elsewhere: if left on a place other than the exit, it is disliked; if left on the exit, it is not disliked. And what is narrated from Anas: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to enter the lavatory, and I and a young boy would carry a small water skin and a pointed stick, and he would perform istinja with water' – agreed upon. This is apparent in his regularity with water, and its requirement is the dislike of leaving it. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And this is based on the proposition that the form 'kana yaf'al' indicates repetition, and there is disagreement among usuliyyun. The chosen view, held by the majority and the verifying scholars among the usuliyyun, is that the word 'kana' does not entail continuity or repetition; it is simply a past tense indicating its occurrence. If evidence indicates repetition, it is acted upon; otherwise, it does not require it by its linguistic coinage. Indeed, 'A'ishah said: 'I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah ﷺ for his ihram before he performed tawaf' and it is known that he did not perform Hajj after marrying 'A'ishah except one Hajj – the Farewell Pilgrimage – so she used 'kana' for a single occurrence. It cannot be said that perhaps she perfumed him during his 'umrah because the mu'tamir is not allowed to apply perfume before tawaf by consensus. So it is established that she used 'kana' for a single occurrence, as the usuliyyun said. Al-Nawawi mentioned this in his commentary on Muslim in the chapter of witr, and the researcher (al-Muhaqqiq) chose it in al-Tahrir, for he chose that its indication of repetition is from usage, not from linguistic coinage, but usage varies as you have seen.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It reaffirms that istinja is sunnah mu'akkadah, and if one omits it, the prayer is still valid because a small amount of impurity (najasah qalilah) is excused (afw) in the Hanafi school. However, leaving impurity on the exit is not disliked, while on other areas it is disliked. The main proof is the hadith of Anas that the Prophet regularly used water for istinja. The author then addresses a linguistic argument: the phrase 'kana yaf'al' is taken by some to imply repetition, thus proving the Prophet's continuous practice. But the chosen opinion among usuliyyun is that 'kana' does not necessarily indicate repetition; it only confirms that the action occurred. Evidence is given from 'A'ishah's statement about perfuming the Prophet for Hajj, which happened only once. Therefore, the regularity is based on usage, not the word itself. Nonetheless, the hadith still establishes the practice as a sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; an act the Prophet regularly performed and emphasized.
كان يفعل (kana yaf'al): A grammatical form that some consider indicates habitual or repeated action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view of the usuliyyun mentioned, what does the word 'kana' in 'kana yaf'al' indicate?
A) Repetition and continuity
B) That the action occurred once
C) That the action occurred without specifying repetition
D) Obligation

Key Takeaway
Istinja is a confirmed sunnah; its proof rests on the Prophet's action, and the linguistic debate over 'kana yaf'al' does not weaken the ruling.

Condition of Inqa' and Valid Materials for Istinja
Specifies that inqa' is the goal and lists valid materials for istinja

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the necessity of inqa' and identify which materials are valid for istinja.

Core Idea
Inqa' is the sunnah goal of istinja, not a condition for validity; stones suffice if pure, removable, and valueless.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that achieving thorough cleanliness (inqa') is the goal of istinja, but its absence does not invalidate the purification. Rather, the sunnah is missed. It also specifies the materials that are valid for istinja: any pure, removable, valueless substance such as stones, clay, or wood. Glass, snow, and charcoal are excluded because they either have value or do not effectively clean.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of inqa'
Determine whether inqa' is a condition for validity or merely for fulfilling the sunnah. The text states that it is for the attainment of sunnah, not a condition for permissibility.
2
Recognize the scope of impurities
Note that the text leaves the impurity unrestricted, meaning both normal and abnormal impurities (like blood) can be purified with stones.
The correct view is that stones suffice even for dried stool, though there is a disagreement mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
3
Define valid materials
Understand that 'stones and the like' (nahw al-hajar) refers to any pure substance that effectively removes impurity and has no significant value.
4
List excluded materials
Identify the materials that are excluded: glass, snow, brick, pottery, and charcoal, because they are valuable or ineffective in cleaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد علم مما ذكرنا أن التقييد بالإنقاء إنما هو لحصول السنة حتى لو لم ينق فإن السنة قد فاتت لا أنه قيد للجواز. وأطلق الخارج ولم يقيده بكونه معتاداً ليفيد أن غير المعتاد إذا أصاب المحل كالدم يطهر بالحجارة على الصحيح، سواء كان خارجاً منه أو لا، وليفيد أنه لا فرق بين أن يكون الغائط رطباً ولم يقم من موضعه أو قام من موضعه أو جف الغائط فإن الحجر كاف فيه وفي الثاني خلاف ذكره في السراج الوهاج . وأراد بنحو الحجر ما كان عيناً طاهرة مزيلة لا قيمة له كالمدر والتراب والعود والخرقة والقطن والجلد الممتهن، فخرج الزجاج والثلج والآجر والخزف والفحم.
And it is known from what we have mentioned that the restriction of inqa' is only for the attainment of the sunnah; so if one does not achieve cleanliness, then the sunnah has been missed, not that it is a condition for permissibility. And he left the impurity absolute and did not restrict it to being normal (habitual) to indicate that an abnormal impurity, like blood, if it hits the area, is purified by stones on the correct view, whether it exited from him or not. And to indicate that there is no difference between the stool being wet and he has not stood up, or he has stood up, or the stool has dried: the stone is sufficient. In the second case, there is a disagreement mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And he intended by 'stones and the like' anything that is a clean substance that removes and has no value, such as clay, earth, wood, a rag, cotton, and worn-out leather. Thus, glass, snow, brick, pottery, and charcoal are excluded.
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage further clarifies the condition of inqa'. Achieving cleanliness (inqa') is necessary to fulfill the sunnah of istinja; if not achieved, the sunnah is missed, but the act of istinja is still permissible (the prayer is valid). The type of impurity is left unrestricted, covering both normal and abnormal impurities like blood. Stones suffice even if the stool is wet, dry, or after standing, though there is a dispute in some cases. The valid materials for istinja are those that are pure (tahir), can remove impurity, and have little or no value: e.g., clay, earth, wood, a rag, cotton, worn-out leather. Excluded are valuable or smooth materials like glass, snow, brick, pottery, and charcoal because they do not effectively clean or are impure.

Key Terms
إنقاء (inqa'): Thorough cleaning of the area; the goal of istinja.
نحو الحجر (nahw al-hajar): Stones and similar materials such as clay, earth, wood, rags, cotton, worn-out leather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid material for istinja according to this passage?
A) Glass
B) Clay
C) Charcoal
D) Snow

Key Takeaway
Inqa' is not a condition for validity but for sunnah; valid materials for istinja are pure, removable, and valueless substances like stones and clay.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Number of Stones and Water Preference in Istinja
Discusses the required number of stones and argues water is better than stones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of stones in istinja and explain why water is preferred over stones, including the thamarah al-khilaf with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The number of stones is not fixed; inqa' is the goal, and water is better because it removes impurity entirely.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles two related issues in istinja: the required number of stones and whether water is superior to stones. The Hanafi school argues that the number is not legislatively fixed—only recommended—while the Shafi'i school requires three stones as fard. The passage then defends the view that washing with water is more complete and therefore preferred. We will unpack the proofs, the counter-arguments, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
Recognize that the passage addresses (1) the number of stones and (2) the preference of water over stones. Each has its own evidence and implications.
The 'number' issue is a direct madhhab dispute; the 'water' issue includes a sub-discussion on impurity revival.
2
Analyze the dispute on number of stones
State the Hanafi position (no fixed number, inqa' is sufficient) and the Shafi'i position (three stones fard). Examine the Hanafi proofs: the hadith of two stones, and the interpretation of the three-stone hadith as customary or recommended.
Note that Ibn Hajar's objection is acknowledged but dismissed because the number is not an obligation.
3
Examine the preference for water
Understand the Hanafi argument: water removes impurity, stone only lightens. Therefore water is more appropriate. Then explore the sub-issue: if water touches a stone-cleaned area, does impurity return? The Hanafi view says no, by analogy with dry earth re-wetted.
The sub-issue is resolved by a general principle: once impurity is removed, it does not revive.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For the number issue: Shafi'i requires three stones even if inqa' is achieved with two; Hanafi validates with two if inqa' is achieved. For the water issue: Hanafi holds water as better but not obligatory; Shafi'i considers water fard if available.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that water is better and stones suffice if inqa' is achieved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وما سن فيه عدد أي في الاستنجاء لما قدمنا من أن المقصود إنما هو الإنقاء، وشرط الشافعي الثلاث مبني على أن الاستنجاء فرض ولا نقول به وذكر الثلاث في بعض الأحاديث خرج مخرج العادة لأن الغالب حصول الإنقاء بها، أو يحمل على الاستحباب بدليل أنه لو استنجى بحجر له ثلاثة أحرف جاز عندهم، وبدليل أنه لما أتى له عليه الصلاة والسلام بحجرين وروثة ألقى الروثة واقتصر على الحجرين كذا ذكر أئمتنا وتعقبه شيخ الإسلام ابن حجر في فتح الباري بأن الأمر أولاً بإتيان ثلاثة أحجار يغني عن طلب ثالث بعد إلقاء الروثة، وبأنه ورد في بعض الروايات الصحيحة أنه طلب منه ثالثاً وأتى له به. وبما قررناه علم أن المراد نفي السنة المؤكدة وإلا فقد صرحوا بالاستحباب كما قدمناه. قوله: (وغسله بالماء أحب) أي غسل المحل بالماء أفضل لأنه قالع للنجاسة والحجر مخفف لها فكان الماء أولى. كذا ذكره الشارح الزيلعي وهو ظاهر في أن المحل لم يطهر بالحجر، ويتفرع عليه أنه السبيل باصابة الماء وفيه الخلاف المعروف في مسألة الأرض إذا جفت بعد التنجس ثم أصابها ماء وكذا في نظائرها وقد اختاروا في الجميع عدم عود النجاسة كما قدمناه عنهم فليكن كذلك هنا. ويدل على ذلك من السنة ما رواه الدارقطني وصححه عن أبي هريرة أنه نهى
His saying: 'And what is sunnah regarding number' i.e., in istinja, because the purpose is only cleanliness. Al-Shafi'i's condition of three is based on considering istinja fard, which we do not affirm. The mention of three in some hadiths is customary because generally cleanliness is achieved with three, or it is interpreted as recommended, evidenced by the fact that if one uses a stone with three edges, it is permissible for them. Also, when two stones and dung were brought to the Prophet ﷺ, he threw away the dung and sufficed with two stones. Thus our imams mentioned. But Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Hajar in Fath al-Bari objected, saying that the initial order to bring three stones renders the request for a third unnecessary after discarding the dung, and that in some authentic narrations he asked for a third and it was brought. From what we have established, it is understood that what is intended is negation of confirmed sunnah; otherwise they have stated recommendation as we mentioned. His saying: 'And washing it with water is more beloved' i.e., washing the area with water is better because it removes the impurity, while the stone only lightens it, so water is more appropriate. Thus mentioned the commentator al-Zayla'i, and it is apparent that the area is not purified by stone. A sub-issue arises: if the passage is hit by water, there is the well-known difference of opinion concerning the issue of earth that, after being contaminated, dries and then water hits it, and similarly its parallels. They have chosen in all of them that impurity does not return, as we have mentioned from them, so let it be the same here. Evidence from the Sunnah is what al-Darqutni narrated and authenticated from Abu Hurayrah that he forbade...
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number of stones in istinja. The author of al-Bahr explains that the Shafi'i school requires three stones as a fard, because they consider istinja fard. Hanafis reject this: the number is not fard; the hadith mentioning three stones is either based on customary practice (since three usually suffice for cleanliness) or recommended. The Hanafi proof includes that the Prophet accepted two stones when nothing else was available, discarding dung. Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani objected citing narrations requesting a third stone. The Hanafi response is that the number is not a fixed obligation; it is only recommended. The passage then compares the preference for water over stones: water removes impurity completely, while stone only reduces it. This leads to a discussion on whether water that touches a previously cleaned area re-impurifies it. The Hanafi view is that impurity does not return, analogous to dry earth that was contaminated and then water touches it – the impurity does not revive. The evidence includes a hadith from al-Darqutni (though the text cuts off).

Key Terms
عدد (adad): Number of stones for istinja; Hanafi says not fixed; Shafi'i requires three.
غسل بالماء (ghusl bil-ma'): Washing with water after or instead of stones; considered better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using three stones for istinja?
A) Fard
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mustahabb (recommended)
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The number of stones in istinja is not fard; water is preferred for complete purification, but stones suffice if cleanliness is achieved.
